	Horrified, Weiwei and I scurried over to where a number of the sisters' maids were groveling on the ground in front of them. Weiwei and I dropped down beside them and bowed until our heads touched the stone.
	"Milady"-one of the maids lifted her head-"please calm down! The princes only didn't talk to the two of you today because they were in a rush-"
	"Silence!" Li Qinghua snapped as she slapped the maid across the face.
	"Hey!" Li Qingmei said suddenly. Weiwei and I glanced at each other from where we were bowing on the stones. Neither of us dared to look up. We heard Li Qingmei call to someone else, "You three! Get over here and bow!"
	There was the sound of hurried footsteps from behind us. I wouldn't put it past the sisters to want to punish everyone in their courtyard here and now. I felt my fingers clench as I sniffled softly. I could still feel the phantom sting of the sticks from when I had was beaten for being clumsy back when I first started at the palace.
	"You know what?" I could hear the amusement in Li Qinghua's voice. "I need a good distraction to take my mind off the princes. You, maid, I want you to dance for me."
	I could feel her eyes on the back of my head, and I slowly looked up, wide-eyed. "Me?"
	"Yes, you," Li Qingmei said impatiently.
	I didn't know how to dance.
	"Wait!" Weiwei lifted her head. "I'll dance in her place."
	"Silence, maid!" Li Qinghua hissed. "I want this one to dance."
	Weiwei's eyes met mine, and I offered her what I hoped was a reassuring smile as I shakily rose to my feet.
	"Quickly now," Li Qingmei snapped at me. "Come to the front."
	"Wait." Li Qinghua looked over the small huddle of servants on the ground. "How about we get a boy to dance with her? Wouldn't that be even more interesting?" She pointed a finger. "You, get over here."
	My eyes widened as I watched the gardener I had bumped into a few days ago rise to his feet. Shen Fanghuan? I mouthed.
	Li Qingmei's blue skirts fluttered as a breeze picked up. "If you entertain us, maybe we'll spare all of you."
	Shen Fanghuan shakily made his way to the front of the group as well. All the color had drained from his face.
	"Dance." Li Qinghua waved her purple fan in our direction. "Entertain us."
	I quickly raised my arms and wobbled around on my feet. I couldn't dance, but I needed to try for everyone still kneeling on the stones.
	I wasn't moving for very long before I had to dodge the fan Li Qinghua chucked at me. "What is that? Are you not afraid of being punished?"
	Just as I began to really panic, Shen Fanghuan stepped forward. Even though it was clear he was uncomfortable in the sisters' presence, he slowly began to dance. I blinked as I watched him. Unlike me, the young gardener knew the steps to what appeared to be an old folk dance.
	When he finally stopped, the Li sisters broke out into applause. "Wonderful!" Li Qingmei clapped, beaming.
	Li Qinghua waved a dismissive hand in our direction. "We won't punish you today. Everyone, get back to work." The maids climbed to their feet, and their expressions were relieved as they scurried off.
	Shen Fanghuan and I bowed to the sisters' retreating backs as they vanished into their room. Once the doors closed behind them, Shen Fanghuan began to walk away as well, but I called after him. "Wait!"
	The gardener turned to look at me with wide eyes.
	"Thank you for saving everyone back there," I said breathlessly.
	Shen Fanghuan nodded as a shy smile flickered across his face.
	"Where did you learn that dance?" I asked curiously as I followed him toward the flowers growing off to the side of the courtyard.
	"The people in my village used to dance like that during festivals and celebrations," Shen Fanghuan recalled. "Even though I was young at the time, it's something I don't want to ever forget."
	"You miss your village," I said softly. I could see it in his eyes.
	He let out a sigh. "I do. But like almost everyone working here at the palace, I came from a poor family, and there was only one path I could walk if I wanted to survive. I'm really sorry for running into you the other day. Everyone who knows me always scolds me for being clumsy. You said your name was Xia Xiyan? Which Xi? Which Yan?"
	"It's the Xi that means sunset, and the Yan that means smoke." When I first arrived at the palace all those years ago, the people at the palace didn't like the name Bunny, so I quickly made one up upon the threat of receiving a beating. "What about your name?"
	"Here-" Shen Fanghuan knelt down to draw with a finger in the dirt. "Fang means direction. Huan is a pillar that stands tall and strong-except I'm one of the clumsiest people you'll ever meet."
	I laughed as I knelt beside him. "Somehow I doubt you can be more clumsy than me."
	"Miss Xia," Shen Fanghuan started as he turned to face me.
	"You don't need to be so formal. Just call me Xiyan."
	"Xiyan . . ."
	I tilted my head to the side as I looked at the gardener expectantly.
	"Do you want to be friends?" Shen Fanghuan blurted out.
	I beamed. "Of course!"
	Footsteps sounded, and I looked up to find Weiwei hurrying over to the two of us. She clutched a stitch in her side. "So this is where you ran off to."
	"Weiwei!" I smiled as I rose to my feet. "We have Gardener Shen to thank! He saved us from being punished by the sisters."
	"Gardener Shen?" Weiwei blinked as her eyes fell on Shen Fanghuan, who was still kneeling on the ground.
	Shen Fanghuan hastily stood up and brushed his foot over the characters he had drawn in the dirt. "I'm Shen Fanghuan."
	Weiwei dipped her head in the gardener's direction. "I'm Hu Qiuwei."
	"This is perfect!" I giggled. "Now all of us are friends."
	Weiwei just sighed. "I'll let the two of you be, but try to stay away from the Li sisters for the rest of the day."
	I turned to Shen Fanghuan once Weiwei had left. "That's right-the Li sisters are still here in their courtyard. Let's talk again once they leave. I don't want to dance again."
	Shen Fanghuan gave me a small smile. "Alright."
	"I'll see you around, then." I smiled back before skipping off down the stone path.

~

	Back in my room, I sat on my designated space on the shared bed. The other maids shuffled around, changing into their nightgowns and undoing their hair. I rested my chin on my palms as I smiled to myself.
	"What are you smiling about?" Weiwei asked as she sat beside me on the long bed.
	"Weiwei, my good sister"-I swiveled around and took Weiwei's hands in my own-"for these long seven years, you've been my only true friend here. And now, I think I just gained another one!"
	"Gardener Shen?"
	"Exactly! We've always been following the same routine every day, and now because of the Li sisters' arrival, things have changed."
	Weiwei tilted her head to the side. "I thought you didn't like serving the Li sisters and wanted to return to our original routine. Besides, we've served for short periods in different guest courtyards of various nobles. What's so good about Gardener Shen that makes you want to be his friend all of a sudden?"
	"He's the one who asked me," I said through my smile.
	Weiwei shook her head in exasperation as she flopped onto her back. I let myself fall back onto the bed as well, and the two of us stared up at the ceiling for some time.
	"Just be careful, will you?" Weiwei finally said. "Today was a close enough call as it was."
	The next morning, all of us maids were back in the Li sisters' courtyard. Once the sisters left to take a walk around the palace with their personal maids, I quickly stood up from where I was cleaning the stone lanterns. I grabbed a broom and made my way over to the gardens.
	I found Shen Fanghuan almost instantly and hurried over to where he was busy pulling weeds from between the flowerbeds. "Fanghuan!" I skidded to a stop next to him.
	The gardener turned to look up at me. He looked surprised at first, but then his expression relaxed into a smile. "Xiyan."
	"Are you the only gardener working in this courtyard?" I asked as I used my broom to purposefully sweep fallen leaves off the stone path.
	Shen Fanghuan reached up a dirt-caked hand to brush loose strands of hair out of his face. "That's correct. The courtyard might be large, but I can maintain the plants by myself."
	"Do you have many other friends?" I decided to ask as I continued to sweep away the leaves.
	"I don't," Shen Fanghuan admitted, and his face turned red again as he ducked his head. The loose strands of his hair fell right back into his face. "Was it that obvious?"
	I blinked at that. "It wasn't obvious! I just thought that since you're such a nice person, you must have a lot of friends."
	"A nice person?" Shen Fanghuan echoed as he looked up in surprise.
	"Am I wrong?"
	Shen Fanghuan let out a weak laugh. "Me? I'm timid and clumsy. You could even call me shy if you wanted. You were the first one to really talk to me as another person and not just a clumsy servant in need of scolding."
	I knelt down so I was at eye level with the gardener. "I think you're kind. You don't have to feel alone anymore. I'm your friend now, remember?"
	"What about you?" Shen Fanghuan asked quietly as he continued to pull weeds out of the soil. "Someone as lively as you must have lots of friends."
	"Before I met you," I answered honestly, "Weiwei was my only friend here at the palace."
	Shen Fanghuan blinked. "Really?"
	"All my personality is good for is getting people into trouble. And you know as much as I do that getting in trouble is the last thing any of us want."
	Shen Fanghuan just smiled sadly and reached to brush the flyaway strands of his hair out of his face.
	"Here"-I hopped closer to the gardener-"I can help."
	Shen Fanghuan looked surprised, but he lowered his dirt-covered hands and silently let me try to tuck the loose strands back into his top knot.
	I frowned as I picked at the dirt stuck in his dark hair. "You're getting dirt everywhere."
	"It's fine, really," the gardener said quietly as he dropped his gaze. His face was red again.
	I just smiled.
	
~

	"I came here to see my friends!" the princess raged. "Brother, why did you have to come here right after I arrived?"
	It was a hot day. I had been going about my duties and had just met up with Shen Fanghuan when the princess arrived at the guest courtyard. Things were going fine until the third prince showed up. All the servants in the courtyard were now groveling on the stones as the princess threw a seething tantrum. Shen Fanghuan was at my side as we pressed our foreheads to the floor.
	"My dear sister," the third prince tried, "I did not know you planned to visit the Li sisters today."
	The princess just let out a sob. "First you took away my favorite maid, and then two months later, she vanished from the palace! No one knows about this matter except for me. I complained to our imperial father, but he just said he'd find me another nice maid to take her place!"
	I could feel eyes on the back of my neck as the third prince glanced over at the servants. "All of you can rise. Get back to work."
	"No!" the princess said shrilly as we started to climb to our feet. "Did I say any of you could stop kneeling? None of you can look at my face. If any of you rise, I'll have you beheaded!"
	We instantly dropped to the ground again, shaken.
	"Dear sister," the third prince said in exasperation, "it's your own crying that ruined your makeup."
	As the two of them continued to argue, I turned my head slightly to notice that Shen Fanghuan was shaking. His expression was terrified as he pressed his forehead to the ground.
	Since the two of us were toward the back of the group, I reached out to tap his arm. Shen Fanghuan turned his head to look over at me in surprise.
	Are you alright? I mouthed.
	Shen Fanghuan shook his head ever so slightly. I'm scared.
	I offered him a smile. Don't be afraid. I'm here with you.
	Ever so slowly, Shen Fanghuan seemed to stop shaking as he smiled back.
	Before long, the princess stormed out of the courtyard, and the third prince motioned for us to rise before leaving with the Li sisters.
	I sat with Shen Fanghuan near the gardens. "This must have been your first time in the direct presence of the imperial family. Weiwei and I had crossed paths with the princess a few times before. It was when that common cold was circulating through the palace, and a number of her own maids contracted it. We had to temporarily take their places. One time, she was throwing a fit and made all the maids kneel. She left the courtyard and must have forgotten we were still there because we had to bow for hours. It was only when she came back after dark that she was surprised we were still there and dismissed us."
	Shen Fanghuan looked horrified. "That sounds awful!"
	"It wasn't that bad," I said as I ran a hand over the grass. "Weiwei was there next to me, and we chatted quietly."
	"Xiyan," Shen Fanghuan started.
	I turned to look up at him expectantly.
	He held my gaze. "Thank you for being there next to me."

~

	Over the next few weeks, I would spend my days at Gardener Shen's side. As he made his rounds around the courtyard, pruning the plants and pulling weeds, I would follow him around with my bucket and mop, cleaning the path next to him.
	"Look." Shen Fanghuan pointed up at the leaves of the tree we were standing under. "Autumn is coming. See? Some of the leaves have already changed colors."
	"It's so pretty!" I clasped my hands behind my back, beaming as I admired the colors of the orange leaves high above us. But when I turned back to look at Shen Fanghuan, the gardener had vanished. "Fanghuan?" I looked around the empty courtyard.
	After a moment, I spotted the gardener jogging back over to me with a flower in his hands. Shen Fanghuan stopped in front of me and gently tucked the flower behind my ear. "For you."
	"For me?"
	"I think it suits you," Shen Fanghuan said as he averted his gaze.
	I twinkled. "Thank you!" I crouched down and picked up a windswept flower from the path. This I placed in Shen Fanghuan's hair. "Here's one for you."
	The gardener gave me a shy smile as he touched the flower. I smiled as I picked up my broom, and my smile remained as I swept the rest of the leaves off the path.
	During the walk back to the maids' quarters, I pulled out the flower Shen Fanghuan had gifted me from where I had carefully tucked it into my waistband. I smiled happily down at the flower as I twirled its stem between my fingers.
	By the time I reached the room I shared with the other maids, the sun had long set, and the moon gleamed as it painted the palace walls in its silvery light. I skipped inside and took a seat on the bed, setting the flower down beside me.
	Weiwei took a seat next to me. "Let me guess. Gardener Shen gave you that flower."
	"Is it that obvious?"
	"Why else would you be smiling so widely?"
	I giggled.
	"Honestly now, what do you see in Gardener Shen?"
	I tilted my head to the side as I began to undo my braids. "What do you mean?"
	"You like him, don't you?"
	"I think he's a kind person," I said confidently as I fumbled with the knots in my hair.
	"So then . . ."
	I paused for a moment with my fingers caught in my hair. "How do I know if I'm falling in love with him? Is this what it's like to fall in love with someone?"
	Weiwei just gave me a look. "I think that's something you'll have to figure out for yourself."
	I flopped down onto the bed and rolled onto my stomach. I stared determinedly at the wall in front of me. How difficult can it be?
	In the morning, I was up early. After getting dressed and doing my hair, I sat on the bed for a while before the other maids began to wake. Weiwei sat up, tiredly rubbing the sleep from her eyes.
	"Weiwei!" I said quickly as she turned to look at me. I scooted closer to her and made my hands into fists as I massaged her shoulders.
	Weiwei raised her brows in a half-suspicious, half-exasperated look. "What's going on, Xiyan?"
	"Weiwei, my good sister. Could you do me a favor? Please?"
	Weiwei caught my hands and placed them back in my lap. She sighed. "What kind of favor?"
	"How do I know if I'm in love with Gardener Shen?"
	"What-? This again?"
	"Please, Weiwei." I looked up at Weiwei with large eyes. "I've never been in love before. I want to know what love is like. In all the stories I've read-"
	"You're always talking about these stories you've read in the past," Weiwei said softly as I placed my hands on her shoulders and turned her around so I could braid her hair. "Do you think Gardener Shen is the courageous hero in your story?"
	"Well, I'm the beautiful heroine, aren't I?" I joked.
	"Yes, yes, yes." Weiwei sighed as I finished tying up her hair. "All someone needs to do is take one look at your face to know you're the beautiful heroine. Come on, let's go get breakfast."
	After breakfast, the other maids and I made our way to the Li sisters' courtyard. I heard the sounds of hurried footsteps behind me and turned to find Sun Xiaoting walking toward me.
	"Sister Sun?" I blinked at her as she fell into pace beside me.
	"Qiuwei said you wanted to know what it's like to be in love," Sun Xiaoting said. "So she asked me to come to talk to you."
	"So then you know what it's like to be in love?" I asked eagerly.
	Sun Xiaoting waited for the other maids to pass us up before lowering her voice. "Not many people know this, but I have a lover in the palace."
	"You do?" I whispered. "But you were always the most responsible of us maids!"
	Sun Xiaoting gave me a look. "He's also a servant, but that doesn't matter. I came to the palace in the hopes that maybe I could become a maid favored by one of the princes, but after I met my lover, I don't want a prince. I only want to be with him."
	"Do the two of you meet often?"
	Sun Xiaoting smiled faintly. "We do. We meet in secret."
	"How do you know when you're in love?"
	"Love is like a strong bond," Sun Xiaoting explained. "Love is when you're willing to give your entire heart and soul to another person."
	When we arrived at the Li sisters' courtyard, I picked up my broom before hurrying over to the gardens.
	"Halt!" A voice called, and I froze midstep.
	I turned to find Li Qinghua standing on the wooden porch of the sisters' shared room. She was dressed in her usual flowing purple, and her arms were folded across her chest.
      "You!" Li Qinghua recognized me. "You're that maid who didn't know how to dance! Where are you off to in such a hurry? Come help me."
	"Yes, milady." I reluctantly followed Li Qinghua into her room to find the sisters' two personal maids helping Li Qingmei into her blue dress.
	"Help me change," Li Qinghua ordered as she held out her arms. "My older sister and I are going to see the princes today. We need to look even more beautiful to get their attention."
	"Yes, milady." I swiftly pulled off her flowy scarves. After setting them aside, I helped her out of the rest of her outfit until she was standing in her undergarments.
	"Sister," Li Qinghua called as she looked over at where Li Qingmei was now getting her hair and makeup done. "Which dress should I wear today? I had all twenty of the best ones brought here to the palace."
	"How about the purple one?" Li Qingmei called back.
	Li Qinghua frowned. "All the princes know that I like to wear purple. Wouldn't I be more eye-catching if I wore a different color? What about red?"
	"Red's too bold for going to see the princes, no?" Li Qingmei rose from her seat. Her maids followed her, trying to finish pinning up her half-done hair.
	"Pink, then," Li Qinghua decided. "You, maid, go fetch me my pink dress!"
	I nodded and curtsied before hurrying off. By the time I returned with the dress, two other maids had appeared in the room and were helping Li Qinghua with her hair and makeup.
      "Quickly now!" Li Qinghua snapped as she noticed me reemerge with the dress. "Just leave it over there. You can go. I don't need you anymore."
	"Yes, milady." After leaving the room, I quickly snatched up my broom from where I had left it outside. I made my way back down the stone path toward the garden, but in my haste, my foot caught on the hem of my skirts, and the entire world tilted around me.
    


    Chapter Five

	I hit the ground with a thud. My hands skidded over the stone path as I tried to prevent myself from rolling into the dirt. I lay there for a long moment, dazed. My head spun. Why can't I just pay attention to where I am going?
	"Xiyan?" A worried voice sounded, and I groggily sat up to see Shen Fanghuan hurrying toward me.
	"Fanghuan . . ." I started, then trailed off when I realized I was covered in dirt.
	Shen Fanghuan dropped to his knees beside me. "Xiyan, what happened?"
	"I fell." I sniffed as I started to brush the dirt from my face, but then hissed from the stinging in my hands. I held them in front of me to find them scratched and bleeding.
	Shen Fanghuan quickly helped me to my feet. "Let's go clean that before it can get infected."
	I nodded, allowing the gardener to lead me toward the small storage room on the far side of the courtyard. When we arrived, I took a seat on the porch outside as Shen Fanghuan went inside to fetch a bowl of clean water. The gardener took a seat next to me when he returned, then gently took my hands and lowered them into the bowl.
	My raw hands stung from the water, but I bit my lip and endured the discomfort as Shen Fanghuan brushed off the dirt. Even though his own hands were covered in rough calluses, his touch was gentle.
	"I don't think we have any bandages," Shen Fanghuan said regretfully as he finally lifted my hands from the bowl.
	"It's fine." I offered him a smile. Then I remembered that my face was still covered in dirt, and I quickly dropped my head.
	"What's wrong?" He asked in concern.
	"My face is a mess-I'm not pretty anymore."
	Shen Fanghuan shook his head, and I blinked as I timidly looked back up at him. "Have you ever heard the phrase that the most important things lie within? Being pretty is only a person's outer appearance. True beauty comes from within."
	I curiously tilted my head to the side. "What do you mean?"
	"Take the Li sisters for example," he explained. "They may look beautiful, but their personalities practically repel people from them."
	"If I looked like this when we first met"-I gestured to my dirt-covered face-"would you still have wanted to be my friend?"
	"Of course," he replied. I looked on in surprise as Shen Fanghuan dipped his sleeve into the bowl of water before turning back to me. I sat still as he skillfully wiped the dirt from my face. "Sometimes, what matters the most isn't visible on the outside. But when you look closer . . ." Shen Fanghuan finished wiping the dirt from my face and sat back with a genuine smile on his face. "You'll find that's where true beauty lies."
	I found a smile tugging on my lips. I scooted closer to the gardener, looking up at his face. "I like you."
	He blinked. "What?"
	"I like you," I repeated determinedly. "I just wanted to say it. I've never experienced love before-I've never fallen in love before. Maybe you just want to stay friends, and that's fine. I just wanted to let you know."
	Shen Fanghuan's face turned red, and he dropped his gaze. "I like you, too. I've never fallen in love before either. Maybe it was fate that we ran into each other."
	Around noon, the Li sisters and their maids finally left their courtyard. Once they were gone, Shen Fanghuan and I walked over to the small pound that glittered off to the side of the courtyard. The two of us stood on the wooden bridge that arched over it, looking down at the clear water. I leaned forward to look down at our reflections. I caught Shen Fanghuan's gaze in the water, and the gardener gave me a shy smile. I twinkled back.
	That night, I sat on my bed, rocking back and forth as I hummed to myself.
	"Xiyan, what happened this time?" Weiwei asked as she sat down next to me.
	"I told Fanghuan that I liked him!" I answered between smiles.
	"And then what happened?"
	"The two of us are going to give it a try."
	"Are you sure about that?"
	I turned to face Weiwei. "Weiwei, for the past seven years here at the palace, every day has felt like a blur. But now that I've I met Fanghuan, it's almost as if I can see the world in a new light."
	"Does he make you happy?"
	"He does."
	"In that case," Weiwei said seriously, "the two of you have to be careful. Servants aren't allowed to be in relationships. If you get caught . . . Xiyan, is it worth it?"
	I didn't have to think about my answer. "It's worth it."
      Since arriving in the human realm, I found it was almost nothing like the stories I had read. This world was a dark place, and I experienced it firsthand when I was kidnapped all those years ago. Since being separated from Yuxin, there had been an empty space in my chest-a painful hole that wouldn't go away. Although life in the demon realm had been dreary, it hadn't hurt in the same way. Despite everything that happened, I still wanted to believe it could be beautiful-that the people living in it could be kind.
	"Did Sister Sun give you any useful advice?" Weiwei asked, drawing me back from my thoughts.
	"She did," I said confidently as I got to work undoing my hair. Then I paused. "Speaking of Sister Sun, where is she?"
	Weiwei looked perplexed as she glanced around the room. "You're right-she's really not here."
	I broke into a smile as I motioned for Weiwei to lean close. I lowered my voice. "She told me that she has a lover in the palace! She must be meeting up with him!"
	Weiwei frowned slightly. "I knew she had a lover, but Sister Sun is the most responsible out of all of us. She's never come back late before."
	I brushed off Weiwei's concerns. "It's fine. If she isn't back in the morning, that's when we can start worrying."
	Weiwei wrung her hands together as the other maids began to get ready for bed. "Alright."
	When I woke in the morning, I quickly did my hair and changed into my maid uniform. This time when I looked around, I quickly spotted Sun Xiaoting instructing everyone to hurry if we didn't want to be late for breakfast.
	I spent the day following Shen Fanghuan around, listening attentively to the stories he told about his old village and the traditions they would follow there.
	I crouched down to help the gardener pull the weeds that had begun to sneak up between the flowers. "The way you talk about your mother . . . I can tell you were everything to her. I find it hard to believe that she sent you into the palace."
	Shen Fanghuan offered me a sad smile. "It's because she loved me that she decided to let me go. I was my mother's only child. She didn't want to part with me, but she and my father also knew my body was too weak to survive the harsh northern winters. Every winter I would be on death's doorstep, so she finally had an old friend of hers bring me to the palace. He was a martial artist. When I was little, he would always bring me trinkets from his travels and even promised that he would take me to see the tallest mountains, but that never happened. At first, I resented my parents for abandoning me. It was only when I got older that I understood. They sent me here because they wanted me to survive. I've been here for over ten years now."
	I sighed. "I didn't have a choice in coming here either. I was kidnapped and sold. My sister and I were captured together, but we were separated. I don't know what happened to her."
      "I'm sorry," Shen Fanghuan said quietly.
	I smiled brightly as I shook my head. "I think I'm slowly coming to accept that this is my life now." Then my smile faltered. "I just . . . I hope my sister is doing okay."
	After a long pause, Shen Fanghuan changed the topic. "How are your hands healing? You don't have to pull weeds with me, you know."
	"Don't worry, my hands are fine. And I know, but if we can finish in the gardens early, we'll have more time to relax later. Well, unless the Li sisters decide to call on us."
      Shen Fanghuan nodded, then said suddenly, "I just had a thought."
      I tilted my head. "What's the thought?"
      "Since we were just talking about my hometown-when the Li sisters are away from their courtyard during dinner, what if I teach you that one folk dance?" 
      I beamed. "I'd love that!"
      Night had fallen by the time both Li sisters left with their personal maids. While they were at dinner, Shen Fanghuan and I met up at the back of the courtyard.
      "It's dark," I remarked as I squinted through the dim light. The moon glowed in the inky sky above, and the world below was illuminated in the orange light of the lanterns around the stone path.
      "It is dark," Shen Fanghuan agreed, glancing around almost worriedly.
      "It's fine." I offered him a smile. "I can still see you well enough."
      Shen Fanghuan smiled back. "Okay. The dance itself isn't very long, and it only consists of three main parts. First, you step forward with your right foot-just like this."
      I copied Shen Fanghuan's movements, and slowly but surely, I began to get the moves of the dance. The autumn leaves that covered the ground swirled in my wake, and my skirts fluttered around my feet. "What do you think?" I asked as I twirled.
      Shen Fanghuan grinned at me. "You're a natural!" Then his tone suddenly changed. "Watch out!" I blinked as he hurried forward, catching my hand and pulling me back just before I could collide with one of the stone lanterns.
      Suddenly, Shen Fanghuan's hand fell from mine as he slipped on the leaves scattered over the path. I quickly grabbed his hand in an attempt to prevent him from falling backward. But I didn't have nearly enough strength, and the two of us both toppled over.
      Shen Fanghuan let out a quiet hiss as he hit the ground. I lay there on his chest in a daze.
      "Are you alright? I'm so sorry!" Snapping out of my daze, I quickly tried to sit up. But Shen Fanghuan had wrapped his arms around me during our fall to protect me from the impact, and I found myself unable to move. "Are you alright?" I asked again.
      Shen Fanghuan gave me a pained smile. "I'm fine."
      "I'm sorry-I got too carried away."
      "This is my fault. I'm the one who slipped."
      The cool night air was crisp against my face as I lay there on his chest. The fallen leaves whispered across the stones around us. "I can hear your heartbeat. Your heart is beating quickly."
      "So is yours," he breathed.
      I blinked. I hadn't realized it until he pointed it out. "What happens now?" I asked softly, suddenly all too aware that my lips were mere inches from his as the two of us looked at each other.
      "What do you want to do?"
      "I-" I started. I didn't know how to put all the thoughts and emotions racing through my mind into words.
      Shen Fanghuan's face was red as he turned his head away. "Xiyan, I think I want to kiss you."
      "I think I do too," I whispered. "May I?"
      Shen Fanghuan turned back to me, eyes wide. He dipped his head in a nod.
      I leaned forward and our lips met.
      I felt Shen Fanghuan's arms leave my back as he reached up to tuck the loose strands of hair behind my ear. When we finally drew away, I could hear his heart beating even quicker than it had been before, and for a long moment, the two of us just stared at each other. He was smiling, and I was smiling too. I rolled off of his chest, brushing the leaves from his dark hair as we sat up.
      Shen Fanghuan gently pressed his lips to my forehead. I giggled.
      "Xia Xiyan?" A voice in the distance called out. "Where are you?"
      "It's Sun Xiaoting-Sister Sun," I whispered, realizing with a jolt that I was supposed to be back in the room with the rest of the maids. I had completely lost track of time.
      Shen Fanghuan helped me to my feet. "You should go."
      I reluctantly nodded. "I'll see you tomorrow."
      "See you tomorrow."
      I offered Shen Fanghuan a smile as I waved. He waved back, and then I hurried in the direction of Sun Xiaoting's voice. "I'm here!"
      "Next time try to be on time, will you?" Sun Xiaoting let out a sigh as she motioned for me to follow her out of the courtyard.
      I nodded, but I found a smile playing on my lips all the same.
      Once Sun Xiaoting made sure I changed out of my uniform and into my nightgown, I jumped onto the bed. "Weiwei! I'm so happy!"
      Weiwei rolled over to look at me. "What happened?"
      I leaned in close and whispered in her ear, "I kissed him! And then he kissed me!"
      I looked up to see Sun Xiaoting walking over to us, exasperated. "The two of you need to go to sleep." 
      "Yes ma'am," I said quickly, pulling the blankets over Weiwei and me.
      But even long after all the other maids had fallen asleep, I couldn't help but smile throughout the night.
      
~

	"I can't believe it's almost time for the Li sisters to go back to their manor," I remarked as Shen Fanghuan and I sat in front of the gardening shed. It was noon, and the sun was high in the clear sky. The Li sisters had left for lunch, and the courtyard was silent. "Even though I can't say that I care much for either of the sisters, it was their presence that brought the two of us together."
	Shen Fanghuan nodded in agreement. "As much as I don't want to admit it, it seems like we have them to thank."
	I rested my head on his shoulder. "What do we do once we're sent back? Will we really not be able to see each other anymore?"
	Shen Fanghuan wrapped his arms around me. "We'll figure out something. I promise."
	"I could try and find you," I whispered. "Where do the gardeners live?"
	"It's very far from here," he said sadly. "Even with a map, the palace is such a maze that getting lost is nearly inevitable. Where do the maids live? What if I were to come to you?"
	"It isn't far from here. Here-" I leaned forward and drew with a finger in the dirt. "It's this one path, and then two right turns. But could you really sneak in? Men aren't even allowed near that block."
	"It's worth a try," Shen Fanghuan said determinedly. "Even if we can only see each other from a distance, it's worth it."
	That night, when I returned to my lodging, all the maids in the room were murmuring among themselves. I looked to Weiwei as I took my seat next to her. "What happened?"
	"The second prince just got His Majesty to grant him a marriage with the eldest Li sister," Weiwei explained. "And then the third prince went ahead and requested a marriage with Second Lady Li. The emperor granted it too."
	"It seems like Eldest Lady Li got her wish of marrying a prince fulfilled, then," I said absently.
	"With it being the emperor's wish, both Li sisters couldn't refuse the marriage," Weiwei continued quietly. "One accepted with tears of joy, and one accepted in tears of sorrow. They're heading back to their manor tomorrow morning to prepare for the wedding. If I remember correctly, their father should be back later this week to take them back."
	"I'm glad the Li sisters are finally leaving . . ."
	"But you're also sad that you won't be able to see Gardener Shen anymore."
	I shook my head as I smiled. "Fanghuan and I are going to try and meet up."
	"Meet up?" Weiwei echoed. "You mean in secret? But that's dangerous! If the two of you get caught sneaking around-"
	I held Weiwei's gaze. "I'm willing to take the risk. I want to see him again."
	Weiwei looked conflicted before she finally let out a sigh. "Just tell me what you need, and I'll try my best to cover for you."
	"Really?" My eyes lit up. "Weiwei, my good sister, I knew I could count on you!"
	"Where's Sister Sun?" Weiwei asked as she glanced around the room. "Normally she'd be telling us to go to bed by now."
	"She'll be back soon," I reassured her. "Let's get ready for bed so she doesn't scold us when she returns."
	In the morning, Weiwei, me, and the other maids helped pack up the Li sisters' extensive wardrobe of clothing and jewelry. We spent the majority of the day transporting the boxes to the palace gates, where carriages were already waiting.
	When the last box was finally moved, I stood in a line with the other maids, waiting to see the sisters off. It didn't take long before footsteps sounded, but the two figures that appeared were not the Li sisters.
	Even with my head bowed, I watched out of the corner of my eye as the second and third princes walked over to the middle-aged man waiting in front of the carriages. I was too far away to hear their conversation, but I could see them greet each other respectfully.
	"Father!" a voice called, and I watched Li Qinghua appear, followed closely by Li Qingmei.
	The middle-aged man bowed respectfully to the princes before climbing into one of the carriages. The Li sisters curtsied politely as well, then climbed into the carriage after their father.
	Once the entourage of carriages vanished from sight, the princes turned and walked in opposite directions. Even though their paces seemed normal enough, their postures were stiff, as if they were trying to get as far away from each other as possible.
	I spent the rest of the morning cleaning up the guest courtyard with the other maids. After that, Shen Fanghuan and I spent our last day together pruning the flowering bushes. When night fell, the gardener gently pulled me into a warm hug.
      "You're getting bolder," I whispered as I wrapped my arms around his back.
      "I've come to realize that the time we'll be able to spend together is short," Shen Fanghuan said softly. "But I want to spend more time with you. I'll come see you tonight."
	"Please be careful." I stood on my tip-toes to press a light kiss against his cheek.

~

	Back in our room, even after the other maids had fallen asleep, I was still wide awake. My ears perked up at every small noise, and I had to remind myself that it would take Shen Fanghuan some time to arrive. Just then, there was the sound of a twig snapping outside the window. I slowly sat up, careful not to wake Weiwei and the maid sleeping on the other side of me.
	I tiptoed over to the window and pushed it open to look over the ledge. Shen Fanghuan smiled at me, and I reached out to lace my fingers through his.
	"You made it," I whispered breathlessly.
	"You don't know how scared I was the entire time," Shen Fanghuan whispered back as he helped me climb over the ledge. His skin seemed to take on a silvery sheen in the moonlight. "My heart was beating so quickly the entire way that I thought I'd pass out from fright before I even got here."
	We chatted quietly until I finally urged him to head back before he could get caught.
	After that, Shen Fanghuan would show up in the middle of the night once a week. Even though the time we had together was brief, I treasured every minute of it.
	A few weeks later, we were sitting next to each other under the window of the maids' room. Hand in hand, the two of us looked up at the vast sky. The full moon glowed in the center of the sky, and the world was bathed in silver.
	"Today's the Mid-Autumn Festival," Shen Fanghuan said softly. "I'm really glad that I'm able to spend it with you."
      The night air was cool and crisp as I rested my head on his shoulder. "I'm just happy that we can spend time together. I'm happy whenever I get to hear your voice. I like hearing you talk, you know that? Your accent is different from any other I've heard in the palace."
      Shen Fanghuan let out a soft laugh. "It must be from my village in the north. The people from my village also have a special Mid-Autumn custom."
      "What is it?"
      Shen Fanghuan took one of my hands and gently pressed a red leaf into it. "We write wishes to the loved ones who are not with us on dry autumn leaves. Every year, I write one for my parents. This Mid-Autumn Festival, you can write one to your sister."
      I glowed as Shen Fanghuan handed me a thin stick of charcoal. Yuxin, I wrote, careful not to break the delicate leaf, I hope you get everything you wish for.
      When the two of us had finished writing our wishes, I turned back to Shen Fanghuan. "Now what do we do?"
      "We crumple the leaves," he explained, "and then we let the wind scatter the pieces to the four corners of the world, hoping that at least one will reach the ones we think of."
      Together, we crumpled the leaves under our hands, tossed the pieces into the air, and watched the wind sweep them away. Once they vanished into the night, I rested my head on Shen Fanghuan's shoulder again. "Happy Mid-Autumn Festival, Fanghuan."
	"Happy Mid-Autumn Festival, Xiyan."
    Chapter Six

	The palace was bustling with preparations for the double wedding between the princes and the Li sisters. Even though months had gone by, it seemed as if no time had passed since the sisters left. Now, I was working with the other maids to prepare the courtyard that the second prince would be sharing with Eldest Lady Li.
	I worked absently, scrubbing the paths and railings. Even though I was physically present, my mind was elsewhere. I had met with Shen Fanghuan the previous night, and now I had to wait an entire week to see him again.
	When night fell, Weiwei helped me unbraid my hair. As I sat there in our room, I snuck a glance over at Sun Xiaoting. She was sitting in the corner, staring unseeingly at the wooden floor. As of recently, her entire demeanor had changed.
	"Sister Sun . . .?" I whispered to Weiwei.
	"I tried to ask her if she was alright a few days ago," Weiwei said quietly. "But she just told me that everything was fine and quickly changed the topic."
	"Do you think she fell out with her lover?"
	"I really don't know."
	Even after the other maids had gone to sleep, Sun Xiaoting still sat there in the corner of the room. I was debating whether to try to comfort her when I heard a quiet tapping on the window.
	I slowly sat up and gently prodded Weiwei with a finger. I motioned with my head toward the window, and Weiwei nodded. Weiwei rose from the bed first and silently walked over to Sun Xiaoting. Once the two of them began to whisper in lowered voices, I slid out of bed and tiptoed through the dark.
	When I arrived at the window, I carefully pushed it open to find Shen Fanghuan standing there. I quickly climbed outside and closed the window behind me.
	I turned to Shen Fanghuan with wide eyes. What are you doing here? I mouthed as I let myself fall into his awaiting arms.
	"I wanted to see you," he whispered, the wind picking up to send loose stands of his hair fluttering.
	I drew back to place my hands on the sides of his face. "Fanghuan, you shouldn't be here. Making the trip here once a week is already dangerous enough as it is."
	"I know," Shen Fanghuan breathed. "Here-" I blinked as he took one of my hands and gently pressed a flower into it. "This is for you."
	I smiled as my fingers closed around the flower. "And this is for you." I stood on my tip-toes and brushed my lips against his.
	The two of us spent the next hour sitting together under the window. Shen Fanghuan's head rested on my shoulder as we looked up at the cloudy night sky. "Do you think I'll see you at the Li sisters' wedding tomorrow?"
	Shen Fanghuan's voice was tired. "There's a chance."
	"Are you still awake?" I asked after a long pause.
	"I'm so tired, Xiyan. Would it be bad if I fell asleep right here?"
	"You'll be punished if they find you here in the morning," I whispered.
	"Xiyan," he said softly, "am I crazy? Just a few months ago, if someone told me I'd be sneaking around the palace at night, I'd never believe them. But here I am now."
	I sighed as I wrapped my arms around him. "I never thought I'd be sneaking out of my room either. Have your roommates noticed anything?"
	"You don't have to worry-all of them are heavy sleepers. What about on your end?"
	"Normally, all the maids are asleep, and if someone does wake up, I can say that I'm heading to the toilet. Tonight, though, one of the maids was awake. I think Weiwei should have gotten her to go to bed by now."
      There was a pause before Shen Fanghuan spoke again. "If we weren't servants here at the palace, what kind of life do you think the two of us would live?"
      "That's an easy question. We'd be able to live for ourselves."
      "And what kind of life would that be?"
      I smiled as I watched the stars flicker in the night sky. "In that life, you'd still be able to live with your mother. And maybe then I'd get to meet her and become a daughter-in-law that she could be proud of. In that life, I'd still have my sister, and she'd be happy for the two of us. Weiwei would be there too, of course."
      Shen Fanghuan frowned faintly. "Speaking of Hu Qiuwei, I get the feeling that she doesn't like me very much."
      "Don't take it personally," I reassured him. "Weiwei just wants to keep me out of trouble-and she thinks that you're trouble. But that was at the beginning. She's willing to help us now."
      "Xiyan," Shen Fanghuan started, "do you think we'll be stuck here in the palace as servants forever?"
      I fell silent at that. After a while I said, "In the past, I used to think that this world was a wondrous place. It didn't take me long to realize just how wrong I was about it. But then I met you, and I'm starting to believe that maybe there are wonderful things after all." I slowly rose to my feet and helped Shen Fanghuan to his. "You should go," I whispered. "You're tired. If you stay here any longer, I'm afraid you won't be able to keep your eyes open."
      Shen Fanghuan gave me a faint smile. "I'll go."
      "Please be careful." I reluctantly let my hand slip from his grasp. I stood there, watching until Shen Fanghuan vanish into the dark. My heart was already longing to see him again.

~

	Red silk and ribbons stretched as far as the eye could see. Today was the day of the wedding, and the maids were chattering excitedly among themselves. Apparently, one of them had been sent to help sew a bead that had come loose from Eldest Lady Li's wedding dress back on and now was telling everyone how exquisite the bride-to-be looked.
	"There was real gold embroidered in her dress," the maid said dreamily. "And the red and green silk-it shimmers in the light!"
	"I wish I could see such a dress," one of the other maids piped up. "Maybe once I see it, I'll be able to picture myself wearing it in my dreams."
	"Eldest Lady Li is overjoyed," the first maid informed the small crowd of maids gathering around her. "But I've heard that her youngest sister is not happy."
	"Why wouldn't she be happy? She's marrying a prince."
	"Word is that it isn't the third prince she wanted to marry."
	"That's right," yet another maid added. "The third prince doesn't even like Second Lady Li. He only proposed to her because the second prince proposed to Eldest Lady Li. The second prince is furious now. He wanted General Li's military power and influence for himself, but now he has to share with his brother."
	I turned to Weiwei and lowered my voice. "So that's why the second prince proposed to Eldest Lady Li!"
	"Did you really think there was any love between them?" Weiwei asked tiredly.
	I frowned faintly. "I suppose not."
      Suddenly, Weiwei nudged me with her elbow, and I turned in the direction she was looking. I followed her gaze to the line of servants carrying colorful assortments of flowers. I immediately spotted Shen Fanghuan among them, and a smile cut across my face.
      Shen Fanghuan caught my eye and smiled back.
      Weiwei let out a sigh. "Everything you're thinking is written on your face. If you don't want to be reported-"
      "I know, I know. Let's get back to work."
      That night during the wedding banquet, I stood outside the banquet hall with the other maids. Sun Xiaoting stood next to the doors, helping direct the guests to their seats. Sun Xiaoting's expression was polite as she curtsied to each guest. Out of the corner of my eye, I scanned the guests making their way toward the hall. I spotted the Crown Prince almost immediately, and my gaze lingered on him as he made his way up the steps. His wife, the princess consort, followed a few paces behind. I was admiring the intricate embroidery of her outer garment and long skirts when something strange caught my attention.
      When the Crown Prince and his wife passed Sun Xiaoting, the maid seemed to freeze up. Even after the Crown Prince swept past her, Sun Xiaoting continued to stand there, petrified.
      After what felt like an eternity, all the guests finally entered the banquet hall. "Weiwei," I whispered. I turned my head ever so slightly so I could see her face. "Did you see the way Sister Sun's expression changed when the Crown Prince walked by?"
      "I did," Weiwei whispered back. "But I don't get it. Sister Sun has worked in the Crown Prince's courtyard for years now. She's always seemed to like it there too. She was only away for a couple of months when we were all sent to help out with the Li sisters."
      "Wait . . ." I said slowly. "Now that I'm thinking about it, I rarely saw Sister Sun in the Li sisters' courtyard. She must have constantly been moving between the Crown Prince's eastern wing and the Li sisters' courtyard."
      "Do you think she got punished for not being able to complete her normal workload there?" Weiwei asked quietly.
      I just shook my head in bewilderment. The banquet continued for hours, and I felt the tiredness begin to creep up on me the longer I stood there under the stars. The night air was cold, and I shivered. It seemed like tonight we wouldn't be getting any dinner ourselves.
      It was only when the sky began to lighten that we were sent back to our rooms. Sun Xiaoting led the way, and I quickened my pace to catch up with her.
      "Sister Sun," I called. My breath puffed out in front of me. "Are you alright?"
      "Why do you ask?" Sun Xiaoting said stiffly.
      "Are the maids in the eastern wing giving you a difficult time? Did the Crown Prince give you a difficult time?"
      "The Crown Prince?" Sun Xiaoting looked at me as if she couldn't quite register the words coming out of my mouth. "The Crown Prince, he . . ." Sun Xiaoting's face paled as she rapidly shook her head. "Come on, if you want to get any sleep tonight, we better move faster."
      I turned to exchange a glance with Weiwei. Maybe it was better not to ask. Either way, whatever was bothering Sun Xiaoting was not something she was willing to share with us.
      I was so tired when we arrived back at our room that I didn't even bother changing out of my uniform. I struggled to keep my eyes open long enough for Weiwei to help me undo my hair. When she finished, I flopped over and was fast asleep within seconds.
      It only felt like a moment had passed before I was startled awake by the sound of someone screaming. I sat bolt upright as my head snapped toward the source of the noise. A maid I recognized from the room across from ours was standing in the doorway, completely out of breath.
      "The third prince is dead!" she cried.
      I turned to Weiwei in stunned silence. Her look of shock must have been an exact mirror of mine.
      "What happened?" one of the other maids asked quickly.
      "The third prince was found dead in his bed," the maid in the doorway said in a breathless rush. "Apparently his new wife woke up screaming beside him. The royal physician came running, but the prince was long dead." With that said, she turned and scurried off to share the news with the maids in the next room over.
      There was silence before all the maids in our room began whispering. "Do you think Second Lady Li killed him?" the maid next to Weiwei asked in disbelief. "The third prince was just as healthy as his brothers, and Second Lady Li was the one who was with him last night . . ."
      "While it might be true that Second Lady Li didn't want to marry the third prince," I said as I leaned across Weiwei to address our fellow maid, "I can't believe that she would killed him. The third prince is still a prince after all. Even someone as arrogant as Second Lady Li wouldn't dare to kill one of the emperor's sons right in his own palace."
      "How do you think the prince died?" the maid on my other side asked. "Do you think the murderer used a knife? Or do you think they poisoned him?"
      "If it really wasn't Second Lady Li," Weiwei said thoughtfully, "anyone could have poisoned his food during the banquet. Anyone could have poisoned the wedding wine brought to the bride and groom's room after the banquet."
      "Hey," I said softly as I turned to Weiwei. "Remember how Sister Sun acted last night when the Crown Prince passed by her? Do you think she knew something about the plot?"
      Suddenly, there was the sound of hurried footsteps as yet another maid appeared in the doorway. "It was the maids in your room that served Second Lady Li during her stay in the guest courtyard. Right now, Second Lady Li is the largest suspect in the third prince's death, and she's calling all of you to help testify for her."
      All the maids scrambled to their feet. When we arrived at the courtyard, the sound of anguished crying greeted us. Li Qinghua was sobbing at the feet of the officials, who were staring down at her grimly. "I didn't kill him! I swear I didn't kill him! Even though I was reluctant to marry His Highness, I would never do anything to harm him!"
      Just as the other maids and I lined up near the officials, the doors to the bedroom opened, and a middle-aged man walked out. Judging from his outfit, I could immediately tell that he was the coroner.
      "What happened?" One of the officials asked quickly as the coroner stopped in front of him.
      "Poison," the coroner said as he shook his head. "The third prince died from poison."
      The official turned back to Li Qinghua, glaring. "Did you poison your husband?"
      "It wasn't me!" Li Qinghua shrieked as she groveled at his feet. "I'm innocent!" Her unbound hair spilled over the stones, and the long fabric of her flowing outer garments rippled around her as she trembled.
      The official stomped his foot impatiently. "You vicious woman! Still won't admit to your crimes?"
      Li Qinghua's head snapped up as her gaze fell on me. Her eyes widened in recognition. "You, maid! Tell these officials that I would never murder my husband!"
      I took a step forward and dropped to my knees. "Milady wouldn't kill her husband. After all, this marriage allowed her to become part of the royal family. She wouldn't jeopardize that new position." As much as I didn't like Li Qinghua, I didn't want her to be wrongly accused of a crime.
      "Exactly!" Li Qinghua nodded vigorously.
      The officials just frowned down at Li Qinghua, still unconvinced. One of the officials waved his hand dismissively. "Lock her up."
      "Wait!" a voice called, and everyone looked over to watch the princess sprint into the courtyard. "I don't think Qinghua killed my brother!"
      "Your Highness," an official said in exasperation, "Second Lady Li is the biggest suspect right now."
      "I think you're being too hurried," another voice called. I looked on as a pair of figures glided into the courtyard to join the small gathering.
      "Your Highness," the officials chorused as the second prince came to a stop next to the princess. Li Qingmei stood at his side, and her eyes immediately fell on her younger sister.
      "This is a murder case," the second prince said smoothly. "I think you should leave the investigating to me. The deceased is my brother. I feel his loss, just as any brother feels the loss of a dear sibling."
      "Leave the investigating to you?" Everyone turned to watch the Crown Prince stride into the courtyard with a flustered look on his face. "Of course you want to be the one investigating the case! You're the one who killed him!"
      "Me?" The second prince just blinked. "I know you never thought highly of me, but accusing me of murdering our brother . . .?"
      "I know it was you!"-the Crown Prince pointed at his brother-"It was you!"
      The officials standing around looked at each other uneasily before turning to address the Crown Prince. They had clearly never seen him this flustered before. "Your Highness, please calm down. You can't just accuse the second prince like that without any evidence."
      "Evidence-?" The Crown Prince opened his mouth to speak, but instead let out a laugh. He continued to point his finger at his brother before turning on the spot and marching out of the courtyard.
      The second prince turned back to the officials. "As I was saying, I want to help investigate the case and bring my brother's killer to justice."
      The officials exchanged a glance. "I think we better let His Majesty decide."
      The second prince offered them a smile that didn't quite reach his eyes. "Let's go, then."
      "After you."
      I watched as the second prince, Li Qingmei, and the officials left the courtyard. The moment they vanished from sight, Li Qinghua started sobbing again. "I'm so young, and yet I'm already a widow!" she wailed.
      Her maids were at her side in an instant to console her. 
      The princess turned to look at the line of maids standing in silence. She waved a hand at us, her expression more serious than I had seen before. "All of you can leave now."
      "Yes, Your Highness," we chorused.
      For the rest of the day, I absently scrubbed floors and lit candles. A different sort of silence had settled over the palace since the death of the third prince. Soon, we'd be taking down the red wedding decorations and replacing them with the white funeral ones.
      That night, there was a soft tapping at the window, and I climbed out to meet Shen Fanghuan.
      "Did you hear the news about the third prince?" Shen Fanghuan whispered worriedly as I shut the window behind me.
      I nodded tiredly. "I did."
      Shen Fanghuan's eyes were sad. "I'm afraid that while the palace guards are on high alert, I won't be able to meet you here."
      "I was afraid of that too. But I think it's for the best."
      Shen Fanghuan sniffled quietly, and I watched him wipe away a tear. "I'm sorry." He gave me an embarrassed smile and blotted his face with the back of his sleeve. "It only occurred to me when I was on my way here that this might be the last time the two of us will see each other."
      I smiled as I gently reached up to brush another tear away. "Don't say that. Once the culprit is found, the security will loosen, and things will go back to normal."
      Shen Fanghuan took my hands in his. "If this really is our last time seeing each other, I want to tell you that I don't regret meeting you. All the time we've spent together-I've treasured every moment of it. Every night that I snuck over here to talk to you has been worth it."
      I hugged him tightly as tears threatened. The stars in the sky above blurred together before my eyes. "Why do I feel like you're saying goodbye? Fanghuan, I don't want to say goodbye."
      "Since last month," Shen Fanghuan started, "I've had the feeling that someone was following me on my way here. But whenever I looked around, there was never anyone there."
      I nearly stopped breathing at that. "Could someone else be sneaking around the palace at night?"
      "I don't know. Come to think of it, there was one time when I could have sworn that I saw someone dressed in black running in the dark. If that was who was involved with the third prince's death . . . I can only pray I don't run into them."
      I begin to panic. "When you get back to your own room tonight, don't come back here. I don't want anything bad to happen to you. You should go. Quickly now."
      Shen Fanghuan let out a soft laugh, even though his eyes were still teary. "How am I supposed to leave if you won't let me?"
      I realized my hands were still wrapped tightly around his arm, and reluctantly let them fall away. But just as he turned to go, my feet were moving, and I wrapped my arms around his back. I was scared. "Please be careful," I whispered. "Please stay safe."
      After another round of goodbyes and reassurances, I watched his figure vanish into the night. Even after he was gone, I clasped my hands together in silent prayer. Please keep Fanghuan safe.
      
~
      
      I awoke in the morning to Weiwei gently shaking my shoulders. "Xiyan. Xiyan?"
      I sniffed as I sat up. "I'm awake."
      "Xiyan," Weiwei said in alarm as she looked at me. "Your eyes are puffy!"
      I raised a hand to my face. My tears had long dried on my skin, and my eyes were crusty. "Oh."
      "I'll go get you a bucket of water so you can wash your face," Weiwei said quickly as she slid out of bed. "Wait here-I'll be right back!"
      The days turned into weeks in the blink of an eye. Everything was foggy-my thoughts, my mind, the sky above the palace walls. I walked around in a daze, and yet at the same time, I was more alert than I had ever been before. I wanted to catch a glimpse of Shen Fanghuan. Even if it was just for a moment . . . I wanted to know if he was alright. As I walked the long corridors, I found myself wondering if he was just on the other side of the tall stone walls. Every time I passed a flower in full bloom, I wondered if it had been tended to by him.
      Every now and then, I would hear new gossip about the investigations: they had discovered letters the Crown Prince had hidden discussing his involvement in a shady business with a mysterious contact, but the prince was adamant that the letters weren't his and that someone was trying to frame him.
      "I think the Crown Prince did it," said one of the maids sitting next to me as we took apart old candle holders. I absently scraped the wax off a candle holder, only half listening to the conversation taking place.
      "Really?" one of the other maids replied. "It's becoming more and more obvious that the second prince did it and is now framing the Crown Prince."
      "Obvious?" the first maid questioned. "How?"
      "Apparently, the second prince has been having the Crown Prince spied on," the second maid said seriously. "They just caught the spy this morning. The Crown Prince is accusing him of planting evidence."
      "Who's the spy?"
      "No one special, apparently. I find it hard to believe. He's just a gardener. What was his name? Shen . . . Shen . . . I can't remember now."
    

    Chapter Seven

	My mind was completely blank. Shen Fanghuan-accused of planting evidence? But he wouldn't do such thing. He must have been sneaking out to see me.
	A silent tear slid down the side of my face. I needed to find Sun Xiaoting. She worked in the Crown Prince's courtyard, after all, and I had questions I needed answered. I stared unseeingly as I walked outside.
	"Xiyan!" a worried voice called, and I found Weiwei hurrying toward me.
	"Have you heard about Fanghuan?" My voice was a broken sound. "The Crown Prince is blaming him for working for the second prince and planting evidence. He's innocent, though," I said desperately. "Whatever he says in his defense-no one will listen to him. What's the word of a servant against the Crown Prince? There's more to the story than this. The last time Fanghuan met me outside our room, he told me that he had sensed someone else sneaking through the palace at night. This is all a setup!"
	"Even if it is a setup," Weiwei said, holding my gaze, "what proof do we have? We can't just go around making claims without evidence. No one will believe us based on our words alone."
	"Evidence . . . evidence . . ." I paced back and forth, wringing my hands together. Then I stopped. "Weiwei, have you seen Sister Sun? She knows more about the Crown Prince than she's letting on. And if the Crown Prince really is the murderer-"
	"But we don't know for sure if the Crown Prince is the murderer."
	"If Sister Sun still refuses to talk," I started slowly, "I'll need to think of another way to clear Fanghuan's name." I began to talk faster and faster as my panic rose. "Weiwei, what do I do? Is it even possible to sneak into the Crown Prince's courtyard and investigate for myself?"
	Weiwei's face paled. "Xiyan, sneaking into the Crown Prince's courtyard could get you killed!"
	"I know," I said faintly. "But if I don't do anything, Fanghuan will die."
	"How about you talk to Sister Sun first," Weiwei said worriedly. "I don't want Gardener Shen to die, either."
	That night, I sat in front of the mirror, combing through my inky hair as I waited for Sun Xiaoting to return. My hair was completely free of knots, but now if I were to stop combing, my panic would set in.
	Finally, Sun Xiaoting stepped inside the room, and I bolted toward her. "Sister Sun," I said breathlessly as I scanned her surprised face. "I have questions I want to ask you."
	Sun Xiaoting blinked at me. "Questions?"
	I took Sun Xiaoting by the arm and led her over to the corner of the room. I lowered my voice, even though I found that I didn't care that all the other maids in the room were watching us. "What do you know about the Crown Prince and his relation to the third prince's death?"
	Sun Xiaoting dropped her gaze. "So this is what you wanted to ask."
	"Do you know anything?" I asked desperately. "Please, Sister Sun."
	"I-" Sun Xiaoting opened her mouth but then closed it again. "I'm really sorry, Xiyan. I don't know."
	I felt my heart sink. "Alright. But could you help me with something else? One small favor?"
	Sun Xiaoting sighed as she crossed her arms over her chest. "What's the favor?"
	I took a deep breath. "You work in the Crown Prince's courtyard. Tomorrow, could you help sneak me in?"

~

	I followed Sun Xiaoting through the palace. The stone walls were tall and unyielding, and the sky above was hidden behind a thick layer of clouds. I tried to steady my breathing when we finally arrived at the eastern palace, the residence of the Crown Prince.
	"If the head maid here asks about you," Sun Xiaoting told me quietly, "just tell her that I'm not feeling well today and you're here to help out."
	I nodded.
	Sun Xiaoting dipped her head and walked off into one of the many rooms surrounding the large open yard.
	I glanced around the yard, scanning each of the closed doors of the buildings encircling it. Even though I had made it to the Crown Prince's residence, I had no idea where to begin looking for him. I took a deep breath, squared my shoulders, and set out to work my way through all the rooms until I found the Crown Prince.
	When noon rolled around, I was beginning to feel panicked again. I had nearly made my way through all the rooms, cleaning and polishing as I went, but the Crown Prince was nowhere to be found.
	My heart sank. Why had I thought I'd be able to find the him here? He was the Crown Prince after all-he could go anywhere in the palace he pleased.
	While cleaning a room, I suddenly heard the sound of light footsteps outside. Quietly, I walked to the door and peered out. My heart nearly skipped a beat as I recognized the princess consort gliding down the walkway.
	I trailed after her, careful to keep out of sight as she stopped in front of one of the rooms. She knocked once on the door with an elegant hand. "Your Highness?" she called through the wood.
	"Oh, it's you." The Crown Prince's voice was muffled.
	"May I come in?" the princess consort asked. There was something like exasperation in her voice.
	"Sure, fine."
	The princess consort pushed open the door and carefully stepped over the threshold. After glancing around to make sure no one was watching, I crept toward the room. I crouched by the window and pressed my ear against the wall.
	"Darling, is everything alright?" the princess consort's voice asked.
	"My second brother is too clever." There was annoyance in the prince's voice as he addressed his wife. "He's got everything in his control. I just found another fake document in my study linking me to illegal trading. I burned immediately, but I'm worried more of them have been hidden around the palace."
	"What do we do, then? The second prince is trying to frame us! Do we present our own evidence to the emperor? That way we can make it clear that you weren't the one who killed the third prince."
	"Present the evidence? I can't do that!"
	"But if the crime of killing the third prince really is placed on your head-"
	"If I present the evidence that I was planning to kill the third prince, even though I never went through with it, it's enough to get me deposed anyway! I just can't believe it. I had everything in place, and then my second brother had to go ahead and kill him. And now I'm the suspicious one for having to scramble to hide everything I set up!"
	"I know," the princess consort said sympathetically. "Neither of us expected the investigators would search our eastern palace either."
	"I know he's framing me. At least you keep that bottle of our poison powder on you at all times . . . I can't believe we never even got to open it. And then that servant boy we caught sneaking around at night . . . when I had him questioned, he claimed he had nothing to do with the second prince! He was adamant he saw someone else sneaking through the palace at night."
	"He's the perfect scapegoat for now," the princess consort said. "He might be a liar, but what if there really is someone else sneaking around? Then what?"
	The Crown Prince let out a heavy sigh. "I don't know. I just want to know where I went wrong. I've always been cautious. How did my brother get ahead of me? It's almost as if he knew every move I was going to make."
	"What do we do?" the princess consort asked again, quietly this time. "His Majesty already thinks you're the culprit. Just present the evidence, and maybe we'll be able to keep our lives."
	"I can't," the Crown Prince said shortly. "I've been playing the game for so many years already. I can't let this be the way the second prince beats me."
	Gathering my confidence, I rose to my feet, steadied myself, and, with a trembling hand, knocked on the door.
	The husband and wife stopped their conversation immediately. There was a long silence, then the princess consort called out, "Who's there?"
	"I'm a maid." My voice shook, but my resolve remained firm. "I'd like to request an audience with His Highness, the Crown Prince. I have something important to tell him."
	The door opened, and I found myself face to face with the princess consort. "How dare you," she said coldly.
      I instantly dropped to the floor in a bow and pressed my head to the wood. "Please, milady! Just let me talk to His Highness!"
      "The Crown Prince doesn't have time to speak with maids like yourself-" she started, but the prince cut her off.
      "Let her in."
      The princess consort frowned, but she stepped aside to let me into the room. Quickly climbing to my feet, I hurried inside and dropped into a deep bow. "Greetings, Your Highness."
      The Crown Prince stood from his seat, brushing invisible specks of dirt from his robes before motioning for me to rise. "You have something to say?" he asked tiredly. "Say it."
      I sat on my knees in front of the Crown Prince. "Your Highness, you've wrongly accused Gardner Shen."
      "The gardener?" The Crown Prince blinked at me. "You know that gardener?"
      "Please, Your Highness." I pressed my head to the floor in a bow. "He's innocent."
      "Oh?" The Crown Prince raised his brows, getting over his initial surprise. "It was reported to my men that he was sneaking around at night. The fellow servants he shared a room with testified to it. Tell me, how could he be innocent if he was sneaking around the palace at night? Would he not have malicious intentions?"
      "He had no such intentions." I lifted my head. "I'm guilty, Your Highness. He was only sneaking around at night because he wanted to visit me."
      "Visit you?" the Crown Prince echoed.
      I nodded shakily, mustering as much confidence as I could into my voice. "That's right. The two of us are in love. Your Highness can't falsely accuse him of planting evidence when he never did such a thing! I heard Your Highness's conversation with the princess consort. Your Highness, you can't use Gardener Shen as a scapegoat. Yes, in your eyes, he's just a gardener. In your eyes, he's just another disposable servant. But to me, he's one of the kindest and most innocent people I know. I love Shen Fanghuan. I won't let you wrongly accuse him!"
      The princess consort turned to her husband in annoyance. "Your Highness, should I send this unruly maid away for you? Let me have her beaten and-"
      "Wait, wait," the Crown Prince said as he brushed his wife off. "Is it true that the gardener doesn't work for the second prince?"
      I nodded my head vigorously. "It's true!"
      The Crown Prince sat back down in his seat. "How much of our conversation consort did you hear?" 
      "All of it."
      "Your Highness!" the princess consort hissed as she strode over to her husband. She looked at me icily. "We should silence this maid now before things get out of hand. All loose ends need to be-"
      "No, no." The Crown Prince shook his head. "We'll let her live. She could be of use. Obviously, the second prince has spies watching me. I should add to my number of spies watching him."
      "But what if she tells-"
      "She won't tell anyone if she wants to live," the Crown Prince said firmly as he looked at his wife. "You're far too suspicious for your own good, you know that?"
      The princess consort's eyes blazed, but she fell silent.
      The Crown Prince turned back to me. "May I ask, what's your name?"
      "My name's Xia Xiyan, Your Highness."
      "I've never seen you around here before," the Crown Prince noted. "How did you get in?"
      "I snuck in," I said simply.
      The Crown Prince raised his brows. "You're quite bold for a maid."
      I held his gaze. "I don't dare to lie to Your Highness. Your Highness wronged my lover. I'll do anything to prove his innocence."
      The princess consort took a step forward, and I couldn't help but flinch. "How dare you speak this way to the Crown Prince!"
      The Crown Prince stared at his wife in exasperation. "Why are you trying to scare her away when she can be of use to us?"
      The princess consort's expression was a permanent frown. "I don't understand, Your Highness. I still think it makes more sense to silence this unruly maid."
      "You're always wanting to silence people, but I'm starting to think that you're just jealous."
      "I-" the princess consort spluttered. "You're my husband! I'm just trying to help you-I'm trying to lighten your burden!"
      The Crown Prince turned to me. "Will you be willing to be sent into the second prince's palace as a spy?"
      I pressed my forehead to the floor as I bowed deeply. "Yes, Your Highness."
      The Crown Prince sighed. "I'm still in the process of investigating him. Fortunately, my father ruled that neither my second brother nor I can take charge of investigating the murder. If I can just catch my brother with that special informant . . . once I capture the culprit, I'll have the means to issue a full investigation of the second prince."
      I kept my head pressed to the floor. "I'll await Your Highness's orders."
      "Rise," he said tiredly. "The princess consort will show you out."
      I shakily climbed to my feet. The princess consort swept past me, and I silently curtsied to the prince a final time before following his wife.
      "I'd be careful not to run your mouth if I were you," she told me as I stepped past her. "My husband might be merciful, but I'm not. One wrong move from you, and I won't hesitate to have you silenced."
      "Yes, milady."
      
~
      
      When night fell, I returned to the maid's lodging. Weiwei instantly hurried over to greet me. "Xiyan!" she looked me up and down with worried eyes. "That was reckless."
      "I know." I took her arm and led her over to the mirrors and benches on the far side of the room. "I'm fine though, aren't I?"
      Weiwei lowered her voice as she began to unbraid my hair. "What happened? Did you find anything about the situation with Gardener Shen?"
      "The Crown Prince said that as long as I follow his orders and agree to spy on second prince, he'll let Fanghuan go."
      Weiwei's hands stilled. "You spoke with the Crown Prince? Xiyan . . . you could have died going there. And now he-he wants you to spy for him?"
      "Weiwei, my good sister"-I leaned back to look up at her-"I'm fine, really. I'm still alive. Even if I really did die, it would have been worth it. You don't understand, Weiwei. I'll do everything I can to prove Fanghuan's innocence. When you fall in love one day, you'll understand my efforts."
      Weiwei just pushed my head back up so she could continue working on my hair. When she finished, the two of us climbed into bed, and I listened to the soft chattering among the maids until they finally drifted off to sleep.
      I rolled over in bed for what must have been the hundredth time. It must have been the middle of the night, and the world was silent. Weiwei was right-I could have died going to the Crown Prince's palace, and if the princess consort had her way, I would have. I rolled over again. Suddenly, I sat upright and looked around the dark room.
      Where is Sun Xiaoting? I asked myself. I felt someone tug lightly on my sleeve, and I looked over to find Weiwei staring up at me. She silently gestured to the door.
      I slid out of bed, my feet tapping quietly over the wooden floorboards. When I reached the door, I gently pushed it open a crack and peered into the darkness beyond. A gust of chilly wind hit me in the face. Wrapping my arms tightly around myself, I pushed the door open and stepped out into the night.
      My unbound hair fluttered around me as I tiptoed over the stones and grass. I could hear the faintest sound of voices coming from the back side of the building. I crept toward them, holding my breath as I finally stopped and looked around the corner.
      Sun Xiaoting stood with her back to me, facing a man I had never seen before. He was dressed head to toe in black, and even in the dark, I could tell his outfit wasn't a palace design. I eyed the sword hanging at his side. Could he be a martial artist?
      "His Highness has new orders for you," the man told Sun Xiaoting. His voice was like ice.
      "I've already done so much for the second prince," Sun Xiaoting replied hopelessly. "I've already risked so much-why can't he let us go?"
      The man in black ignored her as he held out a small bottle to Sun Xiaoting. The smooth ceramic glinted in the moonlight. "You're to hide this in the Crown Prince's palace."
      Sun Xiaoting inhaled sharply. "Poison?"
      "This is the poison that was used to kill the third prince. If the investigators find this, there's no way the Crown Prince can escape blame this time. He put the blamed on a gardener for planting the evidence we snuck in before, but this time he can't keep making up excuses."
      "Why can't he let us go?" Sun Xiaoting asked again, and her voice broke as she dropped to her knees.
      "The life of your lover is in your hands," the man in black said contemptuously. "If you want him to live, do as the second prince tells you." With that said, he turned and strode away.
      Sun Xiaoting just sat there on the grass as she stared after him, shaking all over.
      Still trying to process what I just heard, I hastily turned on my heel. I crawled back into bed and pulled the covers over myself as my heart pounded away in my chest.
      I felt Weiwei poke me in the side, and I rolled over to face her. She looked at me with wide eyes. What happened?
