      I glanced over my shoulder to make sure that Sun Xiaoting wasn't coming back inside. "Sister Sun met up with a man who doesn't seem to work at the palace," I whispered. "He works for the second prince and wants Sister Sun to plant the poison used to kill the third prince in the Crown Prince's palace."
      Weiwei's eyes were wide. "This is the evidence we need to prove the Crown Prince's innocence. And if we can prove that he isn't the murderer-"
      "He'll let Fanghuan go!" I finished for her breathlessly. "She's probably going to plant the poison soon. If we want to take it from her, it will have to be tonight."
      Weiwei quickly shook her head. "We can't take it now. It's the middle of the night. Everyone in the court has long gone to bed. Besides, who do you want to present the poison to? The Crown Prince? The emperor himself?"
      "Of course it would have to be the emperor."
      "Xiyan, we're maids! Can we even request an audience with the emperor?"
      "I'll go find the Crown Prince," I whispered. "I'll bring the poison to him. You'll go request an audience with the emperor."
      "Me?"
      "Please, Weiwei."
      Weiwei took a deep breath, but then she nodded. "Fine. I'll try to request an audience with His Majesty."
      "Tomorrow morning," I said quietly. "That's when we'll steal the poison from Sun Xiaoting."
      
~

      I was positive I didn't get any sleep that night. Sun Xiaoting had returned shortly after I finished my conversation with Weiwei, and I kept one eye on her the entire night. I had watched her place the bottle of poison under her pillow, and now that the sky was slowly brightening outside, it was time for Weiwei and me to make our move.
      As the maids began to wake up and shuffle around the room, I sat up as well. Weiwei and I quickly changed into our uniforms and tied back our hair as usual, all the while keeping an eye on Sun Xiaoting.
      When Sun Xiaoting finally sat and began changing into her own uniform, Weiwei and I exchanged a glance.
      "Oh no!" I faked a cry of surprise as I knocked one of the mirrors onto the floor.
      Instantly, I felt all the maids' eyes on me. Sun Xiaoting walked over to check on me, and in that moment of distraction, Weiwei took the opportunity to snatch the bottle of poison from under Sun Xiaoting's pillow.
      "Sorry everyone," I called. "I'm fine." The maids were still giving me strange looks as I swiftly made my way over to the door. Weiwei was already waiting for me outside and handed me the bottle. The moment the door closed behind us, the two of us took off at a run. It wouldn't take long for Sun Xiaoting to realize the poison was gone.
      Once Weiwei and I were out of the maids' housing, we slowed to a walk. Running would only arouse suspicion. We walked together in silence for what could have been minutes or hours before our paths branched off in different directions. We exchanged nods as we split up, knowing we'd be seeing each other again very soon.
      I arrived at the eastern palace but began to panic when the guards at the entrance wouldn't let me pass. Spotting the princess consort beyond the entrance, I waved my arms furiously until she turned to look at me. Surprise flashed across her face, and she glided over to meet me.
      "I have evidence that can help clear the Crown Prince's name," I blurted, showing her the bottle of poison. "Please, let me see His Highness!"
      "Wait here," she said quickly as she turned and hurried off.
      I stood there with my heart beating rapidly in my chest. As I held the bottle of poison, I carefully examined the small ceramic container. There was nothing unusual about it-nothing out of the ordinary. But the longer I held it, the more I began to notice an almost floral scent.
      I frowned slightly, furrowing my brows as I sniffed at the bottle. I knew this scent: it was the fragrance Li Qingmei used.
      I nearly let out a laugh of disbelief. While I was certain the elder Li sister had nothing to do with the murder, her floral fragrance must have been everywhere in the second prince's residence by now. The second prince thought he hadn't left a single clue linking this murder back to him. But now, in his eagerness to incriminate the Crown Prince, he missed his wife's unmistakable fragrance clinging to the bottle.

    Chapter Eight

	I didn't have to wait long for the princess consort to return with her husband.
      "Your Highness," I said, holding out the bottle of poison to the Crown Prince, "last night, a maid working for you was given this bottle of poison by a man dressed in black. I heard the man tell her that this was the poison used to kill the third prince. She's been the one planting evidence in your palace, and she would have planted the poison too if my friend and I hadn't stolen it!"
	The Crown Prince immediately took the bottle of poison from me, his eyes widening as he turned the small bottle over in his hands.
	"You said you stole this?" the princess consort asked quickly. "Does the person know you stole it?"
	I could feel my panic beginning to creep up again. "By now, definitely."
	The Crown Prince turned to look at his wife. "We've got to hurry, then! We need to present this new evidence to my father before the second prince is alerted!"
	"You, maid"-the princess consort looked down at me-"run as fast as you can and request an audience with the emperor."
	"Yes, milady." I quickly jumped up and sprinted down the stone path.
	Everything blurred by me as I ran. I hoisted my skirts in an attempt to keep myself from tripping over them. My sweat plastered loose strands of hair to the sides of my face.
	When I reached the main courtyard in front of the courtroom, I paused for a brief moment, my hands on my knees as I tried to catch my breath. But then I heard the sound of something hard colliding with human flesh, and my head snapped up in horror.
	Weiwei was lying on an elevated wooden platform, and a palace guard stood next to her with a wooden paddle in his hands.
	"Weiwei!" I cried, and then I was sprinting forward.
	Weiwei raised her head from where she was lying on her stomach. Her face was streaked with tears, and her eyes were glazed with pain.
	"Stop!" I cried as the palace guard brought the wooden paddle down on Weiwei's back. The guard ignored me and raised the paddle again.
	I desperately threw myself over Weiwei's back. The guard's paddle hit me instead, and my entire body seemed to snap. I let out a cry as my eyes watered, but I didn't have time to catch my breath before the paddle struck me again.
	"Xiyan!" Weiwei was crying. "Get up!"
	"I won't move!" I gritted my teeth as I braced myself for the next blow.
	"Stop!" a loud voice commanded. "Stop in the name of the Crown Prince!"
	This time the guard immediately stopped, and I turned my head to watch him salute the Crown Prince.
	The Crown Prince looked to where Weiwei and I were lying on the wooden platform. "What's going on here?"
	"Your Highness," the guard said, "this maid was causing a scene outside the courtroom. She wanted to request an audience with His Majesty. She was unruly, so now we're punishing her."
	"You can leave," the Crown Prince dismissed the guard.
	Once the guard vanished from sight, I carefully uncurled myself from Weiwei. My back was tender, and my eyes stung with tears. I helped Weiwei off the board and dropped to my knees.
	The Crown Prince turned to the eunuchs standing in front of the courtroom. "Tell my father that I request an audience with him."
	Suddenly, a voice called out from the opposite side of the courtyard. "Wait."
	My heart sank as the second prince strode in, followed closely by Sun Xiaoting.
	"What is the meaning of this?" the Crown Prince asked. His eyes narrowed, and his posture became stiff as he watched his brother come to a stop in front of him.
	The second prince just smiled lazily. "I've come here to request an audience with our father."
	"What a coincidence," the Crown Prince said coolly. "So did I. You're not escaping this time."
	"Escaping?" the second prince raised a brow. "I'm afraid I don't understand."
	"This"-the Crown Prince pulled the bottle of poison out and held it out for the second prince to see. "Recognize this?"
	The second prince just chuckled mildly. "I'm sorry to disappoint, but I have not the faintest clue."
	"This is poison," the Crown Prince said grimly. "Your poison."
	"My poison? You do know that making such accusations won't work. Our father will see through them immediately. Dear brother, you're flailing."
	"So you won't admit it, then?" The Crown Prince scoffed. "That's fine. I know all about the man in black who's sneaking around the palace at night for you."
	"Do you, now?" The second prince's tone was laced with amusement. "How come I don't know about any man in black?"
	I lifted a shaky hand from where I kneeled on the stone floor next to Weiwei to point at Sun Xiaoting. "I saw the man in black speaking to her. He said he wanted her to plant the poison in the Crown Prince's palace!"
	"Xia Xiyan?" Sun Xiaoting's eyes were wide as she shook her head. "What are you talking about?"
	I blinked. "But you-"
	"I never thought you would slander me like this," she said as she looked down at me from behind the second prince. "Did the Crown Prince force you to say this?"
	"What-? No!"
	The Crown Prince pointed to Sun Xiaoting, and his eyes widened in recognition. "Aren't you a maid in my palace?"
	Sun Xiaoting quickly dropped into a curtsy. "I am, Your Highness."
	The Crown Prince frowned. "What are you doing with my second brother?"
	Sun Xiaoting dropped to her knees, tears glistening in her eyes. "Your Highness, I might be a maid at your palace, but I couldn't just stand by without doing anything. I've wronged you, Your Highness. But if I didn't say anything, I'd never be able to rest easy."
	The Crown Prince blinked in bewilderment. "What are you talking about?"
	Sun Xiaoting looked up at the Crown Prince. "You killed the third prince!" she shrieked. "And now you're trying to escape the blame!"
	As the exchange was going on, the eunuchs standing in front of the courtroom looked at each other, unsure what to do.
	"Here," the Crown Prince suddenly said as he handed the bottle of poison to one of them. "This is the poison that was used to kill the third prince, was it not? You're part of the investigation team, after all."
	The eunuch hastily took the bottle from the Crown Prince and carefully looked at the contents inside. "This is, in fact, the poison that killed the third prince."
	"See?" The Crown Prince turned back to the second prince. "What do you have to say for yourself?"
	"How do I know this isn't your poison?" the second prince asked lightly. There was an amused smile on his face.
	"The bottle-that's Eldest Lady Li's scent clinging to it!" I answered. "It had to have come from your palace!"
	"Be quiet, maid," the second prince said silkily. "You have no right to talk to a prince this way." But he was no longer smiling.
	"Sister Sun," I desperately turned to my fellow maid. "I know the second prince is forcing you to say these things. Please, I know the Crown Prince can help you if you tell the truth. Who's the man in black? Where's he hiding?"
	Sun Xiaoting just looked at me. "Xiyan, no one's forcing me. There is no man in black."
	"You had the poison," Weiwei gasped out. "Sun Xiaoting, we were the ones who stole it from you this morning."
	"The Crown Prince is desperate," the second prince said. "He knows he's at the end of the line. Now he's taking out the poison he himself used to kill the third prince. And he's blaming it on me?"
	The princess consort's eyes blazed as she took a step forward. "The poison doesn't belong to my husband."
	The second prince sighed. "My dear sister-in-law, I know you only mean well to defend your husband, but the fact stands that my third brother was poisoned to death, and his killer is still running free. Where's the justice in that?"
	"You have no right to talk about justice," I rasped as I glared at the second prince.
	The second prince just ignored me.
	The Crown Prince turned to address the eunuchs. "I demand a thorough investigation of the second prince's palace. And I want to be there to ensure my second brother doesn't threaten or bribe anyone."
	"Both our palaces have already been investigated," the second prince countered. "I hope I don't have to remind you that yours hosted incriminating evidence."
	The Crown Prince pointed a finger at Sun Xiaoting. "From this day forth, you aren't allowed to place a single foot in my palace."
	The second prince stepped forward. "Why take your anger out on an innocent maid?"
	The Crown Prince glared at his brother. "She works for you!"
	"These two maids certainly seem to work for you," the second prince rebutted with a nod to Weiwei and me.
	"These maids are helping me get justice!"
	"Silence!" a loud voice commanded, and the two princes instantly went quiet. Everyone turned to the courtroom as a middle-aged man dressed in gold robes emerged.
	Weiwei, Sun Xiaoting, and I immediately pressed our foreheads to the stones in a deep bow.
	"Father!" the second prince said hurriedly. "I have something to report."
	"Father!" the Crown Prince said desperately. "Please hear me out-"
	"Silence!" the emperor commanded again. His tone was a mixture of anger and annoyance. "It was difficult not to hear you both arguing outside my courtroom. What have I done to raise such errant sons like yourselves?"
	"Father," the Crown Prince tried again. "I have evidence that my second brother is involved with my third brother's death."
	"Evidence, evidence," the emperor said irritably. "I don't want to hear it. Can the two of you stop getting at each other's throats? The two of you are princes for god's sake, not wild animals. Stop pinning the blame on each other. Which one of you started this ruckus?"
	"Father, these maids started this mess," the second prince answered quickly. "The Crown Prince is using them to try and prove his innocence, and now they're slandering me."
	"How dare you." The emperor's voice was cold. Even though I was staring at the stone floor, I felt a shiver run down my spine knowing that he was looking at me. "Disrupting my court is a crime," the emperor continued. "And slandering the second prince . . . how bold the two of you maids are. You don't value your lives?"
	"Your Majesty!" I cried. "Please investigate the second prince! The bottle of poison-it had Eldest Lady-"
	"Silence," the emperor said, and I instantly fell silent. Groveling there at his feet, the feeling of complete and utter helplessness was beginning to sink in. "Guards, take these unruly maids away. Throw them in the prison."
	My head snapped up, and I barely even registered the clinking of armor as the palace guards hurried forward. "Your Majesty, have mercy!"
	The emperor just ignored me as someone roughly dragged me to my feet.
	"Your Majesty!" Weiwei's and my voice blended together as we were led away. The Crown Prince's face was pale as he stared after us. The princess consort stood by his side, her expression stoic as the two of them looked on.
	As we were dragged through the prison, I glanced through the dim light into the different cells, hoping to get a glimpse of Shen Fanghuan. But of the figures I could see through the dark, none of them were the gardener. It was cold and quiet, and our footsteps echoed loudly over the stones.
	I heard the jingling of keys in a lock, and then the guards shoved us into one of the cells. Still injured from the flogging, Weiwei tumbled to the floor, and I instantly dropped to my knees beside her. My back hissed in protest. I turned back to the guards just in time to see them lock the door to our cell and walk off without looking back.
	"Weiwei," I whispered, my voice shaking. "Are you alright? How long were they flogging you before the Crown Prince and I arrived?"
	"It wasn't very long," Weiwei answered with a wince. "I think I got around seven hits before you ran in."
	I quickly hurried to sit behind Weiwei. "Let me check your back." To my relief, there was no blood showing through the fabric of her dress. Then I slumped back against the stone wall as the reality of our situation sunk in. "Weiwei," I whispered as I drew my knees to my chest. "What do we do now? Are we going to die here?"
	Then a voice said, "Dying here depends on what exactly the two of you did to end up here in the first place."
	I blinked and raised my head to search for the source of the voice. A young man stood behind the bars of the cell next to ours. His eyes were tired behind his tangled hair, and he wore the outfit of a servant.
	"How long have you been in here?" I asked hesitantly.
	The man took a seat on the floor of his cell. "A few months now."
	I jumped up and scooted over to take a seat in front of him. Even with the wooden bars between us, it was as if we were all in the same cell.
	Weiwei took a seat beside me as she looked over at the young man. "Why were you locked up?"
	"My luck was bad," the man said with a sigh. "That's all. The guards didn't even tell me why they were arresting me, and I've been in here ever since. What about the two of you?"
	"We were thrown in here for acting unruly," Weiwei answered tiredly.
	The young man looked confused. "That shouldn't be enough to get you sent down here."
	I exhaled heavily. "The people we offended were in a bad mood."
	The man scooted closer to the bars, noticing our outfits. "The two of you are maids-would you happen to know a maid named Sun Xiaoting?"
	"Sun Xiaoting?" Weiwei and I exchanged a glance.
	"You know her?" the young man asked hopefully.
	Weiwei raised a brow. "Do you know her?"
	"Xiaoting is the woman I love," the man said simply.
	She really does love you, was what I wanted to say as I dropped my gaze.
	"Did you happen to see a young man brought down here a couple of days ago?" Weiwei asked quickly. "He's also a servant."
	The man frowned as he furrowed his brow. "There were a few young men who were brought down here in the past couple of days. I can't say for sure what happened to any of them."
	"Thank you," I said softly. I climbed to my feet, walked to the far side of the cell, and curled up on the cold stone floor. Is Fanghuan locked up here? If I yell, will the guards flog Weiwei and me again?
	I closed my eyes as they began to string with tears. I took one deep breath after another. I could smell the mildew, and I nearly gagged.
	I drew my knees to my chest. Where is Shen Fanghuan?
	The next few days were cold and silent. Weiwei and I huddled together in the corner of our cell. The light fabric of our own clothes did nothing keep us warm. My breath puffed out in front of me whenever I exhaled, and my fingers felt numb.
	The guards stopped by once a day to give the young man next door a bowl of porridge, but there was never anything for Weiwei and me. The second prince was keeping Sun Xiaoting's lover alive to control her, but there was no reason to keep Weiwei and me alive.
	My stomach let out a loud growl, and I curled in on myself as the pangs refused to subside. If we didn't freeze to death first, we'd certainly starve.
	The young man in the cell next to us offered us his bowl of porridge, but we declined. Even though I knew I should have hated Sun Xiaoting for turning against Weiwei and me, I couldn't bring myself to hold a grudge against her. She wanted to protect her lover's life; she had no choice.
	On the fourth day, we finally had a visitor. It was the Crown Prince. Weiwei and I both dropped to our knees and pressed our foreheads to the stone floor as he entered our cell.
	"Your Highness," I finally said as I straightened. My eyes searched his face. "How's Fanghuan?"
	"Shen Fanghuan . . ." the Crown Prince said slowly. "The gardener?"
	I nodded vigorously as I waited for him to continue.
	"He's dead," the Crown Prince said regretfully.
	I just stared at him. "What?"
	The Crown Prince shook his head. "When I sent someone to check on him, he was already dead. He had a withered flower in his hand. There was no mistaking that he was the gardener."
	"No." I couldn't believe what I was hearing. "Fanghuan isn't dead. He can't be."
	The Crown Prince sighed heavily. "I'm sorry."
	My tears were already flowing as I turned to look at Weiwei as if she'd reassure me that the prince was only joking. But her eyes were just as wide and disbelieving as my own.
	"Why come to see us?" Weiwei asked the Crown Prince in a whisper. "Your Highness isn't inclined to visit a couple of maids."
	The Crown Prince looked at me. "I feel inclined to thank you. If it wasn't for you getting that bottle of poison and recognizing Li Qingmei's scent, I wouldn't have been able to get the second prince reinvestigated."
	"How did he die?" I didn't even bother to wipe my tears away as I looked at him in despair. "When did he die? Where's his body now?"
	"It was my wife who went to check on him," the Crown Prince told me regretfully. "When she found him a few days ago, he had died from an illness. I'm afraid it was a combination of the cold and his lack of nourishment. My wife said he had a weak body to begin with and was surprised he even survived after being tortured by the interrogators. He refused to tell them what he was doing sneaking around the palace at night but remained adamant he had nothing to do with the second prince."
	I let out a sob.
	The Crown Prince sighed again. "I feel guilty. Even though I wasn't able to keep the gardener alive, I can help the two of you keep your lives. Tomorrow, a wagon will arrive at the palace. It will transport disobedient servants from the palace to the mines. You'll have to spend the rest of your years there as slaves, but it's the only way to stay alive."
      I just sat there, my mind and body completely numb.
	"Thank you for your generosity, Your Highness." Weiwei bowed deeply and pressed her forehead to the stones. When I didn't move, Weiwei tugged on my sleeve, and I slowly bowed as well. My fingers curled into fists.
	There was an echoing of footsteps through the prison as the Crown Prince exited the cell. I remained there with my forehead pressed to the floor for a long time before Weiwei gently helped me up.
	"Fanghuan's dead!" I whirled on Weiwei as my voice broke. 
	"I'm so sorry," Weiwei whispered. Tears glittered in her own eyes.
	"Weiwei," I sobbed as my eyes burned with tears. "Don't feel sorry for me. The one to feel sorry for is Fanghuan. I can only imagine how much pain he was in all alone in the dungeons. I can only how frightened his was. There's no sun. Did he freeze to death? Did he starve to death? He was innocent-why didn't anyone help him? And now . . . now he's . . ."
	I could no longer feel the cold of the cell. The silence roared in my ears, and my vision blurred. And then I really was screaming. My own chest hurt. My heart was breaking, shattering. There was so much pain. My head hurt as if someone had pounded a white-hot knife into my skull.
	"Xiyan!" Weiwei inhaled sharply as she made to move forward.
      I threw out a hand to stop her. A moment later, I was clapping my hands to my head, but there was nothing there. White-hot pain shot through my skull, and though all I could touch was my hair, I could feel the phantom sensation of my demon horns protruding. Suddenly, there was a crack, and I was crying again as my left horn exploded.
	A rush of magic surged through my veins. I could feel the power growing, growing . . . and then the world tilted as I passed out from the agony.

~

      After I finished my work, I hurried toward the library. The doors were open, and I slipped inside. I searched for Lady Hui, but the ghost was nowhere to be seen.
	Eagerly, I floated over to the far corner of the library and landed on the floor between two towering shelves. This time, instead of picking up a book, I gathered my magic and transformed myself into a human. I beamed as I looked down at my human form. I twirled around, and my billowing robes flowed with me. I held out one of my hands, and a gleaming spear appeared.
	I jumped to the other side of the aisle, and in a puff of smoke, I transformed into the beautiful maiden. I wasn't sure how many hours I spent jumping back and forth, acting out the roles of the brave hero and the beautiful maiden, until . . .
	"Found you!" a voice cackled from behind me.
	I jumped and swung my spear toward the source of the voice. The demons scattered into the air as I waved the blade at them.
	These demons were low level, like me, without physical forms. They laughed as they floated out of reach of my spear. Their smoky bodies gilded around my head. "If you want to play, we'll accompany you," they called.
	There was a flash as each of the demons took on the form of a different nightmare. In seconds, I was surrounded by a horde of ghosts. My fingers tightened around my spear. The stench of their rotting flesh filled the air, and I squeezed my eyes shut as I whirled at them with my spear.
	My spear was stopped mid-swing, and I slowly opened my eyes. Lady Hui stood in front of me, holding my spear.
	"Lady Hui!" I exclaimed. I looked around to find that all the demons had reverted back to their original smoky forms and were cowering from the ghost.
	Lady Hui smiled at me, but it was a smile that didn't reach her eyes. Today she was dressed in purple, and her scarves fluttered as she lowered my spear. "Are you pretending to be a human?" Before I could open my mouth to answer, Lady Hui snapped her fingers, and my human form vanished. Back in my original form, I floated in the air in front of her.
	"Please, Lady Hui," I pleaded, but she just snapped her fingers again. This time, when she turned to glide out of the library, a magnetic force dragged me along behind her.
	"The library is open for important purposes only," Lady Hui said coldly. She left me outside the library doors. Surrounded by the endless fog of the demon realm, I turned sadly and glided away.

~

	When I came to, the clattering of wheels over dirt was loud in my ears. If I listened carefully, I could hear the sound of hooves. I felt myself sway back and forth with the motion. Slowly, I opened my eyes and squinted from the sudden rush of sunlight.
	"You're awake!" Weiwei exclaimed in a whisper.
	The pain I felt in the cell had vanished completely. The surge of magic I had felt-it was gone too.
	As my initial grogginess faded, I pulled myself up and looked around. I was sitting in a wooden wagon, surrounded by a number of other palace maids. Some of them had tears streaking their faces, others silently stared at the green fields rolling out around us.
	"How long have I been unconscious?" I asked weakly.
	Weiwei glanced around at our forlorn companions. "Almost two days now."
	"Two days?"
	"What happened, Xiyan?" Weiwei's eyes were full of concern. "You just started screaming, and then you passed out in the cell."
	I reached up and absently ran a hand over my head. There were no horns there, only my tangled hair. But the phantom sensation still lingered. Of the two horns I had in my demon form, only one remained. It had been my overwhelming heartbreak that shattered it-a feeling completely foreign to demons. Did this mean I was one step closer to becoming a full human? But at what cost? I let my hand fall back down to my side and instead watched the land roll by around us.
	"We're out of the palace," I said blankly. I had always wanted to leave the palace and search for Yuxin. But during those last few months after I met Shen Fanghuan . . .
      I drew my knees to my chest, only to notice my feet were tied together with a bundle of thick rope.
	I reached down to try and untie it, but Weiwei just placed a hand on my arm. "I've already tried," she said quietly. "They purposely tied them this way so that the only way to remove them is to cut them."
	I closed my eyes for a moment, feeling the wind on my face. I opened my eyes and gazed unseeingly at the blue sky. The entire world had gone dull around me.
	From somewhere far away, Weiwei placed a comforting hand on my shoulder. But I could barely feel anything now.
	"Xiyan," Weiwei said quietly after the wagon rolled to a stop. The guards had dismounted their horses and were now passing out steamed buns among the prisoners. "Xiyan," Weiwei tried again. "You have to eat something."
	I just shook my head. "I'm not hungry." It was true; I had no appetite. Even the pangs I had previously felt in my stomach had vanished.
	"You haven't eaten for days," Weiwei said as she pressed one of the steamed buns into my hands. "At least take a bite."
	Too tired to argue, I lifted the bun to my mouth. Everything was flavorless.
	
~

	The next day, our path led us through a dense bamboo forest. As I watched the green blur around me, I found myself thinking back to the time when Yuxin and I had run away from the village.
	I closed my eyes again, and a silent tear slid down the side of my face.
	Suddenly, the wagon jerked to a stop. I blinked as the sound of whispering from my companions filled the still air, and I looked at Weiwei.
	Weiwei just shook her head, equally bewildered.
	I leaned around the side of the wagon, trying to get a glimpse of the guards in front. Suddenly, there was movement from the bamboo around us. A number of men charged toward us, each holding a wicked-looking blade. Despite my numbed state, fear flooded through me.
	There were screams as the maids in the wagon all dropped down. They pressed their hands over their ears as the bandits engaged the guards in combat. But the guards quickly fell one by one, and before long, the forest was silent again.
	My heart pounded away in my chest as one of the bandits stepped toward the wagon. The blood on his blade dripped onto the dirt path. "Listen up," he called gruffly. "You girls belong to us now. Be good and stay in your wagon until we find someone who will buy you for a good price."
	Trembling, I watched one of the bandits mount the horse pulling our wagon and made to steer the wagon around. But before he could move, there was a loud thump, and he tumbled off the horse.
	Two of the other bandits quickly hurried over to where their companion had fallen. I heard one of them inhale sharply. "He's dead!"
	Weiwei and I exchanged wide-eyed glances. 
	Suddenly, there was movement from the bamboo again, and a figure dressed in flowing red robes burst through the leaves.
	The bandits hesitated as they gawked at the young woman now standing in front of them, then charged at her with their blades raised.
	Sword in hand, the woman blocked and parried the bandits with ease, practically dancing among them. She cut them down as if they were stalks of bamboo, spraying blood as she went. It was gruesome, but there was something mesmerizing about the way she moved.
	In a matter of minutes, all the bandits lay dead on the forest floor.
	The woman sheathed her sword before walking over to the wagon. A lazy smile spread across her red-painted lips as she stood there in front of us. "Hello there, beauties."

    Chapter Nine

	"Who are you?" one of the former palace maids asked as the woman in red leaped into the wagon and effortlessly cut through our ropes with a dagger.
	The young woman flashed the girl a smile. "I'm Chen Han. No need to thank me, though-we ladies should always be helping each other. Isn't that right?" I just stared at her as she sliced through the ropes binding my ankles together. When Chen Han finished cutting all the ropes, she jumped back out of the wagon. Her robes billowed around her, and she flipped her long ponytail over a shoulder as she turned back around to face us. "There's a village just down the path there. Off you go."
	I hastily climbed out of the wagon, rocking on my feet as my stiff legs protested my weight. "Heroine, please wait!" I called.
	Chen Han blinked at me expectantly and folded her arms over her chest.
	"Where are you going?" I asked breathlessly.
	"I'm on my way to Jingcheng, the capital," Chen Han answered.
	"Can you take us with you?" I gestured to Weiwei and myself.
	The heroine in red just blinked again. "Take you with me? I don't know if that would be very convenient . . ."
	I suddenly pointed to the sheath strapped to Chen Han's back. I had seen it before, and I recognized it. "Do you know the hero Wu Ren?"
	"Wu Ren?" She let out a laugh. "Of course I know Hero Wu! He's the one who taught me martial arts. Do you know him?"
	"Hero Wu helped me out once," I explained.
	A grin split across Chen Han's face, and her eyes lit up. "Well, if you know my master, of course I can take you to see him! You can travel with us to Jingcheng as well." Then Chen Han looked over her shoulder and raised her voice at the rows of bamboo. "Fei Ziyi!"
	I looked on, stunned, as a handsome young man emerged from the foliage. As he made his way toward us, he nearly tripped over the dead bandits scattered across the forest floor. He was dressed in pale green robes and cradled a gourd of liquor in his hands. Despite being otherwise neatly put together, his dark hair was full of leaves.
	"Where were you when the bandits attacked the wagon?" Chen Han asked with a sigh. She took a step forward and began picking the leaves out of the young man's hair. "You were supposed to help me, you know, or at least be my backup."
	The young man, Fei Ziyi, just brushed her hand away, grinning lazily. Up close, he was noticeably flushed in the face and smelled of alcohol. "What bandits? I don't see any bandits attacking."
	Something flickered behind Chen Han's eyes as she pressed a hand to her head. "Forget it." Then she turned back to Weiwei and me with a semi-exasperated smile on her face. "This is my junior, Fei Ziyi. We learned martial arts together under Master Wu."
	Fei Ziyi saluted Weiwei and me. "Hello. I'm Fei Ziyi. But you can call me Handsome Fei-"
	"Don't mind him," Chen Han interjected, unamused. "He's a hopeless drunk."
	Fei Ziyi stared at me with furrowed brows, then grinned again. "Hey, who does she look like?"
	I blinked. "What?"
	Chen Han crossed her arms again. "Who?"
	"Lady Xu Moyue!" Fei Ziyi exclaimed triumphantly.
	Chen Han frowned faintly as she looked me up and down. "Now that you mention it, she does resemble Lady Xu a little bit."
	"Who's Lady Xu?" I asked quickly.
	"A prostitute," Chen Han answered matter-of-factly.
	"She's not just a prostitute," Fei Ziyi cut in. "She's said to be the second most beautiful woman in the capital."
	"We should get a move on if we want to see our master before it gets dark," Chen Han cut in.
	Fei Ziyi ignored her as he staggered in front of me. "Are you sure you aren't her twin sister?"
	"Heroine Chen," I started, but the heroine in red just waved me off with a wry smile.
	"Just call me Sister Chen. There's no need to be so formal."
	"Sister Chen," I said. "Do you know if Lady Xu has any other names?"
	Chen Han tilted her head to the side. "Other names?"
	I dropped my gaze. "I actually have a sister. We were separated years ago. As a maid in the palace, I had no way to look for her. But now that I'm free, any clue as to where she might be is one I need to investigate."
	Fei Ziyi burst into laughter at that. "You think Lady Xu might be your sister?"
	Weiwei frowned at him. "Why not?"
	Fei Ziyi continued to laugh. "She might look like Lady Xu, but I'm sure that's as far as the similarities go."
	Chen Han took a step forward. Then, taking Weiwei and me by the arms, she marched us past Fei Ziyi and down the path.
	"Wait for me!" Fei Ziyi called after us.

~

	We walked for a few hours before we came across a small town. We stopped to buy food and, despite our protests, Chen Han even took Weiwei and me to buy a new set of clothes.
	The heroine in red flashed us a grin when we left the clothing shop. "Don't worry about paying me back. Martial artists like me don't ask for anything in return. We just believe in helping those in need. Now"-she glanced around the bustling streets-"where did Ziyi run off to?"
	As the heroine walked through the streets, crimson robes billowing, numerous heads turned in her wake. But Chen Han didn't seem to mind in the slightest. She just smiled as she inclined her head to the gawking townsfolk.
	I could feel the eyes of the townspeople on my back as I hurried to keep pace with Chen Han's strides. "Do they always stare at you like this?" I asked quietly.
	Chen Han just gave me a knowing smile. "I wear red for a reason. This way, I can attract attention. I don't need to go searching-all the good and bad will always come to me."
	We found Fei Ziyi further down the path. He was walking aimlessly, drinking from his gourd of liquor.
	"Ziyi!" Chen Han came to a stop in front of him. "We're all done here. It's time to go visit our master."

~

	After leaving the village, we walked for another hour before veering off the main road. Then after a long trek up a hill overflowing with greenery, we finally arrived at its summit. There, Chen Han lit incense and bowed to the stone plaque before setting the thin sticks in the dirt.
      "Master," Chen Han said solemnly. "Your disciples have come to visit you."
	I stared at the characters carved into the rough stone. "The Tomb of Wu Ren," it read. Clasping my hands together, I bowed deeply.
	"Liquor," Chen Han said, and Fei Ziyi passed her his gourd. The heroine in red took a swig from the gourd before pouring what remained in front of the tomb as an offering. She smiled faintly after she passed the gourd back to Fei Ziyi. "Master, we owe you so much. I know how you were mocked for taking Ziyi and me as your students. But you just laughed them off, saying that you've always liked a lively environment. Thank you for believing in us."
	"Thank you, Master," Fei Ziyi echoed as he and Chen Han bowed to the tomb.
	Chen Han straightened and faced Weiwei and me. "Do the two of you have anything you'd like to say to my master?"
	"Thank you, Hero Wu," I said quietly before bowing deeply. Weiwei bowed as well.
	The path was hidden behind the fog as we made our way back down the hill. "There's no more liquor," Fei Ziyi complained. "We need to find the nearest town and get more."
	Chen Han leveled him a look over her shoulder. "If you want liquor, you have to pay for it out of your own pocket. And don't tell me that you're running low on money. That's because whenever we do take on jobs, I do all the work, and you don't get paid."
	"Just this one last time. I promise I won't ask for money again."
	"You said that last time," Chen Han pointed out, "and the many times before that."
	Fei Ziyi blinked. "Did I?"
	After a silence fell between them, Weiwei asked, "Why are the two of you heading to the capital?"
	Chen Han let out a laugh. "It was Ziyi's idea. He's been running low on money for a while now and suspected that there would be more job opportunities in a city like Jingcheng. I'm just tagging along to make sure he stays out of trouble."
	"That's not true," Fei Ziyi said as he slung an arm around Chen Han's shoulders. "You follow me because you're lonely without me."
	Chen Han flashed him an amused smile but made no move to shake his arm off.
	By the time the sun set, we had found a town to stay the night in. Chen Han led us to a hotel, and to conserve money, decided it would make sense for all of us to crowd into one room.
	Once we got a room, I walked over to the window and pushed it open to look out at the now silent streets. From behind me, I could hear the sound of faint murmuring and the jingling of coins. I looked back over my shoulder just in time to see Fei Ziyi's green robes flutter around the corner of the door.
	"I don't think he'll be back until morning," Chen Han said matter-of-factly as she pocketed her coin purse. Then, taking a seat, she unstrapped the sheath on her back and drew her sword. The blood of the bandits we had encountered earlier in the day had dried on it, and she got to work cleaning it off.
	I turned back to the window. After hearing the news of Shen Fanghuan's death, everything seemed to have lost its color. But now that I had the opportunity to find Yuxin, I couldn't give up. If I didn't take this chance to find Yuxin, I'd regret it for the rest of my life.
	I turned to look at the heroine in red. Out of everyone I had met so far, Chen Han and her late master Wu Ren were the most like the heroes in the stories I read. It felt like an entire lifetime ago since I departed from the demon realm.
	When Chen Han caught me looking at her, she shook back her dark hair and flashed me a smile. "Why are you looking at me?" She rested her chin on the palm of her hand. "Don't want to sleep yet? The three of us could have some fun."
	"What kind of fun?" I asked tiredly.
	"No thanks," Weiwei interjected stiffly. "We're going to bed."
	Chen Han just shrugged and went back to cleaning her sword. "Alright."
	Even if I wanted to sleep, I wasn't sure if I could. I looked at Weiwei. She was sitting on the bed, absently combing her fingers through her long hair. If the bandits really had sold us, would we have been separated too?
      My hands clenched in the rough fabric of my skirts. When we had picked out clothing, Weiwei and I gravitated toward the cheapest outfits in the hopes to save Chen Han's money. The color and quality weren't close to that of the maid uniforms we wore at the palace, but I didn't care. I wasn't a palace maid anymore, anyway; I was just a normal girl now.
	And so I sat there by the window until the sun rose over the town in the morning.

~

	"I wonder if we could catch a ride to Jingcheng," Chen Han mused as the four of us walked down the path. Even though we were trying to travel at a steady pace, the way Fei Ziyi would often drunkenly stagger off considerably slowed our progress.
      We weren't in a rush, but I could tell that Fei Ziyi's actions were beginning to get on Weiwei's nerves. "Sister Chen, has he always been this way?" Weiwei finally asked Chen Han after Fei Ziyi strayed from the path again.
	Chen Han glanced over her shoulder at Fei Ziyi, and something like sadness flickered behind her eyes. "As far as I can remember, yes."
	Weiwei sighed. "And you just let him go on this way?"
	Chen Han returned her gaze to the road. "Who am I to determine what he can and cannot do?"
      "Sister Chen, there's one more thing I'd like to ask," I changed the topic. "Your sheath-it looks exactly like Hero Wu's."
	"My master had this commissioned for me," Chen Han said proudly as she pulled out the sheath for me to see. "He got one for Ziyi too. The three of us match, you see. My master wasn't just my teacher; he was also like a father to me."
	Fei Ziyi returned shortly and flashed us a drunken smile. "Hello there, beauties." 
	When Chen Han ignored him, he wrapped an arm around her shoulder and sensually leaned in to brush his lips against her neck. The heroine in red leaned into his touch for a moment, then scoffed and pushed him away. "You reek of alcohol."
	On the way to the capital, we stopped off at another small town. After finding us a hotel to stay in for the night, Chen Han left us there, declaring she would earn us some money. It was obvious that Weiwei felt the same uncertainty as I did about being left alone with Fei Ziyi, but the moment we arrived in the hotel room, Fei Ziyi passed out in the corner, and to our relief, he stayed that way for the rest of the night.
	For a while, I sat alone by the window until Weiwei timidly joined me. "Xiyan, how are you feeling?"
	I just stared out at the night. "Weiwei, Fanghuan entered the palace in the hopes of living a better life. Maybe if he hadn't been caught up with me, he could have really achieved a better position in the palace. Maybe in the future, he'd move on from being a servant and be able to support himself. Maybe then he'd be able to see his mother again."
	Weiwei placed a hand on my shoulder as I blinked back tears.
	"I don't know what to do now," I whispered. "I can't stop. If I stop, I'm afraid I'll fall apart entirely. I need to find my sister. I want to know how she's doing. If she's alive."
	"Once you find her, then what?"
	I watched the moon emerge from behind the clouds. "Then maybe we'll talk. We'll catch up on all the years we spent apart. And then I don't know."
	"Would you join the martial arts world?"
	"Join the martial arts world?" I fell silent. Hero Wu had warned Yuxin and me all those years ago not to join the martial arts world if we wished to live long lives.
	In the morning, there was a knock on the door, and Weiwei quickly jumped up to answer it. Chen Han stepped inside, her crimson robes flowing behind her. "I chased down a few bandits. We'll have enough money for now. I'll go wake Ziyi, then we can head out."
	Weiwei and I exchanged a glance. "You were just up all night," Weiwei said. "You don't want to rest?"
	Chen Han let out a laugh as she prodded a still unconscious Fei Ziyi with her sheath. "Rest? I'm used to this kind of travel. What's the point of sleep anyway when there's so much to do? Come on, wake up."
~
	
	"Another day of walking and we should enter the capital," Chen Han told us as we walked. "Jingcheng itself is gigantic, and the brothel where Lady Xu works is a good distance away from the walls. I know the two of you came from the palace, but have you ever seen Jingcheng itself before? Have you ever experienced Jingcheng outside the palace?"
	I shook my head. "I've only gone through small towns and villages before. I've read about the former capitals, but I think I've only read about Jingcheng a couple of times in the stories."
	"I hope it won't sweep you away," Chen Han said with a smile. "It truly is a magnificent city. But like any sort of glory, it too has a dark side."
	As the towering walls of Jingcheng emerged on the horizon, I felt my pulse begin to quicken. Somewhere behind those walls was the palace-the city within the city. If it wasn't for the three people at my side, I wasn't sure if I'd be able to muster the courage to return.
	Getting through the city gates was surprisingly easy. Once inside, I practically had to grab Weiwei's arm to keep from getting swept away in the crowds of people walking down the wide streets.
	Chen Han raised her voice to be heard over the surrounding chatter. "It isn't like this everywhere. The city gate is always one of the busiest places."
	As we walked, I looked around in awe. Shops and restaurants stretched as far as the eye could see. Vendors called out on every street. I tentatively tugged on Chen Han's sleeve once we got farther away from the city walls. "Sister Chen, do you know the way?"
	Chen Han flashed me a smile. "Of course."
	I looked back over my shoulder only to find that Fei Ziyi had vanished. "He's gone!"
	Chen Han let out a sigh. "He'll find us eventually."
	It felt like no time had passed at all before the three of us were standing across the street from the brothel.
	"What are we waiting for?" I said. "We should go in and check-"
	Weiwei grabbed my wrist before I could move. "Xiyan, we can't go in there."
	I blinked. "Why not?"
	"It's improper for women to enter a place like that," she explained under her breath.
	My hands curled into fists in my skirts. "What do we do? Do we wait for Fei Ziyi?"
	A smile played on Chen Han's red-painted lips. "Getting in is easy. All you need to do is dress up in men's clothing."
	"Easy?" Weiwei stared at Chen Han in exasperation. "You say it as if you've dressed up in men's clothing and snuck into brothels before."
	"I have," Chen Han said simply.
	"Where do we get men's clothing from?" I asked hesitantly.
	"Well, we could wait for Ziyi to find us and then borrow his robe, or we could find a clothing store."
	"We should wait for Fei Ziyi," I decided. "Besides, can we really pull it off? Even if we dress up in men's clothing, none of us would be very convincing."
	Chen Han just flashed me a reassuring smile. "You worry too much. The fragrance they burn inside has an intoxicating effect. The staff have been exposed to it for too long today and won't be able to see straight."
	The three of us ended up sitting outside a noodle shop nearby. Chen Han treated us to lunch, and I was reminded again of the way Hero Wu had helped Yuxin and me.
	By the time Chen Han spotted Fei Ziyi approaching, the sun had set, and the city was glowing with lantern light. Even at night, the bustle of the city was as lively as ever, and I could have sworn there were even more people out now.
	After getting a room in a hotel to change, it was only a matter of minutes before I was standing outside the brothel again. I was alone and dressed in Fei Ziyi's pale green robe. Chen Han had tied my hair up and given me a paper fan.
	Mustering my courage, I squared my shoulders and walked toward the entrance of the brothel. The women lingering by the entrance giggled as they beckoned me inside.
	"Young Master," a young woman cooed as she waltzed up beside me. "Is it your first time here?"
	I quickly nodded, already uncomfortable. I cleared my throat, trying to make my voice sound deeper. "Can I see Lady Xu Moyue?"
	"Lady Xu?" the young woman blinked at me in a disappointed sort of way. "Why, everyone comes here to see Lady Xu. You'll have to wait your turn. Sometimes you'll even have to wait weeks to get a glimpse of her. But if you've got some money . . . who knows? Maybe I could help you get to the front of the line."
	"I-I'm sorry," I stammered, fumbling for the paper note Chen Han had given me earlier. "I only have the standard fee."
	The woman fanned herself with her delicate fan before plucking the note from my hands. "That's alright, then. You got lucky. Lady Xu is only playing one tune on her lute for each of her customers tonight. It will be your turn before the night is over. I'll show you to the waiting area."
	I nodded silently as I followed her through the brothel. Lanterns glowed in every corner of the large room. The entire place smelled of alcohol and perfume, and gauzy silk was draped over every surface. The smokey haze in the air gave the whole place the illusion that it was blurring in and out of focus around me. When I looked closer, I noticed paper talismans discreetly taped over all the doors and windows. Some of them had fallen on the floor, and I paused for a moment to unstick one from the bottom of my shoe. I held it out to the woman escorting me. "What's this?"
	"Why, that's to keep the ghosts away," she giggled as she plucked it from my hands. "With Madam Qin overseeing the practice, you have nothing to worry about."
	"There's ghosts here?"
	The woman's smile gave nothing away. She pointed me to a chair, and I took a seat, trying my best to pretend not to notice the women casting playful smiles and winks in my direction.
	I sat there for what felt like hours until I was finally called to follow another woman to see Lady Xu. I quickly rose from my seat, and my legs were completely stiff as I hurried up the flight of steps to the second floor. There, I was directed down a long hallway to a set of wooden doors.
	I stood in front of the doors for a moment before finally sliding them open. The room beyond was lit by flickering candles, and a screen in the middle hid the woman on the other side. There must have been a window behind her because she was silhouetted in silver, and I held my breath as I slowly walked around the screen.
	A young woman around my age stood in the center of the room. Her smiling lips were painted crimson, and her face was powdered in white. In one hand she held a porcelain cup, and in the other, a pitcher of wine.
	"Young Master," she greeted me.
	"Lady Xu," I started, trying to see if I could recognize any of the young woman's features through her heavy makeup.
	"Young Master," she said again, gracefully gilding forward. "I don't think we've met before." She pushed the cup of wine into my hands. The gauzy fabric of her long sleeves and scarves fluttered, and I could smell the alcohol on her breath as she draped her arms over my shoulders.
	"Wait!" I quickly took a step back.
	The young woman blinked at me with wide eyes. "What's wrong? Do you want me to sing you a song first? But I've been singing songs all night and have gotten bored-"
	"I'm not a 'Young Master,'" I said firmly.
	The young woman stared at me for a moment before bursting into giggles. She raised one of her long sleeves to her mouth as she laughed. "I know. I knew you were a woman the moment you stepped into my room." She took a step forward and reached out with a graceful hand for my robe.
	I took another step back. It was now or never. And if the woman in front of me wasn't who I was looking for . . . 
      "Yuxin," I said desperately as I searched her face. "It's me!"
	The young woman froze, her entire demeanor changing almost instantly. She stared at me as if seeing me for the first time. "Bunny?" she whispered. "Is that you?"

    Chapter Ten

      "Yuxin!" I let out a sob as I dropped to my knees. The cup of wine slipped from my hand, and I burst into tears. "It really is you!"
      "There, there"-Yuxin crouched down in alarm-"don't cry."
      I sniffled as Yuxin wrapped her arms around me. "Yuxin, I'm not dreaming, am I?" I finally drew away to look at her. "What happened to you? Why are you here?"
      Yuxin continued to look at me in disbelief. "Bunny . . ."
      I jumped to my feet and took Yuxin by the hand. "Quick, we need to get out of this awful place!"
      Yuxin sat there on the floor as I tried and failed to pull her to her feet. "I can't leave. Me and all the other women belong to Madam Qin. If we try to run, she'd hunt us down and sell us off to a place where we'd never see the light of day again. Only once we're out of the city walls would we truly be free from her grasp."
      "I'll get you out of the city walls." My tone was more confident than I felt.
      "Unless you have enough money to buy my freedom, I don't think there's anything you can do either."
      I reluctantly let go of Yuxin's hand. After walking over to the window, I opened it to peer outside. It was too high to jump.
      "I have an idea," I said suddenly as I fumbled with Fei Ziyi's green robe. "How about you change into my clothes and sneak out of here!"
      "But then what about you?"
      My fingers stilled over the fabric, and my shoulders slumped. "Oh." I sat on the wooden floor in defeat.
      Yuxin sat next to me and placed a gentle hand on my shoulder. "What happened to you all this time?" she asked quietly.
      "I was sold to the palace and worked as a maid there until . . ." I took a deep breath. Yuxin waited patiently for me to go on. "I worked there as a maid until I fell in love. I fell in love with a gardener. He died because of me, Yuxin. And then I got sent out of the palace to work in the mines. Except on the way, bandits attacked us, and then the other girls and I were rescued by a heroine in red."
      Yuxin blinked. "A heroine in red? Do you mean a martial artist?"
      I nodded my head vigorously. "Exactly! Since then, my friend and I have been traveling with Sister Chen and one other martial artist named Fei Ziyi."
      "Sister Chen?"
      "Chen Han," I clarified.
      Yuxin just shook her head. "I haven't heard of them."
      "Both of them seemed to know of you, though," I pointed out.
      Yuxin furrowed her brow. "Maybe they saw a performance of mine here. When I get individual customers, most of the time I don't get to know their names."
      "Yuxin," I started, but Yuxin cut me off.
      "You shouldn't call me that here," she said sadly. "Here, I'm Lady Xu Moyue."
      "I guess I should tell you that I have a second name now too. Xia Xiyan."
      "Xia . . . you decided to take my surname?"
      "We're sisters. I think it's the most fitting."
      Yuxin smiled as she nodded. "We're sisters." Then her smile faded. "I'm sorry about the gardener."
      Tears stung in my eyes. "My heart aches whenever I think about him, but the only thing I can do is move forward. I kept going, and I found you. I need to figure out how to get you out of here."
      Yuxin gracefully rose to her feet and walked over to pour a new cup of wine. After downing it, she refilled the cup and returned to me. I just blinked as she held the cup out for me to take.
      "I've never drank before," I admitted. "I'm not sure if it's a good idea."
      Yuxin shrugged her shoulders and drank the cup's contents herself.
      "Are you drunk?" I asked hesitantly.
      Yuxin offered me a faint smile. "No. I sobered up when you called out my name."
      As I looked up at Yuxin, I noticed another paper talisman fluttering above the window. "Are there really ghosts here?" I whispered.
      Yuxin smiled and shook her head as she followed my gaze. "Madam Qin knows that she's running a dirty business. This is a manifestation of her own superstitions and paranoia. While I do secretly hope this place will be burned to the ground, if it falls, I fall along with it. A girl like me has no future."
      "You will have a future," I said determinedly. Then I sighed. "I should go ask my friends how to get you out of here." I rose to my feet but paused to look back at Yuxin. "But I don't want to leave you here either."
      "Wait," Yuxin said softly. "Now that we've finally had the chance to meet again, let me play a song for you. Now that we've finally met again, I'm selfish and want to keep you here a little longer." I watched her retrieve her lute, pull up one of the chairs from the table, and take a seat. "I've been composing this song. It isn't finished yet, but I'll play it only for you."
      Yuxin sang the melody and plucked the strings. I was captivated by the music. When she finished the song, I stared at her in awe. "You learned to play the lute?"
      She sighed softly. "I learned how to play multiple musical instruments here. I didn't have much of a choice. When I first started learning, I was forced to practice until my fingers bled. Madam Qin is known for making even the most stubborn of girls into the perfect entertainers. She breaks us down bit by bit and then finally pieces us back together in the image she wants. And now look how profitable we are." I opened my mouth in horror, but Yuxin just smiled sadly. "You shouldn't stay here."
      "Wait for me," I whispered as I reluctantly made my way to the door.
      After opening the doors, I snuck a final glance back over my shoulder. I was worried that I had imagined the entire thing, that my eyes were playing tricks on me, that the smoke in the air had gotten to my head. But Yuxin was still there. I carefully closed the door before hurrying back down the hallway.
      When I arrived at the hotel, I felt as if I were about to collapse. "How did it go?" Weiwei asked as she quickly hurried over to me.
      "Lady Xu is her," I said breathlessly.
      Chen Han beamed. "That's great, then!"
      I tugged my hair out of its topknot. "I just don't know how to get her out of there. I-" I started. "Sister Chen, is there any way we can sneak her out? Could you or Fei Ziyi carry her safely out the window?"
      "Carrying her out the window isn't a problem," the heroine in red said thoughtfully. "The real problem is how to carry her out without the people on the streets noticing. If they do see, then we're all in trouble, and getting out of the city will be a lot more difficult."
      I walked over to the hotel window to look out at the street. Even in the middle of the night, it was still bustling. I frowned slightly. "There isn't some sort of curfew?"
      "Not in this area."
      "Maybe the window isn't the best way to go," Weiwei pointed out.
      I slumped against the wall. "Let's keep thinking of ways, then."
      Weiwei stepped forward to help me change out of Fei Ziyi's robe. "Fei Ziyi went out drinking, but he should be back soon."
      Shortly after the words left her mouth, there was a knock on the door. Chen Han went to get it, and Fei Ziyi joined us in the room. The heroine in red wrinkled her nose. "You smell like you've been drinking too much."
      When Chen Han turned away from him, Fei Ziyi just wrapped his arms around her from behind. "I was wrong. Next time I won't get so drunk."
      Chen Han just sighed. "That's what you said the last time. And the time before that. And countless times before that. Where were you when I needed you to back me up in the fight?"
      Fei Ziyi just grinned at her from over her shoulder. "I'm here now, aren't I? I'll always come back to the woman I love."
      Chen Han didn't protest as Fei Ziyi brushed his lips against her neck. "You're too late," she said quietly.
      Instead of responding, Fei Ziyi kissed Chen Han passionately. Weiwei and I looked on in surprise as Chen Han kissed him back. When the two of them drew apart, Chen Han helped Fei Ziyi take a seat at the table. Once he was seated, Fei Ziyi rested his head on the table and was asleep in seconds.
      "Are the two of you lovers?" I asked, wide-eyed.
      "We were once," Chen Han said as she regained her composure.
      "If you're not anymore," Weiwei said with a frown, "why do you still kiss?"
      Chen Han just smirked. "Even if I don't love him the same way I used to, when it's just the two of us traveling together, it gets boring when we're at odds for too long."
      I opened my mouth to respond, but a yawn came out instead.
      Chen Han's smile softened. "You should try and get some sleep. It's been a long journey."
      "Why are you helping us so much?" Weiwei asked as she followed me over to the bed.
      "Martial artists are honorable," the heroine in red said simply. "And I want to help people out the same way my master helped me."
      
~
      
      When night fell the following evening, I put on Fei Ziyi's green robe and walked into the brothel again. Fei Ziyi came in after me in a new set of robes, and the two of us were both escorted to the waiting area to wait for our turns to see Lady Xu.
      I had to wait at least a couple of hours before I was finally called. I jumped up from my seat and hurried up the stairs.
      When I reached the room, I quickly pushed the doors open. "Yuxin," I whispered through the smoky haze. "I'm here to get you out!"
      "Bunny!" Yuxin's voice greeted me, and a moment later she emerged from behind the screen, her skirts fluttering in her wake.
      I hurried over to the open window and waved into the night. A moment later, Chen Han leaped into the room in a flurry of crimson fabric.
      "You!" Yuxin blinked at Chen Han.
      Chen Han smirked as she flipped her long ponytail over her shoulder. "Greetings, Lady Xu."
      "Do the two of you know each other?" I asked as I looked back and forth between the two.
      Yuxin fanned herself with a silken fan. "I didn't know your name was Chen Han."
      "And I didn't know you had a sister," Chen Han responded in amusement.
      "We're going to get you out of here," I said quietly as I hurried to Yuxin. "You'll change into the robe I'm wearing and then walk out of here as me. No one stopped me all this time. I'm confident no one will recognize you. Don't worry about me. I have a way to leave after you. Sister Chen will meet you outside and take you to our meeting place."
      Yuxin slowly nodded her head. "Alright."
      Chen Han sat Yuxin down on one of the chairs at the table. I took off Fei Ziyi's robe, then watched as Chen Han wiped off Yuxin's heavy makeup before skillfully applying new makeup to completely change her features.
      I applauded the heroine in red when she took a step back to admire her work. "Sister Chen, it's perfect!"
      Chen Han flipped her hair over her shoulder. "Of course it is."
      After helping Yuxin change out of her gauzy skirts and into my outfit, I took Yuxin's hands. "Be careful," I whispered. "I'll see you outside."
      Yuxin nodded and gave my hands a reassuring squeeze. Once she slipped out the door, Chen Han leaped back out the window, and I was left alone in the now silent room. I paced back and forth in front of the window, occasionally glancing out at the glowing city beyond.
      Before long, there was a knock at the door. "It's me," Fei Ziyi's voice called.
      I let out a breath of relief I hadn't realized I was holding in as Fei Ziyi stepped inside. After he gave me his robe to change into as we had planned, I quickly made my way toward the exit. When I reached the door, I turned back to Fei Ziyi. "You remember the plan, right? All you need to do is pretend to be passed out when people come to check on the room."
      Fei Ziyi just nodded as he took a seat at the table and poured himself a cup of wine.
      After leaving the brothel, I returned to our hotel room to find that Chen Han had already escorted Yuxin inside. Yuxin was sitting on the bed, and she smiled as I hurried over to her. "You were right! In the midst of all the haze, no one gave me a second glance. I'm afraid that it won't take Madam Qin long to realize I'm missing, though. If we don't leave tonight, tomorrow morning the streets will be swarming with her spies."
      "We just need to wait for Ziyi to get back," Chen Han reassured her. "Then we can leave."
      I blinked as I looked around the room. "Where's Weiwei?"
      Chen Han winked. "I asked her to run an errand for me."
      We didn't have to wait long before the door opened and Weiwei stepped into the room. She was carrying a tray of snacks and set it down on the table. "I bought what you asked for. I'll start wrapping them up for our journey out of the capital."
      When she finished, Weiwei wiped her hands on her skirts before turning to Yuxin. "I don't think I introduced myself yet. My name's Hu Qiuwei, but you can call me Weiwei like Xiyan does if you'd like."
      Yuxin gracefully dipped her head. "I'm Xia Yuxin."
      "I met Weiwei in the palace," I explained. "If it wasn't for her, I don't think I would have been able to survive there as long as I did."
      Yuxin inclined her head again in Weiwei's direction. "I have to thank you for looking out for my sister."
      After I changed my clothes and fixed my hair, the three of us sat there in the hotel room, waiting for Fei Ziyi to return. We waited and waited and waited. The sun began to rise, and yet there was still no sign of him.
      Chen Han rose to her feet, frowning. "That's it. I'm going looking for him," she said.
      I worriedly turned to Weiwei once the heroine in red left. "Do you think something happened to him? Do you think he was accused of abducting Lady Xu and was taken away by guards?"
      Weiwei shook her head. "That wouldn't make any sense. Besides, they have no proof that Fei Ziyi is related to Lady Xu's disappearance."
      "Do you think they took him away for questioning, then? He would be the last person who was alone with Lady Xu, after all."
      We didn't have to wait long before there was a knock on the door.
      "It's me," Chen Han's voice called.
      I rushed over to throw the door open. The heroine in red stood in the doorway with a very wasted Fei Ziyi leaning against her for support.
      "What happened?" Weiwei asked quickly as she hurried over to help Chen Han drag Fei Ziyi inside.
      Chen Han shook her head. "We told him to pretend to be passed out, remember? Turns out he really did pass out. No one could seem to wake him up either." Then she added, irritably, "The brothel has probably been alerted by now."
      Fei Ziyi looked over at Chen Han. "We want money, don't we? How about we return her?"
      Chen Han ignored him. "Let's get out of here before it's too late."
      Before I knew it, I was walking down the packed streets with Chen Han and Yuxin at my side. For the sake of not attracting attention, Chen Han had swapped her vibrant red robes for a plain dress. Fei Ziyi and Weiwei walked about ten paces in front of us in the hopes that we could avoid attracting attention in smaller groups.
      We walked for hours, and just when we were nearing the city gate, what I feared would happen finally came to pass.
      "Young Lady," a voice called. I slowly glanced over my shoulder to find a group of men walking toward us. "Yes, you," the man said. All the men were looking at me. Since Yuxin was still dressed in men's clothing and her features hidden behind a layer of makeup, she hadn't caught their attention-yet.
      Chen Han caught my eye, but I just motioned for her to take Yuxin ahead.
      I slowed my pace so Chen Han and Yuxin could pass me up before turning around to face the number of men now standing in front of me.
      "I've heard that Lady Xu Moyue, the second most beautiful woman in Jingcheng, has gone missing. We can't let such a famed young woman vanish from our city now, can we? So here we are watching the gates."
      "I'm sorry," I said with a lot more confidence than I felt. "I'm not Lady Xu."
      "That's exactly what a runaway would say," one of the men said with an unpleasant smile.
      "I'm not Lady Xu," I said again. Out of the corner of my eye, I watched Chen Han and Yuxin make their way through the crowded streets and toward the line of people leaving the city gates.
      "When you look closely, she does look a bit different than Lady Xu," another one of the men said as he looked me up and down. "Madam Qin invited us to see Lady Xu dance before. I don't think they're the same person."
      "We should take her back with us just in case," the first man decided. "If she really isn't Lady Xu, then at least we've gotten Madam Qin another pretty young woman, and we can continue our search."
      Just before they could step forward, there was a cry from behind me. "Help! My brother is dying!" I recognized Weiwei's voice immediately as I whirled toward the sound. At the sound of her cries, a crowd of people began to gather, and in the confusion I managed to escape into the mob. I hurried toward the city gates. Once I joined the line to exit, I tugged my hair out of its braid and kept my head down until I passed through.
      I found Chen Han and Yuxin waiting for me outside. "What happened?" Chen Han asked. I could see the concern in her eyes as she looked me over for injuries. "I was just about to go back for you."
      "Weiwei caused a scene," I said. I felt light headed. "Then I managed to escape."
      After concluding that I was unharmed, the heroine in red motion for us to follow her. "We shouldn't stick around here. There's a small town a couple of hours away from here. Ziyi and I always pass through there whenever we leave the capital. He'll know where to find us."

    Chapter Eleven

	The walk along the wide dirt road went smoothly. By the time Chen Han led us to one of the wine houses in the small town, my legs ached to the point where each step became an effort.
	We didn't have to wait more than an hour before Fei Ziyi and Weiwei showed up.
	"Xiyan!" Weiwei excitedly hurried over to me.
	Chen Han just folded her arms over her chest as Fei Ziyi took the vacant seat next to her. "If you had stayed in that brothel any longer, we would have been caught."
	Fei Ziyi looked up at Chen Han. "We're out of the city now, aren't we?"
	Chen Han leveled him a look. "If it wasn't for Weiwei, Xia Xiyan would have been kidnapped."
	Fei Ziyi scowled, fanning himself with his paper fan. "Hu Qiuwei punched me in the stomach and yelled to everyone that I was dying."
	"You'd be more convincing that way," Weiwei said unapologetically.
	"Maybe we should have left you in the brothel altogether," Chen Han said distastefully.
	Fei Ziyi handed Chen Han a cup of liquor. "Here. Take this as my apology."
	Chen Han scoffed but took the cup anyway. Then she turned to Weiwei, Yuxin, and me. "Where are the three of you going to go now?" 
	"I don't know," I admitted. "I don't think we'll be returning to Jingcheng for a long time, though." I turned to glance over at Yuxin. "Maybe we'll find a small town and start over. The three of us know how to do laundry. Maybe we can start a laundry business and make a living."
	Yuxin rested her chin on her hands. "A laundry business? We're free now. We can do anything we want, and you want to start a laundry business?"
	"What's wrong with a laundry business?" Weiwei asked.
	Yuxin let out a sigh. "We tried a laundry business in the past."
	"We were young back then," I pointed out.
	"We were young back then," Yuxin agreed. "We were young, and we didn't know how the world worked."
	"So then what do you propose we do?"
	Yuxin rose to her feet, then bowed deeply to Chen Han and Fei Ziyi. "I want to join the martial arts world. Please take me as your disciple."
	Chen Han coughed. "You want to join the martial arts world? You should know that martial artists often don't live long."
	"I know." Yuxin continued to bow. "Please take me as your disciple."
	I rose to my feet to stand next to Yuxin. Holding my hands in front of me, I bowed as well. "Please take me as a disciple too."
	"And me," Weiwei added as she joined us.
	Chen Han exchanged a glance with Fei Ziyi. "There was a reason our master was reluctant to take students," she said slowly.
	"Then why did he decide to take the two of you?" Yuxin questioned.
	Chen Han sighed. "The two of us didn't have futures to begin with. Our master took us in out of pity."
	I looked up at the heroine in red. "What do you mean?"
	"Take Fei Ziyi, for example. He's actually the son of a well-off family in Jingcheng. Or at least he was before his entire family was killed. He was only four years old at the time and would have been killed too if our master hadn't been drawn to the sound of fighting. Even though my master agreed that Ziyi's family deserved what they got, he also believed that a four-year-old child didn't deserve to die for a mistake his parents had made."
	"If you don't mind me asking," Weiwei said quietly, "what exactly did his parents do wrong?"
	Fei Ziyi answered, "They worked for the government and found they could make even more money by selling classified information to enemy states. When the emperor found out, he ordered them and every generation of their family to be executed for treason. So even now as I live in the world under a different name, I'm still and will always be the son of the treasonous family who nearly brought harm to our empire."
	"Your parents," I started timidly, "they really sold information? They weren't framed?"
	Fei Ziyi shook his head. "When I was old enough, I went to investigate myself. I was convinced my family had been set up, and I would stop at nothing to avenge them. I thought they were righteous. But in the end, the harsh and inescapable truth was that they had betrayed the country for their own greed. In the end, I realized I really didn't know them at all."
	I waited for Fei Ziyi to go on, but he just poured himself another cup of liquor.
	After a moment of silence, Weiwei turned to Chen Han and softly asked, "What about you?" 
	"My story isn't nearly as interesting," Chen Han said mildly. "I was born to a poor family, and it was difficult to get enough food for the three of us. My father tried to sell me, but no one in my village had any money either. So eventually he kicked me out of the house and forbade me to come back. I had nearly starved to death in the snow when our master found me."
	Weiwei dropped her gaze. "My own father sold me for two bags of rice."
	Chen Han let out a sigh. "The three of you really want to become my disciples?" After we nodded determinedly, she sighed again. "I can teach you martial arts. But once you know enough to protect yourselves, you should leave the martial arts world. You still have a future. You don't have to die an early death. For now, I'll grant your wishes and take you as my students."
	"Should we call you 'Master Chen' now?" I asked eagerly.
	Chen Han held up a hand. "Please don't. 'Sister Chen' is fine."
	Yuxin turned to the heroine in red. "When did your late master start teaching you martial arts?"
	Chen Han flashed her a knowing smile. "Ziyi and I have been learning ever since we were children. Now, we should probably start heading off before we lose him."
	I turned to look over at Fei Ziyi, who was nodding in and out of consciousness. "Good call."

~
 
	The five of us journeyed together for three long weeks before we finally arrived at a secluded residence. When Chen Han pushed open the wooden doors, I eagerly hurried forward with Weiwei and Yuxin at my side. I looked around in awe at the courtyard in front of me. Even though it was overgrown, and the paint on the walls was beginning to peel, there was something peaceful about it.
	Chen Han smiled at our energy. "Follow me. I'll show you inside."
	The three of us eagerly trailed after the heroine in red as she led us toward the wooden building at the back of the yard. "How long has it been since you've been back here?" Yuxin asked as she looked around the interior of the building with wide eyes.
	"Ziyi and I haven't been back for around a year," Chen Han said absently. "This was our master's home. He left it to the two of us." We followed her up a flight of steps and then through a doorway into a dusty room. "This is where the three of you will stay."
	Weiwei hurried over to the window and excitedly pushed it open. I joined her and leaned out to look at the foggy landscape beyond. The way the green and gray blended together was almost like a painting.
	When I turned back around, I realized that the only piece of furniture in the room was a small table sitting in the center. "This used to be my room when I was younger," Chen Han explained. "After my master passed, I cleared everything out. All the furniture is in the shed out back, though. We'll head down there later, and the three of you can pick out what you want."
	After leaving the room, Chen Han led us down the rest of the hall. "On the far end is my master's room. And then around the corner is the room Ziyi and I share. There's the study next to the main room down downstairs. The kitchen is on the ground floor as well."
	Weiwei, Yuxin, and I spent the rest of the daylight hours setting up our room. We picked out a couple of furniture pieces from the shed and worked together to haul them up the stairs.
	By the time we finished with the room, the sun had dropped from the hazy sky outside, and night had embraced the world. I stood proudly by the door with Weiwei and Yuxin as the three of us admired our work. We hadn't been able to find any beds, so we had set up makeshift ones on the floor with the blankets we had found.
	It didn't take long before the three of us were lying next to each other. Weiwei was on my left, and Yuxin was on my right.
	I wasn't sure when I had fallen asleep, but when my eyes flickered open, I was greeted by the darkness. I shuddered slightly as a chilly wind brushed against my skin. Noticing that the window was open, I slowly sat up. Weiwei was still fast asleep, but Yuxin was nowhere to be found.
	I rose to my feet, careful not to disturb Weiwei, and tiptoed across the room to the window. I found Yuxin standing on the ledge outside, leaning against the railing as she gazed up at the cloudy night sky.
	"Bunny," Yuxin greeted me without turning around.
	"Can't sleep?" I asked softly as I climbed over to her. "Do you want to talk about it?"
	Yuxin's inky hair fluttered in the wind. "After everything that happened, I just can't believe I'm finally free. After we were separated, for the first year, I would cry each night. Every time I tried to run away, I was never successful. When I first became a full-fledged prostitute, that first year, I cried every night too. But then one day, even when I lay bruised and broken on the floor, I couldn't cry anymore."
