	"What happened?" I whispered.
	"I had come to accept that my fate was no longer mine," Yuxin said simply as she turned to face me. "I remember being stubborn at the start and refusing to work. But if we didn't work, we wouldn't get food to eat. I went hungry for days. That was only at the start, though. Now everyone in Jingcheng knows my name. I made them adore me. Believe it or not, I almost got a taste of freedom once. But fate is a cruel thing. I thought I'd be trapped there forever, and then you showed up."
	I placed a hand on Yuxin's shoulder.
	"What about you and the gardener?" she asked as she rested her arms on the wooden railing.
	I smiled wistfully as I looked up at the sky. "I really loved him. Yuxin, tell me, would it have been for the best if I never told him that I loved him? That way he'd still be alive, and I'd still be a maid in the palace."
	"If you were still a maid in the palace," Yuxin said softly, "the two of us wouldn't have had the chance to meet again."
	"Yuxin," I sniffed, "I don't know what to feel. I know I should be happy about our reunion, and I am, but even now, I just feel so lost."
	Yuxin offered me a faint smile. "Life is unpredictable. Don't completely blame yourself."
	I just shook my head as I wrapped my arms around her. "I've missed you."
	"I've missed you too."
	After I finally drew away, I decided to ask, "What do you think of Sister Chen and Fei Ziyi? You seemed to know Sister Chen. How did you know her?"
	"Sister Chen visited me a handful of times at the brothel," Yuxin said thoughtfully. "Apparently, she was meeting informants there. As for Fei Ziyi, when I would dance, I remember seeing his face in the audience. From what they told us that day when we left Jingcheng, I think their pasts sound plausible. And Sister Chen . . . I think she's gone through a lot more than she's letting on."
	"What do you mean?"
	Yuxin frowned. "You probably don't know this, but she has a deep scar that runs across her entire abdomen. It doesn't seem like the kind of wound one would get in a fight either."
	"Are you sure she didn't injure herself in a fight?"
	"I'm positive," Yuxin said seriously. "I've seen a lot of different types of scars. With Sister Chen, I get the feeling it's almost like someone tried to cut her stomach open."
	I shuddered. "I think it's probably for the best if we don't bring this up with her. That's her own private matter."
	The two of us stood outside in silence for a few more minutes before turning and climbing back into our room through the window. Weiwei was still fast asleep when we rolled into bed.
	I lay there thinking for a while, and I could tell Yuxin was lying awake as well.

~

	In the morning, the three of us were woken by a knock on the door.
	Chen Han stood in the doorway, her red robes starkly contrasted against the thick morning fog. "Help yourself to breakfast downstairs, and then we'll begin our first day of training."
	Weiwei, Yuxin, and I made quick work of changing into the new clothes Chen Han had brought up for us the previous day. I tied my hair back into a high ponytail, then the three of us hurried downstairs in matching outfits. After a quick breakfast, we found Chen Han waiting for us in the yard outside. The air was crisp and cold, and the grass was covered in dew.
	"I can be a lenient teacher if you want me to be," Chen Han said as she placed a hand on her hip. "I can also be a strict teacher. I know that the three of you have no experience in martial arts, and it isn't my intention to torture you with intensive training. But if you want to learn, and if you're willing to put in the effort, I can assure you that with me as your teacher, you will make progress."
	Yuxin bowed. "I want to learn."
	I bowed as well. "Me too."
	"And me," Weiwei added.
	A smile tugged at the corners of Chen Han's red-painted lips. "Then let's begin."

~

	By the time we broke for lunch, I was already in pain. My body and mind ached, and my hair was plastered to my head with sweat. Weiwei and Yuxin were in similar conditions; the former had flopped onto the ground, and the latter was still breathing heavily.
	During our training session, the fog had cleared up to reveal the pale blue sky. "I don't know if I can do this," Weiwei said from where she was still laying on the grass.
	I tiredly pulled Weiwei to her feet. "Come on, let's go get something to eat."
	Yuxin looked around the yard as we followed Chen Han back into the wooden building. "Where's Fei Ziyi?"
	"Ziyi?" Chen Han echoed absently. "He's probably still sleeping upstairs."
	"Does he always sleep until lunch?" Yuxin asked, unamused.
	Chen Han just sighed as we sat at the table inside. "At night, when he's not with me, he's drinking. Then he sleeps until lunch, suffers from hangovers until the sun goes down, and then he's drinking again."
	"He does seem a little pitiful," I said quietly.
	Chen Han nodded as she helped herself to the plates of food laid out on the table.
	"Fei Ziyi must have been different when your master was still alive," Yuxin mused.
	"He was," Chen Han said as she poured herself a cup of liquor. "Even though he always liked to drink, he was different back then. After he went to investigate his family, and then after our master was killed . . . well, he wasn't quite the same."
	"If you don't mind me asking," Weiwei whispered, "how did your master die?"
	"A few of the larger martial art sects were clashing at the time," Chen Han explained as she ran a finger over the rim of her porcelain cup. "A rumor spread that my master had joined the fight, and one of the sects decided to take him out."
	I stared at her. "Who spread the rumor?"
	"Ziyi and I investigated. It was a few members from the losing sect. Apparently, they thought if they used my master's name, they could intimidate their enemy. My master was never interested in joining a sect because of the petty conflicts and cut-throat competition between them, but he was hunted down anyway."
	I turned to Yuxin with wide eyes. "When we met Hero Wu, he told us that he wasn't anyone special. I didn't know he was that powerful."
	"My master was a humble man," Chen Han said wistfully. "He taught Ziyi and me to be humble and help those less fortunate than we are. He was never strict with either of us, but he was firm and always made his principles known."
	"Why was he buried on that mountain?" Weiwei asked. "Why not here where you could visit him every day?"
	"My master told Ziyi and me that when he died, he wanted that hill to be his final resting place. He thought it was peaceful there."
	In the afternoon, we trained some more, and by the time it was time for dinner, the sun had dropped from the sky. The clouds returned and threatened rain on the horizon. After Weiwei, Yuxin, and I took turns in the bath, we shuffled back to our room.
	"Maybe if it rains tomorrow, we won't have to train as vigorously," Yuxin said hopefully as she brushed her damp hair over her shoulder.
	I elbowed Yuxin halfheartedly. "Weren't you the one who said you wanted to learn martial arts?"
	 "I do." Then she sighed and said, "Xiyan, do you remember that story of the female hero who defeats the demon? Even after all these years, is it silly of me to hope that I might still be her?"
	I shook my head and smiled. "I don't think it's silly at all."
	Weiwei looked back and forth between the two of us. "I think I'm missing something. What female hero are you talking about?"
	"I heard a story once," Yuxin said wistfully as she walked over to prop the window open. Pattering rain grew louder as she leaned against the window frame. Staring out at the misty night, Yuxin recalled the tale. "There was a story that a demon would appear in the world, and a female hero would rise up to stop it from doing evil. The female hero is said to be a girl with a cursed fate . . ." she trailed off.
	I stepped over to Yuxin and wrapped an arm around her. "I believe in you. If you want to be the hero, I'll support you. And who knows? Maybe there's more than one female hero. I think you and Sister Chen would make a great team."
	"But then what about you?"
	"Me?" I let out a laugh. "All I want is a simple life."
	Yuxin giggled as she climbed into bed. "I see you haven't changed at all."

~

	The next few weeks of training with Chen Han were just as grueling as the first, but we always put in our best effort. By the end of the first month, I found that the exercises we ran through were less tiring. And by the end of the third month, Chen Han decided it was time to have the three of us try out practicing with swords.
	She handed us wooden swords, smiling. "I think you girls are ready for the basics. Ziyi better start practicing again, or he'll find himself being outshined."
	I looked over at the wooden building at the back of the yard. "Sometimes I forget that Fei Ziyi is living here with us. It's like he's almost nonexistent."
	Chen Han sighed as she drew her blade. "Anyways, watch carefully. If you have any questions when I'm done, make sure to ask them."
	That night, the four of us sat around the table for dinner. Chen Han was watching Yuxin with a faint smile. Yuxin noticed her gaze and looked at her, bewildered. "Sister Chen?"
      "You're very different from the persona that was Lady Xu Moyue," Chen Han commented. "I like this version of you better-the version who chooses her own path and is true to herself."
	Yuxin's smile was genuine. "Me too."

~

      The next evening, I had just finished my bath when a fragrant scent wafted up from the kitchen. I made my way downstairs to find Chen Han sitting alone at the table with a bowl of noodles in front of her.
      I slid into the seat across the table from her. "Today's your birthday?"
      Chen Han nodded as she offered me a smile. "Ziyi forgot again." Even though she was smiling, there was something sad behind her eyes.
      "You made the noodles yourself?"
      Chen Han nodded again. "Ziyi and I used to make them for our master every year. He would make them for us too."
      "Fei Ziyi might have forgotten," I said as I gave the heroine a small smile, "but I'll remember. From now on, I'll make you birthday noodles each year."
      Chen Han really did smile this time. "Thank you, Xiyan. When's your birthday? From now on, I'll make you a bowl of noodles on your birthday."
      I hummed. "I don't know when my birthday is. Whenever Yuxin's birthday is, that can be my birthday too. I'll go upstairs to get Yuxin and Weiwei. The four of us can celebrate your birthday together."

    Chapter Twelve

	Over the next couple of months, I noticed myself gradually improving during our training sessions. As the weeks passed, the rainy season was quickly upon us, and our training sessions were considerably shortened. While we had tried to convince Chen Han that we were fine practicing outside in the rain, she didn't want to take any chances with us catching a cold.
	Some nights, as the rain pattered away outside, I would lie wide awake in the dark between Weiwei and Yuxin. I would stare up at the ceiling, thinking of Shen Fanghuan until I burst into tears. When that happened, Weiwei or Yuxin would wake up and comfort me.
	But tonight, after making sure that the two of them were still fast asleep, I carefully climbed out of bed and made my way over to the window. Then after gently pushing it open, I leaned against the frame and looked out. Out of the corner of my eye, I saw something red fluttering in the cool breeze.
	I pushed the window open further and climbed over the ledge. My feet landed on the walkway that surrounded the entire second story.
	"Sister Chen!" I whispered as my eyes fell on the figure illuminated in silver moonlight.
	Chen Han turned around to face me. Her hair wasn't in its usual ponytail; instead, it fluttered around her in the wind. She smiled faintly. "Looks like someone found me."
	I hurried over to her. "What are you doing out here? You'll catch a cold! It's still raining-what if the rain blows in?"
	Chen Han shook her head. "It's fine, really."
	"What are you doing out here?" I asked timidly.
	The heroine in red gave me a knowing look. "I don't sleep, remember?"
	I furrowed my brow. "How can you not sleep? Everyone needs to sleep."
	I took a step closer to her. Her face was completely bare from the makeup she normally wore, and the circles beneath her eyes were uncannily prominent.
	"Are you always out here at night?" I asked worriedly.
	"Not always."
	I took Chen Han by the arm and made to lead her toward the stairs. "Come with me to the kitchen-maybe we can make something to help you sleep." She didn't move, and I looked at her with wide eyes.
	Chen Han just shook her head. "It won't work. Over the years, I've tried everything that I could. My master took me to see a doctor when I was younger, and the doctor was adamant that my condition couldn't be fixed with medicine."
	I inhaled sharply. "Insomnia?"
	"You could say so," Chen Han said mildly. "If I'm being honest, some days I feel so tired and lethargic that I can't do anything. If I was attacked at a time like that, I'd be a goner."
	"Does Fei Ziyi know about this?"
	"It's hard to say." Chen Han just smiled sadly. "Don't worry about me. I've already tried everything that might help. You should go back to bed. If it isn't raining, tomorrow we might head to the town together to restock our food supply."
	I sighed. "Alright."
      Weiwei and Yuxin were still asleep when I climbed through the window, and I quietly returned to my spot between them. In the morning, I shook my companions awake.
	"I have something I need your advice on," I said as I looked between Weiwei and Yuxin.
	"What is it?" Yuxin asked, still blinking sleep from her eyes.
	I motioned for them to lean in close as I lowered my voice. "I think Sister Chen has insomnia. She can't sleep at night. Last night I saw her without her makeup, and she has circles this big under her eyes!"
	"That would explain why she doesn't sleep," Weiwei said faintly.
	I sighed sadly. "Sister Chen's done so much for us already. If there's something we can do to help her in return . . ."
	Yuxin suddenly perked up. "Yesterday, Sister Chen mentioned that if the rain stops today, she'll take us to the marketplace. Maybe there we can look around for some sort of medicine."
	"She told me that she's already tried everything that could possibly be helpful," I said heavily. "She's probably tried all those medicines before."
	"Then what can we do?" Weiwei asked.
	I frowned thoughtfully. "The three of us will think of something. Maybe we could ask Fei Ziyi for help?"
	"Fei Ziyi?" Yuxin let out a laugh. "What do you think he could do?"
	"I still think we should ask him."
	Weiwei rose to her feet. "I can go with you."
	I stood up and looked at Yuxin. "Would you mind keeping Sister Chen away from the room she shares with Fei Ziyi for a few minutes? If she finds out that we want to help her, I don't think she'll let us."
	Yuxin nodded. "I can do that."
	After the three of us changed and tied up our hair, Yuxin left first to find Chen Han. Once we could hear the sound of the two of them talking downstairs, Weiwei and I hurried down the hall. We came to a stop in front of the door to the room Chen Han shared with Fei Ziyi. Then after exchanging another glance with Weiwei, I gently knocked on the door.
	There was no response.
	Squaring my shoulders, I knocked again, louder this time.
	"Who is it?" Fei Ziyi's voice called.
	"Xia Xiyan," I answered. "And Weiwei. We're sorry for waking you up, but we want to ask you a question regarding Sister Chen."
	I nearly jumped backward as the door slid open. Fei Ziyi stood in the doorway. Even though there was a lazy smile on his face, there was something almost serious in his eyes. "What happened to her?"
	"Do you know about her insomnia?" I asked quietly. "When I saw her without any makeup last night, she looked sickly."
	Fei Ziyi blinked. "Insomnia? She's sick?"
	Weiwei frowned. "So you don't know."
	Fei Ziyi glanced over our heads as if checking to make sure no one was around, then invited us into the room.
	I cautiously stepped over the threshold, and Weiwei quietly slid the wooden door closed behind us. I glanced around the room as I followed Fei Ziyi over to the small table off to the side. I wasn't sure what I had expected, but the room was fairly empty. If it weren't for the messy pile of empty liquor jars in the corner and the smoke wafting up from the small incense burner near the entrance, I would have thought no one had lived in the room for a very long time.
	Fei Ziyi asked Weiwei and me to take a seat on the opposite side of the table from him, and we obliged. I glanced down at the board on the table, my eyes following the rounded black and white tiles snaking over it. When Fei Ziyi caught me looking, he just laughed and brushed the tiles off the board with a sweep of his long sleeve.
	"Go?" Weiwei asked mildly as Fei Ziyi removed the board from the table and set it to the side. "Do you play it with Sister Chen?"
	Fei Ziyi laughed again. Then his expression faltered. "I can never win against her. My pieces always seem to move around the board when I'm not looking, and I can never remember if I was the one who put them there or if she moved them."
	"Are you drunk?" I asked uncertainly.
	"What?" Fei Ziyi fanned himself with his paper fan. "Of course not!" Then he frowned, pausing. "Actually, I might be."
	"Let me get this straight," I tried again. "You don't know that Sister Chen has insomnia."
	"I don't know," he answered immediately.
	"You two share a room, though," Weiwei pointed out. "You haven't noticed at all?"
	Fei Ziyi glanced over to look at the room. "We do share a room. Come to think of it, I don't think I've seen her actually asleep recently."
	"Here's another question," I said seriously. "We know what Sister Chen thinks of you, but what do you think of Sister Chen?"
	Fei Ziyi looked up as if the answers were written on the ceiling. "I love her, of course."
	Chen Han's voice came from the doorway. "Are you sure it's me you love and not your liquor?"
	My head snapped over to watch the red heroine stride into the room, and I jumped to my feet. "Sister Chen!"
	Chen Han looked at us in amusement. "So this is where the two of you ran off to."
	Taking Chen Han by the sleeve, I tugged her toward the door. "Thank you for your time," I called over my shoulder at Fei Ziyi.
	"Sorry for bothering you," Weiwei added as she hurried after us.
	"Are we training today?" I asked as we made our way back downstairs to where Yuxin was waiting for us at the table.
	"The rain stopped," Chen Han observed. "I think we'll be able to go to the marketplace after all."
	I glanced back at the stairs. "Is Fei Ziyi coming along?"
	Chen Han just waved a hand. "I don't think so. If we hurry, we might be able to beat the rain."
	The marketplace was about an hour's walk from the residence, and the road we walked was empty. The surrounding world was painted in green and gray. A thick fog shrouded everything, and mud splashed beneath our shoes. Chen Han led the way while Weiwei, Yuxin, and I trailed behind her. The three of us chatted, and the journey itself, while damp and cold, was lively.
	By the time we arrived at the small town, it had begun to drizzle, and the sun showed no sign of emerging through the heavy blanket of clouds.
	"Quick!" Chen Han motioned for us to follow her into one of the shops. Warmth washed over me the moment we stepped over the threshold, and I absently reached up to brush strands of my damp hair out of my eyes. With the heat radiating from the back of the room and the weapons hanging on the walls, I quickly concluded we were in a blacksmith's shop.
	Chen Han smirked as she straightened her crimson robes. She strode over to the door at the back of the shop and knocked on it with the back of her hand. "Customers are here," she called as she leaned against the frame.
	"Chen Han?" a voice called from the other side of the wood. The heroine casually took a step back before the door swung open. A middle-aged man stood in the doorway, grinning through his thick beard.
	Chen Han looked up at him. "Greetings. I hope you've been well."
	"How many years has it been now since you've paid my shop a visit?" the blacksmith asked as he shut the door behind him. "It feels like forever."
	"It's only been a year," Chen Han said in amusement. "Tell me, Mr. Fan, is it me that you missed, or is it my money?"
	"You, of course!" Mr. Fan replied immediately. "You think too much about it. When have I ever asked you for money? Hero Wu was my most frequent customer, and after all the money he's spent here, of course I'll let his disciples shop for free. I've practically watched you grow up." Then he blinked as he looked around the shop. "Where's Ziyi?"
	"He didn't come today," Chen Han said. "I brought my students along with me instead."
	Mr. Fan looked at Weiwei, Yuxin, and me as if he was just noticing us for the first time. "Students?" Then his face split into a smile. After bowing to each of us in turn, Mr. Fan grinned at Chen Han. "Look at you, teaching students of your own now! I should introduce myself-I'm the blacksmith in this town. You can call me Mr. Fan."
	"Mr. Fan," we chorused.
	"I've come here today because I want to have swords made for them," Chen Han said as she glanced around the shop.
	Mr. Fan nodded enthusiastically. "No problem!"
	Chen Han turned to address the three of us. "Feel free to look around while I give Mr. Fan the details and work out the price."
	"Price?" Mr. Fan protested. "For you and your students, there isn't a price!"
	After a series of arguments, Chen Han ended up giving Mr. Fan money for half the cost. Mr. Fan disappeared into the backroom, and Chen Han asked us to follow her out of the shop. The rain was coming down hard now, so she opened an umbrella and handed it to Weiwei before opening a second one for herself.
	Yuxin and I huddled on either side of Weiwei as we continued through the small town. At the marketplace, Chen Han picked out meats and vegetables. As she lingered at a cabbage stand, I caught Yuxin's eye. "Look," I whispered under my breath. "There's a medicine shop!"
	"Sister Chen has probably already tried the medicine there," Yuxin responded in equal quiet. "What are you planning to do?"
	"I think we should check it out anyway." I clutched my stomach in what I hoped was a convincing representation of pain. "Ouch! I think I have a stomach ache! Good thing there's a medicine shop across the street!"
	Chen Han turned around to look at me in surprise. "Are you alright? I can take you there-"
	"No need!" I held up a hand. "Yuxin can come with me."
	After pushing my portion of vegetables into a very surprised Weiwei's arms, I took Yuxin by the hand and hurried her across the street. We splashed through the puddles of water, and by the time we stepped into the shop, my shoes were completely soaked through.
	"Hello," I said breathlessly as I walked up to the man behind the counter.
	"Hello." The man looked down at Yuxin and me, unsure what to make of us. "Do you ladies need anything?"
	"Do you have any medicine that helps with sleep?" I asked.
	"I have a couple of things like that," the man said thoughtfully. "Let me go get them for you."
	I watched him walk out from behind the counter and make his way over to a series of boxes on the wall. As he searched for the medicine, I walked around the shop and absently ran a hand over the lids of the boxes laid out on one of the tables.
	Suddenly, Yuxin grabbed my wrist. I looked at her in surprise, my hand hovering inches away from a small wooden box.
	The owner of the shop looked over and said, "I wouldn't touch that one."
	I stared at the box apprehensively. "What's in it?"
	"That's for people who have trouble staying awake," he said as he gingerly picked up the box and placed it on a shelf above my reach. "If you accidentally expose yourself to too much of it, you won't be able to sleep for days."
	"Oh," I said.
	The shop owner pulled down a different box from the shelf. "Here. If you mix the powder in with water or tea, it should help with sleep."
	"Thank you! How much is it?"
	The man stated the price, and I turned to Yuxin expectantly.
	She passed me a handful of coins. When we finished paying, we hurried out of the shop. "I'm telling you," Yuxin said once we were outside, "Sister Chen has probably tried this already."
	"But what if she hasn't tried this one?"
	When we returned to Chen Han and Weiwei, the rain had stopped again.
	"Does your stomach feel better?" Chen Han asked with raised brows.
	I nodded my head. "Much better."
	"In that case, we should head back."
	"What about the swords?" Yuxin questioned.
	"They'll be ready on a later date," Chen Han informed her. "Now that you've met Mr. Fan, if you ever need any weaponry, you can go to him."
	Before leaving town, Chen Han led us into the medicine shop. As she spoke to the man behind the counter, he kept casting looks at Yuxin and me. The two of us shuffled around awkwardly.
	Once the three of us left the shop, Weiwei turned to Chen Han. "What did you buy?"
	"Oh, this?" Chen Han said mildly as she opened the small box to show Weiwei the assortment of round pills inside. "Birth control. Fei Ziyi is not fit to be a father, and I have no intention of being a single mother."
	Weiwei quickly looked away.
	When we returned to the residence, the rain clouds had parted, and the sun was high in the sky. "The three of you should take a bath and change clothes," Chen Han told us after we finished stocking the pantry. "Catching a cold wouldn't be ideal."
	Grabbing Weiwei with one hand and Yuxin with the other, I hurried the two of them upstairs. Once we were in our room, I pulled out the small box I had bought from the medicine shop.
	"Look"-I showed the box to Weiwei-"according to the man at the shop, this is supposed to help with sleep."
	Weiwei took the box from me and lifted the lid to look at the powdered leaves inside. "What if Sister Chen's already tried it?"
	I took the box back from her. "That's what Yuxin said too. But I want to give it a try."
	"How much do we put in?"
	"Normally with these kinds of things, a spoonful is enough," Yuxin answered thoughtfully.
	"I'll try a spoonful on myself tonight to see if it works," I declared.
	Weiwei looked to me worriedly. "Are you sure?"
	I offered her a smile. "It should be fine. Anyway, who wants to take a bath first?"

~

	That night, I sat at the small table in our room. Weiwei and Yuxin leaned over my shoulder as they watched me measure out a spoonful of powder and dissolve it into a cup of hot water. After blowing away the steam wafting up from the surface, I took a sip of the mixture.
	Yuxin watched me drink another sip. "How quick do you think the effects are?"
	I frowned faintly. "I'm not sure." After finishing the entire cup, I sat there at the table waiting for something to happen. As we waited, the three of us decided to play a word game. The night outside was cloudy, and the rain had started again.
	Nearly two hours went by before I began to feel drowsy.
	"Is it working?" Weiwei asked quickly.
	"I can't tell if it's the medicine or if I'm just sleepy," I admitted.
	Yuxin sighed. "The effects don't seem harmful, at least."
	After going to bed, I awoke in the morning to Weiwei shaking my shoulders. I had slept through the entire night without waking up.
	Weiwei helped me sit up. "How do you feel?"
	I beamed. "I feel energized! Tonight I'll try and give the medicine to Sister Chen."
	The three of us went through an entire day of training with Chen Han. And to my surprise, I was the first to master the routine she showed us. Yuxin got it shortly after me, but Weiwei continued to struggle with the movements.
	"I just can't do it," she said as she collapsed onto the grass.
	I dropped to my knees beside her. "You can do it, Weiwei! Don't give up now!"
	"I can't," Weiwei said as she stared up at the sky high above.
	I dragged Weiwei to her feet. "Come on. Let's try the routine again."
	That night, we sat around the table with Chen Han. I had gone to the kitchen to prepare the food and drinks for the night. When I handed out the teacups, I placed the one with the sleeping powder in front of the heroine in red.
	I watched Chen Han pick up the cup. She noticed me watching her, and I quickly averted my gaze.
	By the time we finished dinner, all our cups were empty. We bid Chen Han goodnight before heading upstairs to get ready for bed. "Maybe tonight Sister Chen can get some good sleep," I said after Weiwei shut the door behind us.
	After Weiwei and Yuxin had fallen asleep, I was still awake. Against my better judgment, I pushed open the window and climbed outside. I tiptoed down the walkway but stopped when I noticed the fluttering red fabric of Chen Han's robes.
	"Sister Chen!" I exclaimed in a whisper.
	Chen Han turned to face me with a faint smile on her face. "You hoped you wouldn't be seeing me out here tonight, is that correct?"
	I nodded.
	"You put the sleeping powder in the tea," Chen Han said absently. "But I've already tried it before. My master used to buy it for me."
	I just stared at her. "You knew?"
	Chen Han offered me a smile. "I know you're only trying to look out for me."
	My shoulders slumped. "You've done so much for us. I just wanted to see if there was anything I could do to help you in return."
	Chen Han sighed and looked back out at the night. "There is something you can do, actually. Would you be willing to hear me talk for a short time?"
	I agreed, surprised.
	"It's about Ziyi." Chen Han absently ran a stand of her long hair between her fingers. "The two of us used to be together seriously-that is, until things got to the point where I decided to end it."
	"I still find it difficult to believe you and Fei Ziyi were a couple," I remarked. "You're such a good person-such a proud person. And Fei Ziyi . . . what did you see in him?"
	"He used to be charming. He was fearless and calculating, skilled in both the sword and brush. Our master displayed the poems Ziyi wrote all over his study. Then he passed away, and Ziyi hasn't written since. I used to think the two of us would be heroes, traveling the martial arts world together, bringing justice to the unjust. We admired each other. I was willing to give him my heart. I gave it to him, and even now he still hasn't returned it. He still says he loves me, but each time he says it, I find it harder to believe."
	"If he still loves you, why did you end the relationship?"
	Chen Han dropped her gaze. "In fights, whenever I call for his help, he never appears. I rush to his side whenever he says my name, but when I needed him the most, he was never there. This"-she rolled up her sleeve to show me a scar on her arm-"is just one of the many scars I got for thinking I could rely on him. It's his drinking addiction that's the problem. He told me he would work on it, but in reality, he isn't willing to. After I ended our relationship, I was selfish and saw other people in the hope that he would be jealous. He just said he'll only ever love me."
	"You won't give him another chance?"
	"I gave him chances. Again, and again, and again. All I got were scars. Do you really think he deserves another one?"
	I shook my head.
	"Maybe he still does love me," Chen Han continued as she gazed into the distance, "but he never loved me the same way I love him. Part of me wants to leave him far behind and never look back. But I can't bring myself to part with him, either."
      I opened my mouth to respond, but suddenly I sneezed.
	Chen Han turned to look at me. "Have you caught a cold? Or is someone talking about you behind your back?"
	I sniffed. "Now that you've said it, I do feel a little bit congested."
	"I shouldn't have let you run around in the rain like that yesterday. I've kept you out here long enough. Come on, let's get you to bed."
	I let her lead me back to my room. After tucking in my blankets the way I imagined any older sister would do, Chen Han rose to her feet and silently exited the room.
	In the morning, as my luck would have it, I awoke with a horrible fever. I hissed as my head throbbed painfully.
	Yuxin was lying next to me, her hair plastered to her face with sweat.
      Weiwei felt the heat radiating from our foreheads. "You're burning up!"
	"I'm sorry, Yuxin," I sniffled. "I shouldn't have had us run through the rain like that."
	Yuxin coughed. "Don't worry about it. This is just a small cold, that's all."
	That day, Chen Han canceled our training and spent the morning with Weiwei looking after Yuxin and me.
	"You shouldn't stay too close," I rasped. My throat felt like sandpaper. "I don't know if this cold is contagious."
	"I've seen this kind of cold before," Chen Han reassured me. "It isn't contagious, but it does take a couple of days to go away."
	I sighed heavily and stared up at the ceiling. I thought I'd be helping to take care of Chen Han this week, but in the end, she was the one looking after us.
	That night, my fever seemed to have worsened. Even though I knew colds like this only got worse before they got better, it didn't make lying there any easier. To monitor Yuxin and me, Chen Han announced that she'd stay in our room tonight.
	"What about Fei Ziyi?" I asked hoarsely.
	Chen Han just laughed. "He'll be fine without me."
	Yuxin scooted over to make room for Chen Han to lie down between us. And so the four of us lay there in the dark, listening to the rain pattering on the roof. I wasn't completely sure when I had fallen asleep, but I awoke in the middle of the night with a painful headache.
	"Sister Chen," I whispered as I tapped her arm. "Sister Chen?"
	I slowly sat up and blinked in surprise. Chen Han had fallen asleep.

    Chapter Thirteen

	I stared at Chen Han for a long moment before slowly laying back down. My headache was suddenly much more bearable than it had been seconds ago.
      When morning came around, I gently shook Weiwei awake and pointed at Chen Han. "What do you think?" I whispered.
	Weiwei stared in bewilderment. "Do you think her lack of sleep has something to do with Fei Ziyi?"
	"I don't know." But we didn't get to discuss it more because Chen Han was beginning to stir. Her eyes fluttered open as she squinted against the light flooding in through the window.
	"Sister Chen!" I quickly helped her up. "How are you feeling?"
	The heroine in red shook her head, stunned. "I feel rested. Did I really fall asleep here?"
	I nodded energetically. "You seemed to have slept through the night."
	Yuxin sat up and rubbed the sleep from her eyes. "Good morning."
	"How do the two of you feel?" Chen Han asked weakly.
	"Much better than yesterday," I said.
	"Me too," Yuxin agreed.
	Chen Han rose to her feet and straightened her crimson robes. "If you're feeling better, we can resume training again."
	After changing clothes, Weiwei, Yuxin, and I followed Chen Han downstairs for breakfast. To our surprise, Fei Ziyi was sitting at the table, and he looked up as we stepped into the room.
	"Fei Ziyi?" Yuxin blinked at him. "It's rare to see you here. Well, it's rare to see you at all."
	Fei Ziyi just turned to look at Chen Han. "Is there liquor?"
	Chen Han sighed and turned on her heel to fetch it.
	I exchanged a look with Weiwei. "Fei Ziyi," I said quietly after glancing over my shoulder to make sure Chen Han was out of earshot. "You want to help Sister Chen with her insomnia, right?"
	"Why wouldn't I?"
	"At night, you should hug her like this." I wrapped my arms tightly around Weiwei to demonstrate.
	Fei Ziyi stared at me before letting out an amused laugh. "What-?"
	I finally let go of Weiwei. "For Sister Chen's sake, just try it."
	Chen Han reentered the room and placed a jar on the table. "Liquor is here."
	Fei Ziyi reached for the jar, but before he could grab it, Chen Han scooted it of his reach. A slight frown tugged at her painted lips. "Can I convince you not to drink today?"
	Fei Ziyi's hands fell back to his side. "Come on," he said with an exasperated smile on his face. "It's rare that I'm even up this early normally."
	"Could you not drink today?" Chen Han repeated. "I want you to teach my class today."
	Fei Ziyi burst into laughter, then he stopped when he realized Chen Han was serious. "Me? Teach a class?"
	"We have students now. And we're going to teach them."
	Fei Ziyi waved her off. "You can teach them. I don't want to." He reached for the jar of liquor again, but Chen Han moved it for a second time. Fei Ziyi's lazy smile was now replaced with a frown. "Fine." With that said, he stood and left the room.
	"You really want Fei Ziyi to teach us?" Weiwei asked as Chen Han sat down in Fei Ziyi's vacated seat.
	The heroine in red poured herself a cup of liquor and swirled the clear liquid around. "There are a number of things that he can teach better than I can. I want all of you to get the most of your training. After you finish breakfast, head outside to meet him."
	The sky was a clear blue, without a single cloud to be seen. The air was crisp and cold, and the mountains and trees in the distance were shrouded in mist.
	I found myself shivering as I stood next to Weiwei and Yuxin. Fei Ziyi stood opposite us. "So," he said. "What have you been taught so far?"
	"We learned a few routines with the wooden swords," Yuxin informed him.
	"Let's see them, then."
	We spent the entire morning working on martial arts and swordsmanship. In the afternoon, our new teacher had us read and interpret a series of texts.
	Weiwei hopelessly stared down at the book in front of her. "I was never taught how to read anything this complex before."
	"It's alright," I said as I sat down next to her. "I can help you."
	"Hey," Fei Ziyi said, amused. "What about your own work? Whoever finishes first gets to rest, remember? The loser has to make dinner for all of us."
	I shook my head. "There is no winning and losing. I just want to help my friend." Turning back to Weiwei, I looked down at the book in front of her. "Where are you having the most trouble?"
	"Here, and here," Weiwei said in embarrassment.
	"Okay."
	Ultimately, Yuxin was the first to finish the assignment. While Yuxin stayed behind to talk to Fei Ziyi about the day's lessons, I accompanied Weiwei to the kitchen to help her prepare dinner.
	Weiwei let out a tired sigh as she rolled up her sleeves. "You didn't need to come here with me, you know. Where did you learn to read such advanced texts, anyway?" she asked as we began boiling water chopping vegetables. "Yuxin was likely taught in the brothel for the sake of indulging the customers, but you and I grew up at the palace."
      "I learned before I came to the palace," I said simply.
"You really are amazing."
"It's not like that, really. But I'm here to help you."
      Weiwei just smiled faintly as she shook her head. "I don't deserve a friend like you."
	I clung to Weiwei's arm. "Don't say that! We're here to look out for each other."
	That night, I sat next to the window in our shared bedroom. The night sky outside was clear, and the moon hung low in the inky canvas. Weiwei had gone to sleep early, and I looked up as Yuxin silently walked over to me. She took a seat and gazed out into the star-flecked night.
	I opened my mouth to say something, but upon seeing Yuxin's expression, I stopped. Sorrow lingered behind her eyes as she sat there in silence. Yuxin hadn't told me much about her past, and I hoped one day she could share it with me. I wanted to help her, but being in the dark, I didn't know how.

~

	In the morning, I sat at the table eating breakfast. To my surprise, Fei Ziyi was there too. But unlike the previous day, he was already intoxicated when I arrived.
	Weiwei turned to look at Chen Han. "Sister Chen, you look better than usual. Were you able to get some sleep?"
	"I did, actually," Chen Han said, unable to believe it herself. "I can't remember why or how, but I seemed to have slept through the night. When I woke in the morning, I didn't feel the same tiredness I usually do."
	Suddenly, Fei Ziyi started laughing, and everyone turned to look at him in surprise. "It's because Yanyan gave me a suggestion."
	"Who's Yanyan?" I said defensively. "Who said you can call me that? Who said I gave you a suggestion? I didn't!"
	Chen Han looked between the two of us suspiciously, but then she shrugged. "When the three of you are ready, we can go outside to continue our training."
	When our lunch break came around, I flopped over onto the grass. My hair was plastered to the sides of my head with sweat. Somewhere out of the corner of my vision, crimson fabric fluttered. The color was a stark contrast to the pale blue sky high above.
	Chen Han prodded me with the hilt of her sword. "Still alive?"
	"Barely," I said breathlessly.
	She laughed as she crouched down next to me. "So you're still looking out for my health."
	I slowly sat up to glance at Weiwei and Yuxin. "Was it that obvious? I wanted it to seem like it was completely Fei Ziyi's idea."
	Chen Han took sat on the grass across from us. She set her sword down and tipped her head back to look at the sky. "If I'm being honest, I think I know very well what's causing my lack of sleep. The story I told you about my life before I met my master . . . well, I might have left out a few details. Before my father kicked me out of the house, he thought that if he couldn't sell me as a person, he could still try and get some money by trying to sell my organs. One night I was fast asleep, and then the next thing I knew, he was trying to cut my stomach open with a rusty knife."
	I pressed over my mouth as I inhaled sharply.
	"What happened next?" Weiwei whispered.
	"I was scared. I fought back. I managed to wrestle the knife from my father and then ran. But I had nowhere to go. I couldn't find food on the streets, so a few days later, the only place I could return to was the house. I was dying; my wounds were infected, and I was losing blood. But my father threw me out and told me never to come back. All I had was that rusty knife and the clothes on my back. That's when my master found me. He saved me."
	"The trauma still follows you to this day," I said sadly. "No wonder none of the medicines worked."
	"But then that one time you slept in our room," Weiwei started slowly. "You felt . . . safe."
	The heroine in red inclined her head.
	"Thank you for telling us about your past," I said quietly. "No one should have had to experience that."
	Chen Han let out a sigh. "The saddest part is that I don't think I was the only one. That happens to be the way things are. And that is why the world needs heroes with kind hearts-heroes who will help others without a second thought. Heroes like my master."
	"I wish I could have had the chance to meet Hero Wu," Weiwei said softly.
	Chen Han rose to her feet and brushed the dirt from her flowing robes. "How about I arrange a trip for us to pay him a visit? It's been a few months since we last paid respects to him. I think my master would have liked the three of you here," she said wistfully. "He always enjoyed a lively environment."

~

	The rest of the week flew by, and before long, the five of us were walking down the dirt paths snaking across the land to visit Wu Ren's tombstone. This time, when we climbed the foggy hill, Weiwei, Yuxin, and I stood together at the summit. We bowed respectfully before moving away to give Chen Han and Fei Ziyi some privacy to speak to their master.
	As we waited off to the side, Weiwei suddenly grabbed my arm. I blinked at her as she pointed to a patch of bamboo. "I think I just saw movement."
	"A wild animal?" I suggested as I strained my eyes against the fog.
	Weiwei continued to stare at the bamboo. "I don't know. It moved away too quickly."
	Chen Han returned with Fei Ziyi was close at her heels. "Ready to make the trip to the village?" 
	"Sister Chen," Weiwei said quietly. "I think I saw something moving in the bamboo."
	Fei Ziyi walked past her and disappeared into the bamboo. "There are footprints here," he called a moment later. We hurried over to him, and Fei Ziyi motioned to the dirt and the fresh footprints.
	"Do you think someone wanted to pay Hero Wu a visit?" I asked uncertainly.
	"Do you think someone is following us?" Yuxin asked at the same time.
	Chen Han poked at the footprints with her sheathed sword. "It's true that I get a lot of people coming to me, but I don't think they've ever fled like this before."
	"Maybe it's just a coincidence that someone else showed up at the same time as us," Weiwei suggested.
	"Let's not worry about this now," Chen Han said as she shook her hair back. A smile tugged on her red-painted lips. "If this person turns out to be unpleasant, I'll deal with them."
	During the first day of walking back from the tomb, I found myself checking our surroundings for anything out of the ordinary, but nothing seemed amiss. By the second day, all my worries had slipped away, and I was chatting happily with my companions again.
	We stopped at a hotel for the night, and I was undoing my hair when I noticed a flash of motion outside the window. After freezing for a split second, I hurried over and peered outside. My unbound hair whipped around my face as I squinted against the night wind. The lanterns in the street illuminated the buildings, but the street was completely empty.
	I frowned to myself as I slowly leaned back inside.
	"Everything alright?" Yuxin asked as she came over to me.
	I shook my head in bewilderment as I closed the window and shut out the night. "I thought I saw something moving very quickly outside. But now I don't see anything at all."
	"Should we go to Sister Chen and Fei Ziyi's room to tell them about it?"
	"I'm really not sure what I saw," I admitted. "Let's not bother them with it."
	The following morning, the three of us found Chen Han and Fei Ziyi outside the hotel. The heroine in red had a smirk on her face as usual, but something about Fei Ziyi seemed off. Even though he was smiling lazily, his posture was stiff.
	"Is everything alright?" I asked worriedly.
	Chen Han ignored my question. "We should get a move on. It looks like it's going to rain again later, and we should try and get as far as we can before it does. We've got swords to pick up."
	This time, Weiwei, Yuxin, and I continuously looked over our shoulders as we walked. Even though Chen Han and Fei Ziyi weren't admitting it, I could tell they were more alert than usual. What was even more telling was that, for the entire trek to the next town, I hadn't seen Fei Ziyi drink from his gourd of liquor once.
	"I think Sister Chen and Fei Ziyi are being followed," Weiwei said quietly to Yuxin and me. "They just don't want to alarm us."
	When we finally arrived at Mr. Fan's blacksmith shop, my anxiety was beginning to melt away again. For the past few days of travel, there had been no signs of anyone following us, and I was starting to think that maybe we had lost them, or maybe no one had been following us after all.
	"Chen Han!" Mr. Fan exclaimed delightedly as we strode into the shop. "And Ziyi is here too!"
	Fei Ziyi flashed the blacksmith a carefree smile. "Greetings, Mr. Fan."
	The blacksmith let out a rumbling laugh. "It's been how many years since I've seen you last? The last time I saw you, you were still shorter than me. Anyways, I've finished the swords." After walking back behind his counter, Mr. Fan placed three identical swords on the surface. "What do ya think?"
	Weiwei, Yuxin, and I turned to look at Chen Han. The heroine just smiled and nodded. I hurried over to inspect the swords with Weiwei and Yuxin. I stared in awe at the blades glinting in the light.
	"I've got the sheaths here too," Mr. Fan said, placing them on the counter as well. "It's always a pleasure helping out."
	"Are you sure you won't let me pay you the rest for your work?" Chen Han asked. A wry smile played on her lips. "I fear you'll be unable to keep your business going if you keep doing work for free."
	Mr. Fan waved her off. "Nonsense."
	Chen Han turned to Weiwei, Yuxin, and me. "So, what do you think?"
	I just shook my head as I stared at the swords. "I don't know what to think. They look powerful. Deadly."
	Chen Han put a reassuring hand on my shoulder. "Think of them as tools to help you uphold justice."
	Mr. Fan placed all the swords in their sheaths before handing them to us. "Now, whenever I call on you for help, you have to come and help me, yes?"
	Yuxin smiled as she took her sword from him. "Of course."
	When we left the shop, Weiwei, Yuxin, and I strapped our swords to our backs. "I feel like I'm one of those heroes in the stories," I said in awe.
	There was a newfound confidence in Yuxin's step as we walked. The fog surrounding us had thickened since we entered one of the many bamboo forests on the path back to Chen Han and Fei Ziyi's residence. "Bunny, do you think it's difficult to defeat demons?" she asked.
	"It can't be that difficult, can it?" I said mildly. "I'm sure Sister Chen could take down a demon."
      Weiwei joined our conversation. "I've heard you call Xiyan 'Bunny' before," she said softly. "I'm curious where that came from."
	I watched Yuxin's face as she gazed at the sky. "I used to have a pet bunny. The bunny died one day, though, and it was shortly before Xiyan arrived at the village. So I decided to call her Bunny after my late friend."
	"Is that really what happened?" I asked quietly.
	Yuxin nodded as she turned to face me. "When I was younger, believe it or not, I actually used to think that my pet bunny magically turned into you. It's silly, isn't it?"
	We walked for the rest of the day, and when Chen Han and Fei Ziyi's residence came into view, the sun was slowly creeping toward the horizon. As we drew closer, Chen Han came to a stop and held out an arm to halt the rest of us. A man was standing in front of the doors.
	Fei Ziyi swore under his breath. "Looks like we were beaten back."
	I looked at Chen Han and Fei Ziyi in confusion. "Do you know this person?"
	"No," Fei Ziyi said simply. "But I do know he's definitely trouble."
    

    Chapter Fourteen

	"What do we do, then?" Weiwei asked worriedly. "Do we go in through the back entrance?"
	Chen Han shook her head. "There's no point now. Look, he's already seen us. He came all the way to our home. We might as well go and talk to him."
	"Once we started on our way back from our master's grave," Fei Ziyi spoke up, "someone kept slipping me notes. They all said the same thing: 'Meet me outside, alone.' But why must I meet this person outside alone? For them to kill me? I thought if I ignored them they'd go away. I didn't expect them to turn up here."
	Chen Han set off down the path. "Let's go ask him what he wants."
	The five of us stopped in front of the entrance, and the young man, who had been examining the stones in the wall, nonchalantly turned to address us. "Greetings," he said formally. He was dressed in the simple robes of a student, and his dark hair was neatly tied up. He looked directly at Fei Ziyi. "I've been looking for you."
      Fei Ziyi just burst into laughter, then frowned. "Who are you? If you're here to pick a fight, you're outnumbered."
	The man shook his head. "I'm not here to fight. It's been years since we've met, so it is only natural that you don't remember me. I'm your cousin. I've been searching for you, Gao Dujiang."
	Fei Ziyi stared at the man blankly. "I think you're mistaken. There's no Gao Dujiang here."
	"But there is, isn't there?" the man said mildly. "He's you, isn't he?"
	"My name's Fei Ziyi."
	The man let out a sigh. "Let me try this again. My name's Gao Yunzhe. I'm your cousin. Ever since the Gao family was killed for committing treason, I've been looking for any other survivors."
	"Let's pretend that I am Gao Dujiang," Fei Ziyi said. His tone was laced with amusement. "If you are part of the Gao family, how did you survive?"
	"My father had sent me away for school," Gao Yunzhe explained. "When the news reached the school that the Gao family had committed treason and was to be exterminated, my teachers took it upon themselves to give me a new identity and erase all traces of my old existence from their records. I was only eleven at the time, and my teachers were benevolent."
	Fei Ziyi was frowning now. "I didn't know there were any other survivors."
	"So you admit it." A wry smile flickered across Gao Yunzhe's face. "You can't hide it, especially when you resemble your late older siblings."
	"The notes . . ." Fei Ziyi said slowly. "Those were yours, too, I assume. But how did you find me?"
	Gao Yunzhe inclined his head. "I found you by hearing about your late master. Recently, old information on martial artists resurfaced. Have you heard about what is happening in the capital? One of the princes died, and now months later, a pirate was just found to be involved with his death."
	I stared at Gao Yunzhe. "A pirate? In the palace?"
      Gao Yunzhe nodded. "The pirate is skilled in martial arts and fought his way out of the palace. Now the entire capital is under lockdown and in the midst of an investigation. I volunteered to help search through archives to try and uncover the pirate's identity. With all this access to resources about the martial arts world, my investigation led me to discover that the martial artist Wu Ren was spotted with a child on the day of our family's massacre. I learned of the whereabouts of Hero Wu's residence and also learned that he had passed away. It turned out he had two students, so of course, I had to investigate myself. When I found this place, I saw all of you leaving and decided to follow you secretly until I knew for sure that you were Gao Dujiang. Then I tried to pass notes to you so that we could meet face to face. You ignored me, though."
	Fei Ziyi raised his brows. "You never signed the notes. They sounded quite threatening to me."
	Gao Yunzhe dipped his head again. "My sincere apologies."
	After a silence fell between them, Chen Han asked, "Would you like to come in? Now that we know you're related to my junior, it would be inhospitable of us not to invite you inside for some tea." After pushing the doors to the yard open, Chen Han stepped to the side and gestured graciously for Gao Yunzhe to enter. "Please."
	Gao Yunzhe stepped over the threshold and into the yard beyond. The rest of us followed him, and Chen Han shut the door behind us. The heroine in red strode to the front of the group and led the way to the building at the back of the yard.
      In a matter of minutes, Chen Han, Fei Ziyi, and Gao Yunzhe were seated at the table. All of them had steaming cups in front of them, all untouched. Weiwei, Yuxin, and I stood off to the side of the room, quietly observing the scene.
	Chen Han had a wide smile on her face as she rested her chin on the palms of her hands. "So, tell me, Gao Yunzhe. You walked into the martial arts world to try and find your cousin?"
	Gao Yunzhe nodded. "That's correct."
	Fei Ziyi was looking at Gao Yunzhe, frowning. "You found me. What do you plan to do now? I'm sure you already investigated what happened leading up to the massacre. My parents weren't exactly innocent, and I'm afraid your father was complicit as well."
	"I want the two of us to bring glory back to our family name," Gao Yunzhe said seriously. "I've been studying hard ever since I could hold a brush. In a few years, I'll be prepared enough to take the imperial examination. I want to join the court."
	Fei Ziyi gave him an amused look. "Our family is already regarded as scum in Jingcheng. Becoming a minister of the court is one thing, but bringing glory back to our family name? Bring what glory back? It's not worth it."
	"The two of us are not at fault," Gao Yunzhe said as if he hadn't heard Fei Ziyi's response. "Our fates shouldn't have to be determined by what happened back then."
	"They haven't. I'm here now, aren't I? And so are you."
	A crease formed between Gao Yunzhe's brows. "That's not what I mean. You've really never thought about changing the reputation of our family name?"
	"What use is that?" Fei Ziyi asked bluntly. "I'm no longer part of the Gao family. I'm Fei Ziyi now. I'm a martial artist, and no one can make me give that up. Cousin, forget about the Gao family."
	Gao Yunzhe fell silent and reached for his cup of tea. "Will you really not consider it?" he finally asked. "Generations of our Gao family will be referred to with disdain. Why are we condemned to perpetually shoulder our parents' sins?"
	Fei Ziyi gave him another look. "Do you have to ask? You're clearly an educated man. Surely you know that's just the way things are."
	Chen Han turned to Fei Ziyi. "Will you really not consider helping him out?"
	Fei Ziyi looked almost offended by the question. "I'm not going anywhere."
	Chen Han turned back to address Gao Yunzhe. "You're welcome to stay here for as long as you want, but Ziyi doesn't want to help you."
	Gao Yunzhe inclined his head. "Then I'll thank you in advance for your hospitality. It was a long journey-the farthest I've ever traveled on my own. I'll stay for a few days. Who knows? Maybe I'll be able to convince Gao Dujiang to come with me."
	"I've already told you that there's no Gao Dujiang here," Fei Ziyi interjected, rising from his seat. "I don't want to keep talking about this."After turning on his heel, he climbed the stairs and vanished onto the second landing.
	"You heard him," Chen Han said lightly as she glanced over at Gao Yunzhe. "He doesn't want to keep discussing this topic. You can stay, but you can't bring up the Gao family again."
	Gao Yunzhe let out a sigh. "Fine." Then he turned to Weiwei, Yuxin, and me. "I don't think we've been formally introduced yet. I'm Gao Yunzhe. But if we're ever out in public, you can call me Ma Zhe. That's what my fellow classmates know me as."
	I lifted my arms in front of me and clasped my hands together to bow respectfully. "I'm Xia Xiyan."
	"Xia Yuxin."
	"Hu Qiuwei."
	Gao Yunzhe turned back to Chen Han. "I'm afraid I don't know your name either."
	The heroine in red smiled. "Chen Han. These three are my students."
	"Students?"
	Chen Han shook back her long hair. "That's right."
	"If you don't mind my asking, what's your relation to Du-Ziyi, I mean."
	"I'm his senior," Chen Han said simply. "We grew up under the same master and learned martial arts together."
	Gao Yunzhe smiled faintly. "I see."
	Chen Han looked over at us. "The three of you can head upstairs and get some rest. I'll keep Gao Yunzhe company here."
	We bowed again before hurrying up the stairs. When we reached our room, I tugged my hair out of its high ponytail.
	"What do you think of Gao Yunzhe's sudden appearance?" Weiwei asked after we shut the door behind us.
	"Fei Ziyi doesn't seem to like him very much," Yuxin commented.
	I nodded in agreement. "If I were him, I'd probably react the same way. After all, Fei Ziyi has been living his life as a martial artist for years now. Gao Yunzhe, on the other hand, is older. He has stronger recollections of the Gao family."
	"Gao Yunzhe might stay here a few days at most," Yuxin said, lost in thought. "I wonder if he'll be willing to spend some time with us while we're here."
	I instantly danced over to tug on Yuxin's arm. "Has someone taken a fancy to him?"
	Yuxin looked away. "He's a scholar from the capital. He's well spoken, and I can tell he's a good person. I-I just want to try and get to know him if I have the chance."
	"We only just met him, and you can already tell what kind of person he is?"
	She offered me a small smile. "My intuition is pretty accurate, given that I've dealt with a lot of people over the years. I can tell which men have ill intentions, and Gao Yunzhe isn't one of them."
	I was silent for a moment before I decided to change the topic. "On a different note, we've got real swords to practice with now. Sister Chen better make sure we don't end up seriously injuring ourselves with them."

~

	The following morning, the three of us were outside in the yard. As usual, Chen Han was instructing us, but today I noticed my attention was not fully on the lesson. Gao Yunzhe was standing off to the side, observing us. When he caught me looking, he politely dipped his head in my direction. I smiled awkwardly. After spending so much time with Chen Han and Fei Ziyi, I had gotten used to their carefree mannerisms, and something about Gao Yunzhe's stiff and formal conduct was a little daunting.
	I looked away, and my gaze drifted to the wooden building at the back of the yard. To my surprise, I noticed Fei Ziyi on the walkway of the second floor, arms folded, watching his cousin.
	When it was time to break for lunch, I asked Yuxin to follow me, and the two of us walked up the stairs to the second landing. Fei Ziyi was still standing there, looking out over the yard. "Hello, Yanyan," he said without turning around.
	I placed a hand on my hip. "I've already told you that you can't call me that."
	"And don't even think about giving me a nickname," Yuxin warned.
	Fei Ziyi finally turned to look at the two of us. "Do the two of you need something?"
	Yuxin ignored him. "You're suspicious of Gao Yunzhe."
	"I am," Fei Ziyi said simply. He opened his paper fan to fan himself. "I've been watching him all morning, and from what I can see, it seems like he was telling the truth when he said he doesn't have any martial arts experience."
	"I don't think there's any good reason to be suspicious of him," Yuxin pointed out. "I understand that you don't want anything to do with the Gao family, but Gao Yunzhe already stated what he wanted, and he's not going to force you to leave with him."
	Fei Ziyi's expression was somewhere between a forced smile and a grimace. "The sooner he leaves, the better."
	But the longer Gao Yunzhe stuck around us, the more we seemed to accept his presence-well, everyone except Fei Ziyi. One afternoon, I was sitting across from Gao Yunzhe, eagerly watching him as he read through the poem I had just finished.
      "What do you think?" I asked as I rocked back and forth in my seat.
	Weiwei was sitting next to me. "Patience. You just handed it to him."
	Gao Yunzhe smiled faintly as he set the poem down on the table between us. "It's clever. I like it."
	There was a flurry of red fabric as Chen Han strolled into the room with a tray of tea, which she set on the table. "May I see the poem?"
	I nodded my head, and Gao Yunzhe handed the poem to the heroine in red. Chen Han scanned it before letting out a laugh. "It's childish. Gao Yunzhe is just too nice to say so."
	"Sister Chen"-I pouted as I tugged on her sleeve-"don't laugh at me! I worked really hard on it."
	Gao Yunzhe looked up at Chen Han. "Are you interested in poetry too?"
	Chen Han waved him off. "Oh, no. My master made Ziyi and me study poems, but I was always scolded for being lazy in whatever I wrote. Ziyi is the one with talent for it."
	"Would you like to join us?" Gao Yunzhe asked. "I know a number of poems about the martial arts world."
	Chen Han flashed him a lazy smile. "I'll have to pass. I came to let all of you know that I'll be heading out tonight. I'll be back before noon tomorrow." The heroine in red smiled one last time before disappearing out the door.
	Yuxin, who had been writing something, set her brush down and turned her paper around for Gao Yunzhe to see. "I finished my poem."
	Gao Yunzhe smiled faintly as his eyes moved over the page. "It's a good poem."
	Yuxin dropped her gaze to her hands, but she was smiling.
	I exchanged a knowing glance with Weiwei, and the two of us rose to our feet. I let out a big yawn. "Look, it's already dark. I'm feeling a little tired. Weiwei and I will head to bed first." Gao Yunzhe barely had time to open his mouth before Weiwei and I were shuffling out of the room.
	I giggled as I pulled open the doors to our shared room. "Yuxin can thank the two of us later." I got to work lighting the candles, and the dark room slowly began to glow from their fiery light. "I like having Gao Yunzhe around," I commented. "Yuxin likes having him around, so I like having him around too."
	About half an hour later, the door to our room opened, and Yuxin slipped in.
	I jumped to my feet. "How did it go?"
	She was practically glowing. "We talked about poetry. And then I mentioned how I know how to dance and play the lute. Gao Yunzhe knows how to play the bamboo flute. He said one day maybe the two of us would have the chance to play a song together." There was a smile on Yuxin's face as she danced freely around the room. Her black hair flowed around her, and I realized I hadn't seen her this happy before.
	When she came to a stop, I latched onto her arm. "Yuxin, my good sister. Will you ever perform a dance for Weiwei and me?"
	Yuxin laughed as she playfully poked me on the forehead. "One of these days, when we can find music."
	The three of us spent some time quietly chatting before we finally changed into our nightclothes, extinguished the candles, and crawled under our covers.

~

	I sat resting my elbows on the table and my chin on my hands. I was sitting next to Gao Yunzhe in the study, watching the perfect characters that bloomed to life on the paper beneath his brush. I tried and failed to stifle my yawn.
	Gao Yunzhe paused to look at me. "Losing interest already?"
	I flashed him a guilty smile. "Sister Chen wanted me to watch and learn from your study habits." I glanced apprehensively at the book Gao Yunzhe had been poring over for the past hour. "What is this? I don't understand any of it. I don't think I'm cut out for studying for the imperial exam."
	Gao Yunzhe smiled faintly. "You wouldn't want to enter the palace if you had the chance?"
	I rapidly shook my head.
	"Let's learn something practical, then," he said. He placed his brush down and set aside the book he was transcribing. He laid out a blank piece of paper, then carefully held his long sleeves away from the table with one hand and picked up his brush again with the other. "Xia Xiyan. Which Xia? Which Xi? Which Yan?"
	"Xia as in summer, Xi as in sunset, Yan as in smoke." I sat up straight as I watched Gao Yunzhe write my name in neat print. "Your handwriting is amazing! My own writing isn't too bad, but it's nothing compared to yours."
	"Here." He passed me the brush once he was done. "You can use this as a reference. Try to copy the characters."
	I nodded eagerly as I took the brush. As I began to copy my name, Gao Yunzhe picked up a second brush and went back to studying. I had only copied my name once before the door to the study opened and Yuxin stepped in.
      I craned my neck to look behind her. "Where's Weiwei?"
	"Weiwei is still practicing with Sister Chen," Yuxin informed me as she sat across from us at the table. "She's having difficulty keeping up." Yuxin looked down at the paper I had been practicing on. "What's this?"
	"Brother Gao is having me practice writing my name."
	Yuxin smiled faintly at Gao Yunzhe. "If it isn't too much trouble, could you write my name for me to copy as well?"
	Gao Yunzhe dipped his head in a nod as he set his book down for a second time. Yuxin gracefully rose to her feet to take a seat to Gao Yunzhe's left. He handed her the paper, and she looked down at the page. "Beautiful penmanship."
      I handed Yuxin the brush I was using and watched her skillfully copy her name.
	"Your own writing is very good," Gao Yunzhe praised her.
	Yuxin blushed.

~

	The following morning, Weiwei and I found Gao Yunzhe standing next to the balcony railing with a book in one hand and a brush in the other. I followed his gaze to the yard below, where Chen Han was practicing with her sword alone. Smiling, I exchanged glances with Weiwei. I put a finger to my lips and motioned for her to follow me. The two of us tiptoed over to peer over Gao Yunzhe's shoulder. I let out a giggle. Gao Yunzhe wasn't studying now; instead, he was drawing a woman in flowing robes. Even though the picture was in black and white, I recognized Chen Han's form immediately.
	"I didn't know Brother Gao was skilled in painting too!" I said, impressed.
	Gao Yunzhe smiled softly. "If you're interested, I could show you sometime. If your teacher lets me, of course."
	In the afternoon, Weiwei, Yuxin, and I hurried from vendor to vendor, excitedly looking at all the goods they had to offer. Even though Chen Han had given us a few coins to buy what we wanted, by the time we had gone to the end of the main street and back, the three of us had only bought a few steamed buns to split among ourselves. Now whenever the three of us went out, we carried our swords with us the same way Chen Han and Fei Ziyi always did.
	We were just finishing up our snack when a commotion caught our eye. A carriage was blocking the road, and a crowd of confused villagers had gathered around it. I exchanged a glance with Weiwei and Yuxin before the three of us went over to join them. We pushed our way to the front of the crowd.
	A woman in a deep purple dress was pointing her fan at a young boy. From the jeweled pins that adorned her hair and the intricate embroidery on her dress, she had to be of high status. "Where are your parents?" she snapped shrilly. "Look how you ruined my dress!"
	"Milady," the woman's maids tried to calm her, "we have more clothes in the carriage. Please get back in so we can continue on our way."
	A boy was crying on the road in front of the carriage. "I'm sorry! I didn't mean it!"
	The woman raised a hand in the air to hit the boy. I started to move, but Yuxin beat me to it. Yuxin ran between the noble woman and the boy, shielding him with her body.
	The woman blinked at Yuxin as she lowered her hand. "Who are you? Are you the mother of this vicious child?"
	"What happened?" Yuxin asked as the boy clung to her.
	"He spooked the horses," she said angrily. "The carriage jolted, and now my skirt is ruined!" The woman gestured with her fan to the tear that ran up the side of her dress. "It got caught on the seat. I liked this dress too. Now I can only throw it away."
	"I'll buy it from you," Yuxin said quickly.
	The woman blinked in surprise as Yuxin fumbled for her coin pouch and held it out to her. "This is all I have."
	The woman slowly took the pouch from Yuxin and weighed it in her hand. "Fine. I'll let you and that vicious child off. You can have the dress."
	Soon, the deep purple fabric was folded neatly in Yuxin's arms. We watched the carriage drive off, and once it was gone, I turned to Yuxin, bewildered. "Why did you want her torn dress?"
	Yuxin ran a hand over the fabric, smiling faintly. "I can fix it. If I get the chance, I want to dress up for Brother Gao."

~

	We spent the evening prepping dinner, and soon all of us were seated around the table. All of us except for Fei Ziyi.
	Gao Yunzhe let out a sigh. "After spending time with all of you, I can see why my cousin doesn't want to leave. It was wrong for me to think he'd abandon his new life just like that."
	"So you've decided to stop trying to convince me to leave with you?" All of us turned to find Fei Ziyi standing on the stairs.
	Gao Yunzhe inclined his head. "I apologize for my selfishness. I'm just glad I got the chance to meet you here."
	To my surprise, Fei Ziyi let out a laugh as he made his way down the rest of the stairs. "That's more like it!"
	Gao Yunzhe blinked in surprise as Fei Ziyi clapped him on the back. "You aren't trying to avoid me anymore?"
	Fei Ziyi waved him off. "We're cousins-and the only family each other has left."
	Gao Yunzhe nodded. "In that case, I'll call my journey here a success. Reuniting with my cousin made it more than worthwhile. Now that we're all here, I think it's a good time to tell you that I'll be taking my leave soon. I've been here much longer than I anticipated."
	I watched Yuxin out of the corner of my eye. Everything was written on her face.

~

	That night, Weiwei and I were talking quietly when the door to our room opened and Yuxin entered. The moment she closed the door behind her, she sank to her knees, burying her face in her hands.
	"Yuxin!" I was crouching at Yuxin's side in an instant. "What happened?"
	Yuxin just shook her head as she finally lowered her hands, her eyes glistening with tears. "Brother Gao doesn't like me."
	"What?" I blinked at her. "I thought the two of you were getting along fine!"
	"We were," Yuxin said as she slumped down, hugging her knees as she stared unseeingly into space. "But he doesn't like me in the same way I like him. He's leaving soon, so I asked him if he'd be willing to stay a little longer. I told him that I liked him, but . . ." she just let out a sad laugh. "He just told me that he couldn't reciprocate my feelings and that I'll find someone better than him in the future. I know I'm not good enough for him. I just wish he could give me a chance."
	"I know it hurts to be rejected," Weiwei said softly, "but we've only known him for a couple of weeks. Maybe it was love at first sight for you, but you can't control Brother Gao's heart."
	Silent tears ran down Yuxin's face as she just hugged herself tighter.
	I wrapped my arms around her comfortingly. "Brother Gao was right about one thing: I'm certain you'll find someone better than him in the future."
	Yuxin shook her head hopelessly.
	"Yuxin-" I tugged at Yuxin's sleeve. She offered me a sad smile as she reached up to brush her tears away.
      Just then, a piece of paper fell from one of my pockets. I hastily reached to pick it up.
      "What's that?" Yuxin asked.
      I quickly took the opportunity to try and lighten the mood. "It's a secret."
      Yuxin just gave me a look before rising to her feet. I was quickly there to help her. "The two of you can go to sleep first. I want some time alone."
	Weiwei and I watched Yuxin pull open the door and step back into the night.
	"What is that?" Weiwei questioned softly once Yuxin had vanished.
	I unfolded the piece of paper and handed it to Weiwei. "All three of our names are written on it. Brother Gao instructed me to write from my heart, so I wrote the first thing that came to mind. The three of us are on this side, and then . . ." Weiwei flipped it over and read the other side. We were quiet for a moment before Weiwei handed the paper back to me. I stared down at the lone name printed onto the paper. Shen Fanghuan. "Do you think it was wrong of me to tell Yuxin this paper was a secret? In her state of mind, she might have thought Brother Gao gave it to me and it made her even more sad."
	Weiwei was silent for a moment before answering. "Maybe Yuxin didn't make anything of it at all. We should sleep now. You can bring it up with her tomorrow night."

~

      The next day, Weiwei and I were practicing with Chen Han in the yard when suddenly there was the sound of something shattering from inside. The three of us rushed to the source of the sound and found Yuxin and Gao Yunzhe facing each other from across the room.
	"You-" Yuxin was looking at Gao Yunzhe in a pained sort of way.
	"Miss Xia," Gao Yunzhe said stiffly. "You're a lady, and as a lady, I hope you can restrain your actions."
	"I-" Yuxin made to take a step forward, but Chen Han casually stepped between Yuxin and Gao Yunzhe.
	"Let's not make our guests uncomfortable," Chen Han said as she gave Yuxin a look. "How about you start prepping for lunch?"
	Yuxin's eyes filled with tears before she turned on her heel and vanished from sight.
	When night fell, Weiwei and I waited for Yuxin, but we went to bed when we concluded she wasn't coming.
      I wasn't sure when I awoke, but it was still dark outside. Weiwei was still fast asleep, but Yuxin was still missing.
	After carefully climbing out from under my blankets, I decided to go look for her. The morning hours were silent as I walked along the second-story walkway. It didn't take me long to find Yuxin leaning against the wooden railings. She was gazing out at the sky, and her inky hair fluttered gently around her in the soft breeze.
	"Yuxin," I said quietly as I walked over to her.
	Yuxin turned to look at me. If she was surprised by my presence, she didn't show it.
	"Are you okay?"
	She offered me a pained smile. "I've embarrassed myself. I'm embarrassed. I want to apologize, but I have no face left to see him now."
      "Yuxin," I said softly, placing a hand on hers, "what happened today?"
      Yuxin took a breath as she blinked back the tears glistening in her eyes. "I brought tea from the kitchens. When I poured him a cup, I touched his hand. It scared him away. I-I think I might have given myself away. He must think I'm dirty."
      "I don't think he sees you as dirty." When she refused to meet my gaze, I wrapped my arms around her in a warm hug. "I think Brother Gao just likes bold and fearless women like Sister Chen. This has nothing to do with your past."
      Yuxin held me tightly. "Xiyan, I'm really not pure. When I first entered the brothel, the owner, Madam Qin, knew I was frightened and stubborn. But she knew that was what the customers wanted. My first time, Madam Qin had them bid on me. And so my innocence was bought with a handful of coins. I never even got to see the money."
	I took Yuxin's hands in my own as a tear slid down the side of my face. "You've left that place, and you never have to go back."
	Yuxin's grip tightened around my hands. "I was constantly beaten by Madam Qin and beaten by the customers. I was always bruised and barely alive."
	I squeezed Yuxin's hands as I shook my head. "The past is in the past now. You can live for yourself now-your fate is yours to decide."
	Yuxin gazed out at the stars slowly fading into the brightening sky. "I just never want to live the way I did back in the village or the brothel again."
	I smiled as I wrapped my arms around her again. "The future is full of possibilities. I'm afraid Brother Gao will be leaving here with a heartache too. He isn't exactly a good match for Sister Chen, and his own feelings won't be reciprocated. Sister Chen isn't even interested in him!"
	Yuxin let out a weak laugh. "Maybe it's a good thing that he's leaving soon. Once he's gone, I'll slowly force myself to get over him. Thank you, Xiyan. Thank you for being my good sister."

~

	During the rest of Gao Yunzhe's stay, when we were not practicing with our swords, Yuxin kept to our room. She sat quietly by the window with a needle and thread, mending the purple dress. It hurt me to see her this way. As I watched her, she hummed softly, smiling to herself as she finished another line of stitches.
      One night, Weiwei and I were sitting with her when the sound of raised voices came from the walkway outside.
	"He wrote this for you?" Fei Ziyi's voice said angrily.
	"Yes," Chen Han's voice answered. "Is there a problem with that?"
	"I haven't even written a poem for you yet, and you accepted his?"
	Exchanging a glance with Weiwei and Yuxin, I tiptoed over to the door and opened it a crack to watch the scene outside.
	Chen Han and Fei Ziyi were standing on the walkway. Fei Ziyi had a sheet of paper in his hand that he was brandishing at Chen Han. The heroine in red had an exasperated look on her face as she held out her hand for the paper. "I already told him that I'm not interested in him," she said with a sigh. "He knows that and wanted to give it to me anyway as a friend."
	Fei Ziyi scoffed. "As a friend? I don't buy it."
	"Hey-!" Chen Han exclaimed as Fei Ziyi tore up the poem. Then she sighed, tapping her foot impatiently. "Why are you being like this?"
	"I haven't even written a poem for you yet," Fei Ziyi repeated.
	Chen Han just gave him a look before she turned on her heel. "You had plenty of chances to in the past."
	Fei Ziyi watched her stride away before turning and storming in the opposite direction.
