	Weiwei and Yuxin had joined me at the door by now, and the moment Fei Ziyi disappeared, to my surprise, Yuxin threw the door open and dashed outside. She dropped to her knees, frantically collecting the torn pieces of paper. I hurried over to join her.
	"Yuxin?" I asked softly once we were back in our room.
	Yuxin held the scraps tenderly. "Brother Gao wrote this poem. If Sister Chen doesn't want it, I'll gladly take good care of it." Then she turned to me. "Xiyan, can you help me find some glue?"

~

	The following morning, we were all standing outside the wall of the yard to bid Gao Yunzhe goodbye. "It was a pleasure meeting all of you," he said as he bowed to each one of us in turn.
	Chen Han inclined her head. "Likewise."
	"I wish you luck," Fei Ziyi said as he stepped forward to clap his cousin on the shoulder.
	Gao Yunzhe nodded. "I'll work hard to pass the imperial exam and bring the Gao family name back to glory. And once I do, I'll come back to visit you."
	Fei Ziyi smiled. "I'll be waiting. Safe travels."
	Gao Yunzhe bowed to us for a final time before he turned and started down the dirt path. The five of us watched him until his figure became one with the bright horizon.
	"At the beginning," Fei Ziyi said to no one in particular, "I really didn't like this cousin of mine very much. He was too stiff and formal. But in these past few days, he was really starting to grow on me."
	During the days after Gao Yunzhe's departure, Fei Ziyi was much more present around the house than before. He would even help us with maintaining the yard. At night, Fei Ziyi and Chen Han would drink together on the roof. Yuxin had started joining the two of them, which left Weiwei and me alone in our room for a few hours.
	About a week later, I was standing outside in the grassy yard, sword in hand, practicing with Weiwei and Yuxin. Fei Ziyi was instructing us today, and Chen Han had gone out to buy vegetables. Everything was going smoothly until around noon, when the doors to the yard opened and Chen Han stepped over the threshold. Her crimson robes billowed around her as she swiftly walked inside.
	"Sister Chen is back!" Weiwei said as she looked over. All of us hurried over to greet her with bright smiles, but our expressions faltered when we noticed the look on Chen Han's face.
	"What happened?" Yuxin asked quickly.
	"It's Gao Yunzhe," Chen Han said grimly. "He's been kidnapped."
    

    Chapter Fifteen

	"Well?" Yuxin said desperately after a silence fell over the yard. "What are we waiting for? Let's hurry up and save him!"
	Chen Han let out a heavy sigh. "All I know is that the people in the village saw a group of men with swords knock him unconscious and drag him away. Everyone is gossiping about it. But as it is now, we don't even know where he is."
	"Let's go look, then," Fei Ziyi said quickly. His expression was worried. "I just don't understand. Why would someone want to kidnap my cousin?" Then his face paled. "Don't tell me that someone's figured out that he's a survivor of the Gao family?"
	"I don't know if we can come to that conclusion yet," Chen Han said, pinching the bridge of her nose as if to ward off a headache. "I don't want to see any harm come to him either."
	"How do we find him?" I asked as I looked at her.
	"Ziyi and I will go to the town where Gao Yunzhe was seen last," Chen Han said. "We happen to have some skill in tracking people down."
	Fei Ziyi's face went even paler. "What happens if we do find him and he's . . ."
	"It doesn't make sense for them to kill Brother Gao," Weiwei reassured him. "If their intent was to kill him, why would they take him with them? And if they really did find something about his identity, they'd keep him alive and take him to Jingcheng to get rewarded."
	I turned to look at Weiwei with wide eyes. "Do you think they're heading to Jingcheng?"
	Weiwei shook her head. "It doesn't make sense for them to know about his identity. Brother Gao wouldn't just let other people discover such an important secret of his."
	"Speculating now won't do us any good," Chen Han said as she turned around and motioned for us to follow her out of the yard. "The three of you can come along if you'd like. Ziyi, we should hurry."
	By the time we arrived at the village, the sun was sinking beneath the horizon, and the world was steadily falling into darkness.
	I spent an hour asking everyone I could find if they knew anything about the kidnapping. As Chen Han mentioned, most of the villagers had heard about the incident, but when I asked if they knew where he was taken, no one had any answers.
	When I regrouped with the others, Yuxin's devastated expression told me how things had gone on her end.
	"Ziyi and I will spend the night here," Chen Han said a tired sigh. "We'll keep looking. Worst comes to worst, I can go to one of the larger martial arts sects and see if I can pay them to help us search. The government is notorious for ignoring these types of problems. That leaves us with asking sects, but they're going to want a lot of money for their services. The three of you should head back. If there are dangerous people here, I don't want you to engage with them."
	"But," Yuxin protested. "Brother Gao-"
	Chen Han gave her a stern look. "Your safety is just as important. Ziyi and I will keep searching. Listen to me and head back."
	I tugged on Yuxin's sleeve. "Let's go."

~

	As we walked down the silent path, I suddenly spoke up. "Do you think whoever kidnapped Brother Gao did so for his money? He was dressed in the robes of a student from the capital-maybe whoever kidnapped him saw he was a traveler and thought he might have money on him. Or maybe they just thought he wouldn't be able to fight back."
      Yuxin grabbed my arm, and I blinked at her. "If we looked like we were carrying around a decent amount of money, would they try to take us away too?"
	"It's too dangerous," Weiwei countered. Then her tone softened. "Look, we've arrived back. 
We should get some sleep. All we can do now is wait for Sister Chen to return."
	"No," Yuxin said slowly as she stopped by the doors.
	Weiwei blinked. "No?"
	"If we can somehow get the attention of the people who kidnapped Brother Gao, they'll take us straight to him."
	"Can we really say with a hundred percent certainty that they'll take us to him?" I asked quizzically. "I was only speculating when I said the kidnappers would try and take us away. Besides, what happens if we do get captured and separated?"
	"I'm willing to give it a shot," Yuxin said, determination sparking in her eyes. "Brother Gao is in danger."
	"We'll be too if we're kidnapped," Weiwei pointed out in exasperation.
	"Yuxin," I said softly, "I know you want to find him, but we shouldn't be impulsive."
	Yuxin glanced over at us. "The two of you can stay here. I'm not making you to come with me. I'm willing to go alone."
	"I'll come with you," I said quickly.
	"And me too," Weiwei added reluctantly.
	Yuxin's anxious expression melted into a smile. "Now we just need to find something that looks expensive."
	It seemed to hit us at the same time. "The dress!" we exclaimed in unison.
	Yuxin spent the rest of the night sewing by candlelight as she finished mending the dress. At some point, Weiwei and I had fallen asleep. When I woke in the morning, I found Yuxin asleep on top of the dress. Her dark hair spilled out around her like ink over the deep purple canvas.
	I gently shook her awake, and Yuxin stirred, blinking in the light. "I finished it," she said as she looked up at me.
	"Put it on," I encouraged. "You'll be a noble woman, and we'll be your bodyguards."
	Weiwei woke shortly, and the two of us helped Yuxin change into the dress. The purple fabric flowed around her, and she looked at her reflection in the copper mirror, awed.
	"You look beautiful," I said with a smile.
	Yuxin smiled back as she pinned her hair up with slender hands. "I think this is the most beautiful I've ever looked. I want Brother Gao to see me like this."
	"Yuxin," Weiwei said softly. "Are you sure you want to do this? What if something horrible happens? Please think this through again."
	Yuxin looked over her shoulder at Weiwei. "You can stay behind."
	"Xiyan . . ." Weiwei looked at me.
	"I'm going with Yuxin," I said. "I want to be there if she needs my help."
	Yuxin gave me a grateful smile. "Thank you, Xiyan." After taking one last look at herself in the mirror, she rose to her feet. "We should hurry. We can't afford to run into Sister Chen and Fei Ziyi either."
	I turned to look at my friend. "Weiwei, are you coming with us?"
      Weiwei's face was pale, but she nodded.
      
~
      
      We walked around the village for hours, but no one came. Even though we kept our eyes peeled for any signs of Chen Han and Fei Ziyi, it was as if the two of them had vanished from the village. Maybe they found a trail leading to Brother Gao, I thought to myself. Maybe we don't have to be kidnapped at all.
      We stayed out long after midnight and finally came to the disheartening conclusion to head back. It was late, so the three of us ended up at the village's sole inn to wait out the night. We sat around one of the tables. The candles flickered softly, and the only sound came from the man behind the desk sorting through account books.
      "Maybe the kidnappers are already long gone," Weiwei said quietly. "We were out during the day and at night. There's no one. I just don't understand how Brother Gao was captured in broad daylight either. Wouldn't someone have seen which direction he was taken? Wouldn't they have seen the kidnappers leave the village?"
      "Unless"-Yuxin's eyes grew large-"they never left the village!"
      "What do we-" I started in a low whisper, but before I could finish my sentence, I suddenly noticed smoke beginning to fill the room. "Watch out for poison!" I threw my arm up to cover my mouth and nose, but it was too late. One moment my head was spinning, and the next, the world tilted sideways and everything faded to black.
      
~

	I awoke in the dark. I slowly sat up, and my head throbbed painfully. Blindly feeling around, my hand fell on something that was likely a human limb. I froze, horrified.
	"Xiyan?" someone said.
	"Weiwei!" I exclaimed in a loud whisper.
	"Yes, it's me," Weiwei said quickly. Her tone was frightened. "Yuxin hasn't woken up yet, but the three of us are trapped together."
	"Trapped?"
	"I've been in here for a couple of days," a voice from the other side of the room said. "The cages are well built."
	I whirled toward the source of the voice. "Brother Gao?"
	"Yes, it's me," Gao Yunzhe said quietly. "I tried to pick the lock with my hair stick, but my kidnappers noticed and tied my hands together."
	"What happened to you?" I asked weakly. "How did you get in here?"
	Gao Yunzhe let out a sigh. "I had just finished lunch at the inn when I noticed I was feeling dizzy. I realized too late that someone had drugged the food. I ran, but I was caught and dragged down here." Then his tone turned serious. "The three of you shouldn't be here."
	"Where is here?" I reached for my own hair stick but found someone had removed it.
	"In the cellar of the inn," Gao Yunzhe said grimly.
	"Brother Gao?" Yuxin's voice asked through the dark.
	"I'm here," Gao Yunzhe answered.
	I heard Yuxin rise to her feet only to hiss in pain as her head collided with something solid. "We're in a cage?"
	"Brother Gao said he tried to pick the lock," I informed her, "but he got his hands bound as a result." I squinted, trying to make out the bars, but it was pitch black, and I couldn't even see my hand in front of my face. "How do we get out of here?" I whispered as the gravity of our situation began to set in. "Do you think Sister Chen and Fei Ziyi noticed we've gone missing?"
	"What do our captors want?" Yuxin asked faintly.
	"They're human traffickers," Gao Yunzhe said grimly. "I'm afraid the original owner of this inn was replaced by one who ran a shadier business. Plenty of unsuspecting travelers must pass through here all the time."
	I fell silent as I slumped down against the cold bars of the cage.
	Suddenly, there was a creaking sound as a door on the far side of the room opened. I squinted against the light spilling in. There was a staircase beyond the door. A man carrying a lantern stepped inside, and as he neared, I recognized the face of the innkeeper.
	"What do you want with us?" Weiwei demanded. Her voice wavered.
	The innkeeper just sneered. "We weren't originally going to take you three troublemakers, but given that you figured out our little secret, we can't let you keep investigating, can we?" The innkeeper marched over to Gao Yunzhe's cage, unlocked the door, and dragged Gao Yunzhe out by the collar.
	"Brother Gao!" Yuxin cried.
	"Don't be so dramatic," the innkeeper said silkily. "The man has already been evaluated for a price. Just be good and sit here until the evaluator comes back. You'll be reunited again in a couple of days to say your final goodbyes."
	All we could do was watch as the innkeeper dragged Gao Yunzhe across the room and opened another door. I could barely make out the dark tunnel beyond as I craned my neck, but there was only so much I could see before the two of them vanished from sight. There was a scraping sound as someone shut the door to the stairs, and the room fell into darkness again.
	I didn't realize I was shaking until Weiwei put a reassuring hand on top of mine.
	"What do we do?" I whispered. "If we can't get out of here, all of us are going to be sold off."
	"I still have a hair stick," Yuxin said suddenly. "We could try to pick the lock."
	"Hair stick?" I blinked. "Mine was taken away."
	"It's a hidden one," Yuxin explained. "It's in my shoe."
	"We should save it for later," I said softly. "It's only us here now. We don't know where they took Brother Gao. We can only wait for them to take us to him."
	A silence fell between us as we sat there in the dark. As the minutes dragged into hours, I began to feel more and more hopeless. After everything that had happened, was this where the three of us were to be forced apart? I had never been truly alone before. In the palace, I had Weiwei and Shen Fanghuan, and before that, Yuxin. Something about the darkness and the bars of the cage made me think back to the palace dungeons. I shivered.
	"I was in a place like this before," Weiwei said quietly.
	I turned to try and find her through the dark.
	"When my father sold me off, I was locked in a cage with a number of other girls. I must have been there for weeks before I was finally sold to the palace as a maid. If I'm correct, our kidnappers will most likely take us and Brother Gao to the place where they keep the rest of the poor people they've kidnapped."
	I placed a hand on her. "You've never mentioned this before."
	I could hear the sad smile in her voice. "It isn't exactly something I'm enthusiastic to talk about."
	Suddenly, the sound of footsteps echoed on the stairs. We all fell silent as the door opened and the innkeeper stepped inside. This time he had another man with him. The two of them came to a stop outside our cage, and I flinched as he raised his lantern.
	"This one is a good value," the second man declared as he pointed at Yuxin. "This one"-he turned to look at me-"also a fairly good value. But this one . . ." he glanced down at Weiwei. "She can do as a servant." Then he turned back to the innkeeper. "I didn't think you had the guts to capture more than one at once."
	I just watched in silence as they looked us over one last time before turning and leaving us alone in the dark again.
	I wasn't sure how long we waited for the innkeeper to return, this time with more men. They unlocked our cage dragged us through the same tunnel we had previously seen him take Gao Yunzhe.
	Even though it was difficult to see far down the tunnel, I could feel the ground slowly begin to slope upward. I didn't have much time to get a better grasp of my surroundings before one of our kidnappers stuffed a sack over my head.
	As we continued to walk, I could suddenly feel the cool air on my skin. We were outside. The next thing I knew, my hands and feet were being bound, and I was being thrown onto something hard. My heart raced in my chest. I could hear horses.
	"Be quiet if you want to stay in one piece," one of our kidnappers warned.
	For a while, I just lay there, my heart thundering away. The seconds dragged into minutes and the minutes into hours.
	After some time, a gruff voice said, "We should get a move on. Martial artists from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect were spotted in the area." Then the world moved as the cart jolted forward. I could sense Weiwei and Yuxin next to me, but all of us remained silent.
	The cart came to a stop hours later, and we were dragged off it. When the sacks were finally removed from our heads, we found ourselves in a barn of sorts. Our kidnappers left us locked inside, and I looked around the room. There were no windows, and the only light came from the slits between the wood.
	"Brother Gao!" Yuxin exclaimed. She hurried over to the corner of the barn where Gao Yunzhe was lying on the dirt. Given that our hands and feet were still bound, our movements were compromised.
	Gao Yunzhe slowly opened his eyes. "Miss Xia?"
	Yuxin turned to me quickly. "Xiyan, the hair stick in my shoe-see if you can grab it and cut our ropes."
	I reached into her shoe with much difficulty. "Ouch!" I suddenly withdrew my hand to find it bleeding. I stared at Yuxin. "That isn't an ordinary hair stick."
	"I have to be able to defend myself, don't I?" Yuxin said tiredly.
	"Let me try again. I'll be more careful this time." True to my word, this time I was able to retrieve the hair stick.
	Yuxin and I sat back to back as I tried my best to cut through her ropes. When the ropes fell away, Yuxin quickly took the hair stick to free me from my own ropes. I got to work untying Weiwei's restraints as Yuxin freed Gao Yunzhe.
	"I've already tried the door," Gao Yunzhe said tiredly. "It doesn't budge, and now I'm covered in bruises."
	"This doesn't seem to be our final destination," Weiwei said quietly.
	Just then, we heard the sound of keys jingling. Yuxin quickly stuffed her hair stick back into her shoe as the door of the barn opened.
	"You!" one of the men standing in the doorway barked at me. "Can you dance?"
	I jumped backward in surprise. "What?"
	"I asked if you can dance," the man repeated impatiently. If the men realized we had untied ourselves, they didn't seem to care.
	"A little bit," I said hesitantly.
	They turned their attention to Yuxin. "What about you?"
	"I'm a dancer," Yuxin said softly.
	"And you?" the man glanced at Weiwei.
	Weiwei was shaking. "I don't know how."
	The men looked at each other before coming to a silent decision. "We'll take her."
	I stared in shock as the men grabbed Weiwei and dragged her out of the barn. "Weiwei!" my legs finally moved as I rushed at the door. But it was locked, and I fell against it hopelessly. "Weiwei!"
	"When they first locked me in here," Gao Yunzhe said, "they mentioned something about a dinner party and having three girls to choose from to entertain the guests." His face was pale.
	"We need to save her," I said tearfully, ramming against the door with my shoulder.
	"Xiyan," Yuxin called. Her voice was higher than usual. "Brother Gao already tried that!"
	Time passed, and I sat by the door in a daze. The light from outside slowly faded as night fell, and it wasn't until very late that night that the door finally opened.
	In the light spilling in from the doorway, I could see Weiwei being shoved inside. She had been changed into a fancy dress. Her hair was coming free of its pins, and her face was painted nearly beyond recognition. "Weiwei!" I dropped to my knees at her side as she toppled to the ground. She reeked of alcohol.
	"Xiyan." Weiwei let out a laugh as she smiled up at me. She draped her arms over my shoulders before letting out a hiccup.
	"What happened?" I clasped Weiwei's hands as I searched her face. "Are you okay?"
	Weiwei giggled as she fell backward to stare up at the ceiling with unfocused eyes. "They made me dance." She hiccupped again. "They said I was an intoxicated maiden. I danced in front of the guests. Then sent me back here."
	Yuxin and Gao Yunzhe moved closer.
	"The Intoxicated Maiden," Yuxin said, quietly. "When I was younger, I had to perform it too. In the brothel, they poured liquor down my throat until I couldn't remember who I was or what was going on. They always selected the worst dancer for the part so they can point and laugh." Yuxin knelt by Weiwei and me. "We should find a place for Weiwei to sleep. Fortunately, it doesn't seem like she was at their mercy for very long."
	"Brothel?" Gao Yunzhe's asked in surprise.
	Yuxin's eyes were sad. "I didn't want you to know. Those were the worst years of my life."
	After Yuxin and I lay Weiwei down in the corner of the barn, we sat in silence for the rest of the night.

~

	When morning came, the kidnappers stuffed sacks over our heads again and threw us back onto the cart. When the bags were removed later, we seemed to be underground again. It took me a moment to realize I was in another cage. Yuxin and Weiwei were still by my side, but Gao Yunzhe had vanished.
	As my eyes slowly adjusted to the low light, I realized with a jolt that we weren't the only people in the room. There were a number of other cages, each of them with three to four young women locked within them.
	"Hey," I said quietly, trying to get the attention of one of the young women in the cage next to ours. "I don't see any men here. Are they locked up somewhere else?"
	One of the young women glanced around before quietly answering, "They're in the room next door. Sometimes I can hear our kidnappers arguing about which of them can be sold as field laborers and which ones can be servants."
	"How long have you been here?" I whispered.
	"A couple of days."
	"Is there a way to escape?"
	The young woman looked panicked. "If there was a way to escape, all of us would be gone already instead of sitting here waiting to be sold!"
	I turned to Yuxin. "Do you still have that hair stick?"
	Yuxin nodded. "I can pick the lock. But then what?"
	I frowned. "That . . . that's something we'll need to think about."
	Footsteps sounded, and I clamped my mouth shut. Voices followed shortly. "The boss wants us to make a sale tomorrow. How about we take the three men in the back?" From the way their voices were slightly muffled, I concluded they were a wall apart from us. "I think we should sell some of the girls too.
	Suddenly, the voices went silent. "Who's there?" one of the men asked in alarm. "I'm warning you, we're armed!"
	Cries of "ghost!" echoed through the space, and I found myself holding my breath.
	"Who are you calling a ghost?" a voice barked. "You idiots, I'm your boss!"
	I found myself unable to pay attention for the rest of their conversation. They had just given me an idea. Yuxin caught my gaze; it seemed she was thinking the same thing. "They must have seen their boss's shadow in a weird light," she whispered. "They're afraid of ghosts."
	"And so," I finished for her, "we should give them a ghost to be afraid of."

~

	I sat in the cage alone. Weiwei and Yuxin had already left to do their parts, and now all I had to do was wait for the commotion to start. I absently rolled Yuxin's hair stick between my fingers. My heart was beating too quickly in my chest.
	The coppery smell of blood still lingered from when Yuxin cut her hand to paint Weiwei's face and clothes red. Weiwei would act as our ghost. When the guards were distracted, Yuxin would free Gao Yunzhe and the other men, while I stayed to help the women.
	Weiwei was frightened by the task, but she was determined to help us escape. I glanced over at where Weiwei was standing in the corner of the room. The shadows from the lanterns cast her in ominous shadows. I glanced back at the staircase before letting out a cry. "Ghost! Someone help!"
	Following my lead, the other women in the room began to cry out in alarm as well. "Ghost!"
	The sound of running footsteps echoed as the men guarding the stairs rushed into the room. The other women and I frantically pointed at Weiwei, who stood in the corner of the room. From a distance, she truly looked frightening. Her dress was stained with blood, her hair tangled, and her makeup smeared.
	The guards hadn't taken more than one look before they were fleeing back up the stairs in pure terror. Once their footsteps vanished, I quickly pushed open the door to my cage and hurried over to pick the locks.
	We waited and waited, but there was still no sign of Yuxin or the men. Finally, I decided to check on them myself. I pushed open the door across from the steps. We couldn't afford to delay freeing the men any longer. After rushing into the room, I went from cage to cage, unlocking them just as I had done in the previous room. It didn't take me long to find Gao Yunzhe.
	"Miss Xia?" Gao Yunzhe blinked at me as I helped him to his feet.
	"Take this!" I thrust Yuxin's hair stick into his hands. "Can you unlock the rest? I need to find Yuxin!"
	Before he could respond, I was hurrying back the way I came. I only just reached the door before I nearly collided with Yuxin.
	"Yuxin!" I exclaimed. "Are you alright? What happened?"
	"There were two men-they pulled me into that corridor over there," she said breathlessly. Then she looked over my shoulder. "You freed the men already."
	I nodded my head. "We have to hurry, I don't know when the guards might return with back up."
	We rushed back toward the stairs where Weiwei was waiting with the women. Her panicked expression turned to relief as Yuxin, Gao Yunzhe, and I emerged with the other men close behind.
	I turned to Yuxin. "Do you think that corridor leads outside?"
	Yuxin had only just opened her mouth when a thundering of footsteps came from the stairs. Ice flooded my soul as all our kidnappers appeared in front of us.
	"Hey!" one of the men pointed at Weiwei. "The ghost isn't actually a ghost! They tricked us!"
	My heart was racing in my chest as I slid into a fighting stance, but then it nearly skipped a beat. There was a flash of movement as a figure dressed in crimson appeared behind them. Our kidnappers barely had time to yell out before they were knocked off their feet.
	"Sister Chen!" I exclaimed.
	Chen Han was at the bottom of the stairs in seconds, and the men lay in a heap behind her. She pointed her sword at them. "I'll give you three seconds to run if you value your lives. Three, two . . ." Before she hit one, all our kidnappers scrambled to their feet and sprinted. Chen Han let out an amused laugh as she sheathed her sword. "At least they're sensible." Then she smiled faintly as Weiwei and I both hugged her tightly. "You're safe now."
	"Is my cousin here too?" Gao Yunzhe asked.
	Chen Han nodded. "He's waiting at the top of the stairs to catch those human traffickers."
	"Sister Chen." I let out a sob. "We never should have gone off on our own."
	Chen Han gave me a gentle smile. "Let's get out of here first. We can talk about this again when we get home."
	Everything that happened next blurred together. Ultimately, Fei Ziyi brought us back to the residence, while Chen Han stayed behind to hand over the traffickers and their victims to the local government officials. During the days that Chen Han had yet to return, Gao Yunzhe stayed with us, but he made it clear that once the heroine in red returned, he would take his leave again. This time, Fei Ziyi announced that he'd accompany his cousin to make sure he arrived safely at his destination.
	The four of us were still shaken from what had happened, but after a few days, things started to feel like they were returning to normal. Before long, Chen Han returned, and we bid our farewells to the cousins. After watching their retreating figures for a few minutes, the four of us turned to head back inside the walls of the residence.
	A heavy layer of clouds cloaked the sky in gray, with rain threatening in the distance. Fortunately, we were back indoors before the downpour began. I took my bath, then sat in our room, absently running a comb through my damp hair while listening to the patter of rain outside.
	There was a soft sound of a door opening, and I turned to watch Yuxin step into the room. I set my comb down before walking over to her. "Yuxin," I said quietly.
	Yuxin was drenched from head to toe, and her knees were covered in mud. She was still wearing the purple dress, which now looked as if it had seen better days. "Xiyan."
	"I heard Sister Chen scolding you," I said softly. "Yuxin, she didn't want us to be killers."
	"What was I supposed to do?" Yuxin said as rain continued to drip down her hair and face. "If I hadn't killed them, they would have killed me. They wanted to sell us, Xiyan. They wanted to sell us and Brother Gao."
	"I know." Yuxin blinked in surprise as I wrapped my arms around her in a tight embrace. "I'm just glad you're alive." I finally released her. "I know you wanted to be the one to help Brother Gao, but we really couldn't afford to delay any longer."
	Yuxin just smiled sadly. "I'll admit that I'm jealous of you, Xiyan."
	"Jealous?"
	"At least at the palace, you had Weiwei. Before, all I ever wanted was to be respected. But today the only thing I wanted was for Brother Gao to glance at me a few more times."
	Before I could think of an answer, the door to the room opened again, and Weiwei stepped inside. She furrowed her brow as she looked at us. "Is everything alright?"
	"I'll be back later," Yuxin said shortly. "I still need to wash up." I watched as she turned on her heel and glided out of the room.
      Weiwei walked over to our beds and took a seat. She began to run her fingers through her hair, and I picked up a comb to help her. "Xiyan," Weiwei began, turning to look back at me.
	I gently turned her head back. "Weiwei, my good sister, Yuxin and I are getting along fine."
	Weiwei let out a sigh. "Alright."
	After blowing out the lazily flickering candles around the room, I returned to Weiwei. "Are you going to sleep now?"
      She nodded tiredly. "If Yuxin comes back while I'm asleep, tell her I wish her goodnight."
      I sat there in the dark, listening to the rain for a while; it was the only sound in the silent world beyond. But as the minutes slowly melted into hours, Yuxin did not return.
    

    Chapter Sixteen

	When I awoke in the morning, it was still raining. I changed into my day clothes and tied my hair up into a ponytail. I glanced around. My eyes fell on the pile of purple fabric in the corner. I crouch down in front of it. It looked like Yuxin had done her best to clean it, but the bloodstains on it were still visible against the dark fabric. I sighed. It looked like the dress really was ruined this time.
      Weiwei was still asleep, and I silently made my way out of the room so as not to wake her. I went downstairs to find Chen Han and Yuxin sitting at the table. Yuxin turned around and greeted me.
	"Yuxin!" I said, hurrying over to take the seat across from her. "How are you today?"
	Yuxin offered me a smile. "I ended up having a couple of drinks last night. When I returned, you were already asleep. I didn't mean to make you worry."
	I returned the smile. "As long as you're fine, that's all that matters." Then I turned to look at Chen Han. "And the two of you . . .?"
	Yuxin reached across the table to place a hand on mine. "Sister Chen and I made breakfast together. We talked things out. She was right to scold me. I learned my lesson."
      I nodded, relieved. I looked to the heroine in red again. "How many days do you think Fei Ziyi is going to be away?"
	Chen Han thoughtfully rested her chin on her hands. "I'd say two weeks to a month at most. When it comes to traveling, he should know all the roads as well as I do. Anyways, I think it's about time I send the three of you out to take on jobs. With your skills, I think you can take on the smaller ones. You can't rely on me for money forever."
	I exchanged a glance with Yuxin. "Sister Chen, maybe you have a little too much faith in us."
	Weiwei appeared on the stairs with tired eyes, and she joined us at the table. "Why didn't anyone wake me? Did I miss anything important?"
	"Sister Chen thinks we're ready to start taking on jobs," Yuxin informed her.
	Weiwei looked at the heroine in red. "Really?"
	"I think you can do it," Chen Han said confidently. "How about later today I'll take you to one of the towns requesting help? They'll pay you to help complete the tasks."
	I let out a sigh. "We'll do our best."
	
~

	I stood next to Yuxin and Weiwei as we gazed out over the small farm in front of us. Yuxin gave me an exasperated look as I determinedly rolled up my sleeves. "The first job we have is to pull weeds?"
	"The farmer sprained his wrist," I said as I crouched down. "I thought we might as well start with something that won't with us going face to face with something dangerous."
	Over the next couple of weeks, the three of us took on a number of similar jobs, along with some more dangerous ones. Some of these involved protecting trading carts from bandits and tracking down stolen livestock.
      But one day, things didn't go as smoothly as we hoped. As Weiwei, Yuxin, and I crashed through a bamboo forest, chasing after a band of fleeing thieves, we heard a whooshing sound from overhead. Arrows zipped through the air, and I skidded to a stop as they hit the thieves in the legs. The thieves toppled over, hissing in pain. I whirled and raised my sword in front of me as two young men emerged from the fog.
	"You're martial artists," one of the men called out to us. "Which sect do you belong to?"
	I exchanged glances with Weiwei and Yuxin.
	"Sect?" Yuxin called back. "We don't belong to any sect."
	I eyed the young men. Judging by their outfits, they appeared to be martial artists as well. Both were dressed in tawny brown, with their dark hair tied back.
	"No sect?" The men exchanged a glance.
	One of them took a step forward and greeted us respectfully. "Forgive us. Tensions have been rising, and recently the Fire Sea Abyss Sect has been trying to steal all of our jobs. We thought you might be from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect, so-"
	"I've heard the name before," Weiwei said. "There's the Fire Sea Abyss Sect and the-what's it called again?"
	"Owl and Aspen Sect," the second young man said proudly. Though his companion seemed a couple of years older than Yuxin, Weiwei, and me, the second martial artist couldn't have been any older than us.
	"That's it!" Weiwei said triumphantly. "The Fire Sea Abyss Sect and the Owl and Aspen Sect are currently the two most well-known sects in the martial arts world."
	"Now that we've got that cleared up," the first man said, "the three of you can take the thieves back to claim the reward money. Apologies again."
	Suddenly, there was a rustling from the bamboo, and three figures appeared. Each of them was dressed in fiery orange, and they all wore the same sneer on their faces. "Looks like we found some puny birds," the young man at the front of the group drawled. "We'll be taking that reward money, thank you very much."
	The first young man from the Owl and Aspen Sect frowned. "The money isn't yours to take. These young ladies are the ones who took on the job."
	"They don't belong to your silly bird sect?"
	"Leave them alone. Stealing from us is one thing, but you shouldn't steal from those who aren't involved in our sect conflicts."
	The young man from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect eyed us up and down. "I guess they don't look like they're from the bird sect."
	"They aren't," said the second man from Owl and Aspen. His hand went to the hilt of his sword. "Just let them claim the reward money. It's not yours. Don't make us fight you over it."
	"Fight?" called one of the other Fire Sea Abyss members. "We've been itching for an opportunity to make you stupid birds know your place!"
	There was the sound of swords being drawn, and then the members from the two sects pointed their blades at each other.
	"Wait!" I called as I hurried forward to stand between them. "Don't fight! If you want the reward money, you can have it! It would be silly to have someone lose their life over something like this."
	"Move, girl!" The man standing in front of his fellow Fire Sea Abyss members shoved me out of the way. Despite my offer, the sound of clashing blades filled the otherwise silent forest before I could protest.
	Even though the two young men from the Owl and Aspen Sects were obviously skilled martial artists, they were still outnumbered three to two. Finally, the fighting halted as one of the young men from the Owl and Aspen Sect toppled to the ground. His sword clattered to the dirt next to him as he clasped his bleeding leg.
	"Tian Yong!" The second Owl and Aspen member quickly kneeled beside his fallen companion. "Tian Yong, are you alright?" Then he glared at the three Fire Sea Abyss Sect. "You've gone too far!"
	The Fire Sea Abyss members just smirked as they sheathed their swords. "We'll be taking that money. How about you birds stay away from us." With that said, they grabbed the thieves, forced them to their feet, and strode back into the fog from which they had emerged.
	The second Owl and Aspen member drew his crossbow and aimed it at their retreating figures, but he quickly tossed it aside when Tian Yong let out a pained hiss.
	I quickly knelt next to Tian Yong as well. "Are you alright?" I asked worriedly. He had rolled up his pant leg to reveal a deep gash just below his knee.
	"How dare they!" the other young man glowered. "I'll-"
	"Yao Jie," Tian Yong said, pained, "it's fine. It's not like they severed any of my limbs. But my leg . . . I think it might be broken."
	"Where's the closest physician?" Yao Jie asked anxiously as he tried to help Tian Yong to his feet. "We're not familiar with this area."
	"I'll show you the way," I said, stepping forward to help Yao Jie lift Tian Yong. Before long, Tian Yong had one arm around my shoulder and the other around Yao Jie's. Weiwei knelt down to pick up the swords and crossbows they had discarded, and then we were on our way.
      When we finally arrived at the physician's store, Tian Yong was taken to the back room, while the rest of us were told to wait at the front.
	"How long have you been practicing martial arts?" I decided to ask Yao Jie in an attempt to break the heavy silence pressing down on us.
	"Over ten years," Yao Jie said shortly. His posture was tense, and he kept his eyes glued to the door of the back room for any signs of movement.
	"Why are the two sects at odds?" I questioned.
	Yao Jie folded his arms over his chest. "The Fire Sea Abyss Sect has always seen us as their rivals. They want to be number one in the martial arts world, and as long as our Owl and Aspen Sect exists, they can only ever be tied with us. They started stealing all the help requests in the area in an attempt to prevent us from making money. So now we've got to go out even farther to try and find work that they haven't taken already."
	Weiwei frowned. "They don't seem to behave fairly."
	Yao Jie scoffed. "They really don't. I just hope our two sects don't actually go to war against each other. If that were to happen, it's really hard to say who would win or if any of us would survive it at all."
	I fell silent at that.
	The door to the back room creaked open, and we all turned to watch the physician escort Tian Yong out. "I've cleaned and dressed his wound," the physician told us. "As for the broken bone . . . he needs to rest and stay off his leg until it has healed."
	Yao Jie leaped to his feet and hurried over to steady Tian Yong.
	The two martial artists exchanged a glance. "Are there any inns around here?" Tian Yong asked. "We happen to be very far from home."
	"We don't have the money to stay at an inn long enough for your leg to heal," Yao Jie said worriedly. "I wouldn't risk trying to travel back. Is there anywhere cheaper we can stay?"
	"You can stay with us," I offered.
      Weiwei nodded along. "That way, you don't have to spend any money."
	"Really?" Yao Jie's head snapped over to look at us. Then he smiled in relief. "Thank you."
	Yao Jie and I helped support Tian Yong as he limped down the path outside. Fortunately, it wasn't raining, and the sky high above was a shade of brilliant blue.
	"I don't think we've introduced ourselves yet," I said as we walked. "I'm Xia Xiyan. Xia Yuxin is on our left, and behind her is Hu Qiuwei."
	Tian Yong looked at me and Yuxin. "Sisters?"
	I nodded my head.
	"We haven't properly introduced ourselves either," Yao Jie noted. "I'm Yao Jie, and this is Tian Yong."
	Yuxin walked over to me and lowered her voice. "Do you think Sister Chen is going to appreciate us bringing these martial artists to her residence?"
	"Who's Sister Chen?" Tian Yong asked curiously.
	"She's our teacher," I answered proudly.
	Tian Yong offered me a strained smile. "I hope we're not too much trouble. If we are, we can try and find an inn to stay at-"
	"You're not too much trouble," I interjected. "It would feel wrong not to help you after you tried to reason with the Fire Sea Abyss Sect for us."
	When we reached the wall surrounding Chen Han's residence, Yuxin pushed the doors open. After we helped Tian Yong over the high threshold, we helped him limp toward the house at the back of the yard.
	There was a rush of crimson fabric, and then Chen Han was standing in front of us. "You brought guests?"
	Tian Yong's eyes widened. "You're Chen Han! Wu Ren's student!"
	Yao Jie blinked at his friend in surprise. "You know her? How come I don't know of a Chen Han?"
	"You've got to know of Wu Ren though, don't you?" Tian Yong said as his words spilled out in a rush.
	"Of course I know of Hero Wu-"
	"Chen Han is one of his students!" Tian Yong tried to greet Chen Han with a bow, but then stopped when his injured leg nearly gave out.
	"This is Tian Yong and Yao Jie from the Owl and Aspen Sect," I explained. "They were attacked by the Fire Sea Abyss Sect after trying to help us, and Tian Yong was injured."
	A smile tugged on the corners of Chen Han's red-painted lips. "I see. If they want to stay here and recuperate, be my guest. But if they want me to join the war between the sects, I'm going to have to kick them out."
	"Trust us when we say that we're not here to rope you into the conflict," Yao Jie said with a stressed frown. "We just need a place where Tian Yong can recover."
	"You can use the study as a room to recover," Chen Han said as she turned. "I'll get it ready."
	"Thank you!" Tian Yong and Yao Jie chorused.
	Once we helped Tian Yong into the study, Weiwei went to prepare some food. After determining that Tian Yong needed some time to rest, Yuxin and I offered to show Yao Jie around the yard.
	"I've heard of Wu Ren," Yao Jie said as he followed us outside. "He was a master in his own right. I never thought I'd see the place he used to live with my own eyes."
      When we finished our tour around the yard, the three of us took a seat on the front porch of the house. "The weather's nice today," I commented absently as I stared up at the sky.
	"It is nice," Yao Jie agreed. "Again, I'm really sorry to have to disturb all of you here. Once Tian Yong can walk properly again, we'll be gone."
	"It's fine, really," I tried to reassure him.
	Yao Jie let out a sigh. "I'm trying to calculate how much money I can make if I were to sell some of my belongings. I can't sell the crossbows-they belong to our Owl and Aspen Sect. My sword . . . I can't really sell that either. If someone attacks, then what do I do? I have this, though." I looked on as Yao Jie produced a jade pendant from his belt. "I could pawn this."
	Yao Jie held out the pendant for us to examine. I shook my head. "That looks important to you." 
	Yuxin nodded in agreement. "I wouldn't pawn that. You wouldn't be able to get it back."
	Yao Jie sighed again as he refastened the pendant to his belt. Then his expression darkened. "If you didn't offer to help shelter us for the time being, I probably would have had to sell it. This pendant is important to me, but it's not worth anything if my friend loses his leg. The Fire Sea Abyss Sect has gone too far this time."
	"I never thought the martial art sects would be like this," I said sadly.
	"The Fire Sea Abyss Sect wants to be first," Yao Jie explained tiredly. "They'll do anything, even if it means playing dirty. They don't deserve to be first. And what they've done to Tian Yong . . . Well, if he can't practice martial arts, he'll be devastated. I just wish there was something I could do." Something like sadness flickered behind his eyes as he looked at his jade pendant again. "I don't want to see Tian Yong in pain. I wish there was something I could do to make him happier. But I'm useless."
	"I couldn't help but overhear your conversation," Weiwei said, and the three of us turned around to find her standing behind us.
	"How's Tian Yong?" Yao Jie asked quickly.
	"He's just gone to sleep," Weiwei said as she took a seat next to me. "He claimed he wasn't hungry when I brought him food, but he ended up eating it all anyway."
	After nodded in relief, Yao Jie rose to his feet, brushed invisible specks of dust from his clothes, and announced, "I'm going to go practice with my sword."
	Yuxin rose to her feet as well. "I'm going to find Sister Chen."
	"I'll come with you," I said.
	"Me too," Weiwei added.
	The three of us walked through the house, searching for the heroine in red. We checked the first floor and looked out over the yard from the second-story walkway, but Chen Han was nowhere to be seen.
	"Did she go out?" Weiwei asked uncertainly as we watched Yao Jie practicing in the yard. His sword was a flash of metal.
	Suddenly, there was a sound from the room behind us, and the three of us turned in surprise as the doors to Wu Ren's room slid open to reveal Chen Han. She flashed us a smile as she leaned against the doorframe. "Looking for me?"
	Weiwei stood on her tiptoes, trying to peer around Chen Han's shoulders to look at the room beyond. "Sister Chen, what are you doing in Hero Wu's room?"
	"I come here once a week to keep the dust from gathering," she said simply. "Would you like to take a look?"
	I nodded eagerly. Ever since I arrived here over a year ago, I had never entered Wu Ren's room. I had to admit, I was curious to see if there was anything inside that would give a clue to what kind of person Wu Ren was. The door was always closed whenever I passed by during the day, and this opportunity was too good to pass up.
	Chen Han stepped aside and invited into the room. Once inside, I looked around in awe at the number of book-filled shelves lining the room.
	"My master loved to read stories," Chen Han said wistfully as she followed my gaze. "He would read tales of heroes who fought against the evilest of evils. My master always hoped that our world could be more like the worlds depicted in these stories."
	Weiwei let out a sigh. "I wish I could have gotten a chance to meet Hero Wu."

~	

	As the week went by, I found myself growing more and more accustomed to Yao Jie and Tian Yong's presence. At night, Chen Han, Yuxin, and Yao Jie would all go up to the roof to drink, and during that time, Weiwei and I would be left alone in our room.
	Weiwei was sitting by the window, staring out into the night when I entered. I had just finished my bath, and the chill from the cool wind made me wrap my arms around myself. "Weiwei," I said through chattering teeth as I took a seat next to her. "You're not cold?"
	Weiwei turned to look at me. "What? Oh." She shut the window.
	"I'm sorry, Weiwei. I seemed to have interrupted an important thought of yours."
	Weiwei shook her head. "No, no, it's fine."
	My smile faltered as Weiwei continued to look at me. "Is everything alright?"
	"What?" She quickly looked away. "Of course. Everything's fine."
	I angled my head to the side but didn't push it. "I'm going to sleep," I said after a moment. "If there's anything you want to talk about, just wake me up, okay?"
	Weiwei nodded. "Goodnight, Xiyan."
      I smiled.
      
    

    Chapter Seventeen

	"Look!" Yao Jie grinned as he held up a poster for Weiwei, Yuxin, and me to see. "I managed to grab a job before the Fire Sea Abyss Sect got to it! The villagers agreed to give me a week before sending out another request."
	Yuxin frowned slightly at the poster. "A murder case? Are you sure you can take it on by yourself? What if the culprit is dangerous?"
	Yao Jie gave us a knowing wink. "That's where the three of you come in. You're learning martial arts, aren't you?"
	I exchanged a glance with Yuxin. "We are. We might know enough to deal with people who don't know any martial arts, but if someone at your level was our opponent, we'd still lose even with three to one."
	"It's possible that the culprit doesn't know martial arts," Yao Jie suggested. "Apparently, all of the victims so far were stabbed to death with a dull knife."
	"Maybe we should ask Sister Chen to help us out," Weiwei said quietly.
	Yao Jie shook his head. "If we all leave the house, who will make sure nothing happens to Tian Yong? Besides, I can't just crash at your teacher's residence and then make her do tasks for me. I'll split the reward money with the three of you. How does that sound?"
	"I'm in," I said as I took a step forward. "I'll do my best to help."
	"And us," said Weiwei and Yuxin.
	Once the four of us were ready to set off, we regrouped in the yard. We hadn't even started toward the exit when Chen Han appeared on the balcony of the house. She leaned against the railings as she looked down at us. "Where are you off to?"
	"Yao Jie found a job to take," Weiwei called up to her. "We're acting as his back up."
	Chen Han nodded. "Keep an eye on Yuxin, will you?"
	"Don't worry!" Yao Jie called. "I'll make sure your students are safe. If things get dangerous, I promise I'll send them back right away."
	Once we started down the path, I fell into pace at Yuxin's side. "I think she's reminding you not to do anything dangerous."
	Yuxin raised her head to the sky. A breeze picked up, sending her dark hair fluttering around her. "She can afford to let her attackers live. She has the skill to do so. But we're different."
	I sighed. "I get what you mean. What Sister Chen says is reasonable, but you also have a point."
	"I couldn't help overhearing your conversation," Yao Jie said. "Unfortunately, death is very common in the martial arts world. As a martial artist, fighting and killing is inevitable. Danger is around every corner. But if it wasn't for us, who would help defend the people? Who would help uphold justice? Every emperor is just like their predecessor-they all turn a blind eye."
	We walked in silence until I decided to speak up again. "Between you and Tian Yong, who's martial arts are more advanced?"
	"Tian Yong, of course," Yao Jie answered. "He's two years older than me. He also started training two years before I did. I work hard, but even though we've been traveling together for years now, I'm still a little kid in Tian Yong's eyes." He dropped his gaze. "I don't want to be that little kid anymore. I'll grow up quickly, but he'll be a hero in his own right in no time. I'm afraid he won't be able to wait for me. I'm afraid I won't be able to keep up."
	After renting horses, the four of us were galloping along the main road. By the time we arrived at the village that placed the help request, the sun had dropped from the sky.
	Yao Jie got us a room at an inn, and then we parted ways. Even though it was getting late, Yao Jie and Yuxin decided to start investigating, while Weiwei and I opted to stay in the room to rest.
	"Sister Chen told us to keep an eye on Yuxin," Weiwei said softly. I was sitting by the window, and I turned to look over at her. "What are your thoughts on that?"
	I frowned faintly. "If I was in the same situation as Yuxin, I don't know what I would have done."
	"How did Yuxin kill her attackers? I don't remember her ever picking up a weapon. I don't think she'll say it out loud, but I think she felt hurt when Sister Chen made her kneel in the rain."
	"I think Sister Chen is being hard on Yuxin," I said with a sigh. "I don't know who to side with. I don't want to take sides."
	"We should get some sleep," Weiwei said after a long pause. "It's been a long journey."
	I nodded as Weiwei scooted over to make room for me on the bed. "I'll sleep."
	I didn't realize just how tired I was until exhaustion crashed into me. I wasn't sure when I entered the dream, but I recognized the tall stone walls that rose around me. I squinted against the sunlight as the wind swept delicate pink petals over the wall. This was the palace.
	"Xiyan!" a voice called.
	I turned around to find Shen Fanghuan running toward me.
	My eyes widened. "Fanghuan!" I sprinted toward him, and the two of us met halfway in a tight embrace.
	Shen Fanghuan held me tightly. "I haven't seen you in days. Have the Li sisters returned? Are they keeping you busy?"
	I just shook my head and finally pulled back to look at his face. Shen Fanghuan's eyes were full of concern as they held my gaze. I let my face relax into a smile. "I'm here now, aren't I?"
	Shen Fanghuan smiled as well as he nodded. "Oh, that's right. I have something for you."
	I blinked. "Another flower?"
	Shen Fanghuan shook his head, then produced a small pouch from one of his pockets and held it out to me. "These are flower seeds. I know we can only meet sparingly, so during the time we're apart, now you can grow your own flowers."
	My eyes stung as I let out a laugh. Smiling through my tears, I reached out to take the pouch from him. But just before my fingers could close around it, Shen Fanghuan vanished.
	I stood there alone in the palace corridor. The silence was pressing down on me. Slowly crouching down, I wrapped my arms around my body. I was shaking, and it was then that I caught a glimpse of my shadow on the stones. That wasn't the shadow of a young woman. It was the shadow of a demon.
	Startled, my eyes snapped open. The bright sky of the palace was gone, and instead, I was back in the dark inn room with Weiwei fast asleep beside me. I slowly sat up, and for a while, I sat there as silent tears trickled down the sides of my face.

~

	"Here's what Xia Yuxin and I learned about the murders from our inquiries last night," Yao Jie informed us as we ate breakfast at one of the street stalls. "The murderer seems to only target families of three. Either a parent is murdered or their child is murdered. All of the cases have happened at night. The murderer is very stealthy-the other members in the house are never alerted to his presence until they wake up to find one of their family members deceased. Some of the villagers have come to the conclusion that it's the work of a ghost, but I don't believe it."
	I glanced over at Yao Jie. "You don't believe in ghosts?"
	Yao Jie shook his head. "Whenever Tian Yong and I investigate horrible cases, in the end, it's always the work of a human. Even if ghosts really do exist in our world, they aren't the ones causing us the most grief, are they?"
	"Do you have a plan to catch the murderer?" Yuxin asked.
	Yao Jie frowned, deep in thought. "Not yet. The most recent murder was three days ago. I would recommend us keeping an eye on all the families of three in the village, but I'm worried that if we split up, the murderer might be too skilled for just one of us to apprehend. Besides, I promised your teacher I wouldn't let you do anything too dangerous. We might as well start with finding out how many families of three are left in the village and make a plan from there."
	The three of us spent most of the day asking around. The village was small, and it didn't take us long to identify the village leaders. That night, we were sitting in a small restaurant, joined by a middle-aged man.
      "I'm the one who posted the help request," he said tiredly. "Our village is small, and when I reported the murders to the local government, they seemed to ignore the issue altogether. That's why my only choice was to turn to martial artists for help."
	"We'll do our best," Yao Jie said determinedly. "Mr. Gu, you can count on us."
	We finished our meal and were on our way back to our inn when a scream cut through the otherwise quiet night.
	We instantly grabbed our swords and rushed toward the source of the cry. A crowd had already gathered around the house, and they parted for us as Yao Jie hurried to the front of the group. He scanned the fearful faces. "What happened here?"
	"There's been another murder," one of the villagers said tearfully. "It's poor Mrs. Pei."
	Over the hushed murmurs from the crowd, I could hear the sound of crying from within the house. "Mother!" a child was wailing.
	I exchanged a glance with Yao Jie and the others. Yao Jie nodded grimly before stepping forward and knocking on the door. "My name's Yao Jie," he called through the wood. "I'm from the Owl and Aspect sect, and I'm here to help catch the murderer."
	The door opened a few moments later to reveal a man. His eyes were red, and he wiped his tears away with a sleeve. "Please, come inside."
	I followed Yao Jie over the threshold, and my heart clenched in my chest at the scene in front of me. From my side, I could hear Weiwei inhale sharply.
	A woman was lying on the floor, her clothes stained with blood. A child no more than five years old knelt by her side. "Mother!" she cried. "Wake up!"
	"We're here to investigate," Yao Jie said quietly. "Would it be alright if we look for any traces the murder could have left behind?"
	The man silently nodded.
	Yao Jie looked at Weiwei, Yuxin, and me. Even though I was horrified, I stepped forward to examine the woman's corpse. Yuxin crouched down next to me as we examined the wounds. "She was stabbed multiple times with a dull blade," she said softly. "She was stabbed four times in the chest, and then she has three slashes on her forearms."
	"The ones on her forearms most likely came from trying to protect herself," Yao Jie said grimly. While Yuxin and I continued to examine the body, Weiwei and Yao Jie looked around the house. Yao Jie opened each window and peered outside before closing them again. "It's too dark to see if there's any tracks. But given that none of the windows have been damaged or have any blood on them, we shouldn't rule out the front door. Sir, did you return home to find your wife like this? I know you're hurting right now, but please try your best to answer my questions. The more in depth your answers are, the more clues we have to go on to figure out who the murder is."
	The man nodded as he wiped his eyes again. "I just returned home with my daughter. But once we stepped inside, she was already like this."
	"When did you leave?"
	"Shortly before lunch."
	"And when did you get back?"
	"Less than an hour ago. My daughter started crying and attracted the attention of the other villagers. That's when the crowd gathered outside, and I shut the door to try to give our family some privacy."
	"What does your wife do during the day?"
	"She stays home to take care of the house, but in the early mornings she works outside tending our crops."
	Yao Jie furrowed his brow. "Do you usually leave the house with your daughter at the same time of day?"
      The man shook his head. "My daughter usually stays at home with my wife. My wife seemed tired today, so I decided to take my daughter with me."
      "The murderer must have entered the house on a whim," I told Yuxin under my breath. "But to know that both the father and daughter were out, they have to know everyone in the village. They must be a village local."
      Yuxin nodded. "Whoever the murderer is, they're probably still in the village."
      "But why would they do this?" I shook my head as I stared at the woman's body. I wrapped my arms around myself as I slowly rose to my feet. When I looked at the knife marks, I could almost feel them on my own body.
      "Thank you for your time," Yao Jie finally said to the man. "My friends and I will return tomorrow morning to look around outside."
      By the time the four of us exited the house, the crowd outside had dispersed. Once we were back in our inn room, Yuxin asked, "Do you often take on murder cases?"
      "Tian Yong and I have taken on a number of them over the past couple of years," Yao Jie said thoughtfully. "Normally, Tian Yong does the questioning. I just act as his back up. How do you think I did?"
      "Very well," I said.
      Yao Jie must have sensed that the three of us were still shaken because he offered us a smile. "Actually, I heard the two of you talking about how the murderer must still be in the village. I also think that. The murderer knows who all the families of three are and where they live. When we check it for clues tomorrow, we'll keep our eyes peeled for any footprints. With that said, there's a high chance that we won't be able to find anything. If the murderer is smart, he'll have already covered his tracks. The best thing to do is get all the remaining families of three to stay in one place until the murderer is found."
      I couldn't sleep well that night. First, I dreamed of being locked in the palace dungeons. Then I dreamed of being locked in the underground cages the human traffickers used. And then I dreamed of the woman who died. So this was what death looks like.
      My eyes opened to the darkness. I was still lying between Weiwei and Yuxin, but now I was shaking. In the demon realm, I had lived among a number of creatures made of pure nightmare, but none of their forms compared to the thought of death. Death scared me. It wasn't my death that scared me, but the thought of Weiwei, Yuxin, Chen Han, or anyone else I cared about looking the way the woman lying on the floor had-lifeless, still, cold. The body was still here, but the person was gone.
      Was that what Shen Fanghuan looked like when he died? My nails dug into my skin. For a while, I stared unseeingly at the ceiling.
      "Can't sleep?" A voice drew me from my thoughts, and I blinked through the dark to find Yao Jie standing by the door. "Come with me."
      I silently climbed out of bed and followed him outside. We walked down the hallway, and he pushed open the window at the end. After climbing out, he helped me onto the roof, and within minutes, the two of us were sitting under the cloudy sky.
      Yao Jie let out a sigh as he rolled out his neck. "I'm sorry. I shouldn't have brought you to this village."
      I shook my head as I clasped my hands together. "I want to be here. I want to bring the murderer to justice." I was shivering, but I wasn't completely sure if it was from the cold.
      Yao Jie offered me a sad smile before looking up at the sky. Leaning back, he let the dull moonlight wash over his face. "Lonely, isn't it? You and I could be sitting right next to each other, and yet the one we think about is out of reach."
      I nodded quietly, and for a while, the two of us sat there in silence.
      
~

	"Look!" Yao Jie said triumphantly, pointing to the footprints in the dirt. "There are tracks leading up to the window! The interesting part is how they only lead away from the house. The murderer must have entered through the front door and then escaped through the window. Lucky for us, our murderer seems to be either amateur enough not to cover his tracks-or just confident enough that no one will find him."
	The four of us followed the tracks as far as we could before they vanished into the grass just beyond the village.
	"They couldn't have left the village, right?" I frowned as I watched how the tracks stopped once they got to the grass.
	"Judging from the size of the prints," Yao Jie observed, "the murderer is male. Given that his steps aren't very close, and the impressions are shallow, he's probably quite tall and thin. Let's go back to the inn. I'll draw a picture of what he might look like, then we'll ask Mr. Gu if there's anyone in the village that could have a similar build to the murderer."
	That afternoon, the four of us were sitting around the table in Mr. Gu's house. The middle-aged man stroked his beard thoughtfully as he looked at the drawing Yao Jie held out to him. "I know everyone in this village, and there's no one like that."
	Yao Jie blinked in surprise. "That can't be, can it? Whenever Tian Yong and I speculate what the murderer must look like from the clues he's left behind, I always come close when drawing his likeness." He shook his head in defeat as he set the drawing down. "If only Tian Yong was here." Then he looked at Mr. Gu again. "Do you think we could trouble you to gather all the families of three and have them stay at the inn until the murderer is found? I don't think the inn keeper will give them a hard time given that everyone in the village knows by now that there's a murderer in their midst."
	"This . . ." Mr. Gu looked worried. "There's only three families of three left in the village. Two of the three have locked themselves in their homes in the hopes that the murderer won't kill them."
	Yao Jie offered him a smile. "I'll go talk to them."
      After the four of us left Mr. Gu's house, we hadn't gone far before a wooden ball flew through the air, and Yuxin had to jump to the side to avoid it colliding with her. The four of us whirled in surprise to find a group of children staring at us with guilty expressions. One of the children hurried forward. "Pretty sister," he said rapidly as he looked up at Yuxin, "I'm so sorry. That idiot in the back doesn't have any eyes!" He pointed at a young boy with baggy clothes who silently stood toward behind group. "Just say the word and I'll go beat him up for you right now!"
	"That's not necessary," Yuxin said quickly.
	I exchanged a glance with Weiwei. There was something suspicious about the boy at the back of the group. The boy seemed to notice our eyes on him because he stiffened. Then he turned on his heel and ran.
      "Wait!" I called.
	The young boy was fast, but Yao Jie was faster.
	The boy looked around helplessly as the four of us blocked off his escape path. "Why did you run?" Yao Jie asked the boy.
	"He ran because he's the murderer," Yuxin interjected with a gasp. "Look at his shoes! They're too big for him-hence why we were led to believe they belonged to an adult."
	The boy just silently glared up at us.
	"Are you really the murderer?" Weiwei asked.
	The boy just shook his head.
	"Can you talk?" I asked.
	The boy shook his head again.
	"Do you know who the murderer is?"
	The boy nodded.
	Yao Jie exchanged a look with me before turning back to the boy. "Can you tell us?"
	The boy motioned for us to follow him. Within minutes, we were back in front of the group of children playing ball. The boy pointed to one of the boys in the group, and I immediately recognized him as the one who had apologized to Yuxin.
	I blinked in surprise. "Him?"
	Yao Jie was frowning thoughtfully. "Do you have any evidence?"
	The boy shook his head.
	Yao Jie crouched down so he could talk to the child face to face. "Does that boy over there bully you?"
	The boy nodded.
	Yao Jie straightened. "Until we can figure out who the murderer is for sure, I think it's for the best if we keep both children in the inn."

~

	True to his word, that night we had both boys, as well as the remaining families of three, all in separate inn rooms. Yao Jie locked the doors of each child's room, and the four of us patrolled the halls. Two nights passed without any commotion, but on the third night, the silence was broken.
	The sound of something crashing came from one of the rooms. Yao Jie and I were the closest to the noise, and we sprinted toward the room. Yao Jie fumbled with the keys until finally the lock fell away and the doors flew open. The innkeeper joined us, and the three of us hurried into the room.
	The boy in the baggy clothes was lying on the floor, bleeding onto the wood. Horrified, I hurried forward and knelt by his side. The boy just lifted a shaky hand and pointed toward the open window.
	"Oh no!" Yao Jie exclaimed. "He's climbing through the windows from the outside!" The second the words left his mouth, a commotion sounded from one of the rooms down the hall.
	I desperately turned to the innkeeper. "Can you find him a doctor?"
	The innkeeper nodded.
	A moment later, I was on my feet. I looked to Yao Jie, only to find that he had set his sword aside and dropped to his knees next to the bleeding child. "Go," he called to me. His face was pale.
      I didn't need to be told twice and hurried out the door. When I entered the other room, I found Yuxin with the other boy. Yuxin had tied his hands behind his back, and Weiwei stood guarding the door. The family of three was huddled in the corner of the room, and my gaze fell on the bloodied knife lying on the wood between them.
	I sheathed my sword. "Why are you killing people?"
	The boy just sneered at me from behind the sword Yuxin had placed at his neck. "They say that obsession can turn one into a demon. Let me become a demon and be feared by all!"
	"Why are you killing people?" Yuxin repeated. "Why are you destroying families of three?"
	The boy wiped away the splattered blood on his face with a sleeve. "I still haven't finished my mission."
	I looked at him, pained. "Just how many families do you have to destroy until you've had enough?"
	"All of them!" the boy yelled. "Why couldn't I have had a happy family? My parents didn't want me. They hurt me. So I killed them. I'll kill all of them!"
	"Let's lock him up," I raised my voice to be heard over the boy's screams of "I'll kill you too!" Then I turned to Weiwei. "I think we should find some rope. It's best if he can't run this time."
	We bound the boy tightly and locked him in an unoccupied room. As we stood guard, waiting to hear from Mr. Gu, Weiwei turned to me quietly. "I didn't think the murderer would be a child. But it all makes sense now. All the slashes on that woman's body were no higher than her stomach-no higher than a child's reach. And the shoes . . . once he reached the grass, he must have taken them off. It would have been very difficult to see the marks of his bare feet in the tall grass."
	Suddenly, there was the sound of hurried footsteps, and we saw Mr. Gu hurrying toward us. He came to a stop, clutching his side. "I just finished investigating the two children. Our culprit is named Xiao Ming. Ever since his parents died, he's been living in the orphanage. He bullies the other children there and even steals their personal items. One of the children told me that her fruit knife had been stolen a few months back. Finally, under Xiao Ming's pillow, I found the words happy family scratched there."
	"Who's the other boy?" I decided to ask. My head felt empty.
	"He's Liang Mu, a mute. It seems like he knew early on that Xiao Ming was the murderer but had no way to tell people."
	"He was stabbed multiple times by Xiao Ming," I said tearfully. "Yao Jie's with him right now. Could I trouble you to check and see if he's okay?"
	Mr. Gu nodded. "I'll keep you updated."

~

	Over the next couple of days, the four of us took turns checking on Xiao Ming. "I'm an unwanted child," he was mumbling to himself when it was my turn to bring him food. "I don't want to be an unwanted child. Why not let me die and be reborn as a demon? If I can't have a happy family, I'll make sure no one can have a happy family." I just shook my head as I set the bowl of porridge down on the floor.
      I left the inn and walked through the village until I arrived at the local clinic. I entered to find Yao Jie in the middle of telling an animated story to Liang Mu. Even though the young boy was covered in bandages, his eyes were wide as he intently listened to Yao Jie's every word.
	"And then the hero was rewarded by the townsfolk for his courageousness and kind heart," Yao Jie concluded.
	I let out a laugh as I walked over. "Telling a story about yourself?"
	Yao Jie grinned as he shook his head. "Of course not. Tian Yong's the one who's the hero."
	Liang Mu reached over to tug on Yao Jie's sleeve.
	I smiled. "I think he's trying to say that you're a hero too."
	Liang Mu nodded.
      Yao Jie just smiled as he ruffled the boy's hair. After he rose to his feet and accompanied me outside, I turned to face him. "That day," I said softly, "instead of rushing to capture the culprit, you stayed with Liang Mu."
	Yao Jie let out a sigh. "He was dying. I couldn't just leave him there alone. No one should have to die alone. Death is scary, especially for a child. So I held his hand and tried to provide what comfort I could. Yes, martial artists see death all the time, so much that some of them have become numb to it. I refuse to become like that."
	When I arrived back at the inn, I found Weiwei standing by the entrance. "Where's Yuxin?" I asked.
	"She said she was going to talk to Xiao Ming."
	"Talk to him? Talk to him about what? The villagers are still coming to a consensus about how to deal with him."
	Weiwei just shook her head. "I really don't know."

~

	That evening, Weiwei was delivering food to Xiao Ming when the sound of something breaking echoed through the inn. I sprinted toward the sound, but Yao Jie got there first.
	"What happened?" I asked as I skidded to a stop by the open doorway. Yao Jie stepped forward to block my view of the room beyond. "He's dead," he said shortly.
	I took a step backward in disbelief. "Dead?"
	Yao Jie shut the door once Weiwei had joined me in the hall. Her face was pale, and her shoes were splattered with porridge from the bowl that slipped from her fingers.
	"How did he untie his rope?" Yao Jie mused more to himself than the two of us.
	"Yuxin," Weiwei said quietly.
	Yao Jie blinked at her. "What?"
	"Yuxin was the last person to speak to him."
	"Just because I was the last person to speak to him means I'm guilty?" I turned to find Yuxin standing behind us. Her expression was hurt. "I didn't kill him."
	I opened my mouth to say Yuxin couldn't have killed him, but the words wouldn't come out.
	"Xiyan"-Yuxin turned to look at me-"you believe me, don't you?"
	"Yuxin . . ." I just shook my head. "I don't know what happened."
	Yao Jie let out a sigh after a silence fell between us. "It seems like our job here is done. We already collected the money from Mr. Gu yesterday. I think it's time for us to head back. I'll cover the body. Then it's up to the villagers what they want to do with it."
      During the trip back to Chen Han's residence, a heavy feeling settled over me. I wanted to believe Yuxin, but try as I might, I didn't know what to believe anymore.

    Chapter Eighteen

	The second day after returning to Chen Han's residence, I awoke in the morning to the faint sound of metal clashing against metal. I sat bolt upright and shook Weiwei and Yuxin awake. The three of us jumped to our feet, grabbed our swords, and hurried downstairs. We raced across the grassy yard and finally skidded to a stop at the doors. Yao Jie was already standing there with his hand on the hilt of his sword as he looked out at the action happening beyond.
	"What's going on?" I asked as I hurried over to him.
	"The Fire Sea Abyss members we met before tracked us down," Yao Jie said grimly. "They tried to break in, so now Chen Han is fighting them outside."
	My head snapped over to the doors. "All by herself?"
	Yao Jie nodded. "She told me to stay inside the walls."
	Crimson fabric rippled in the wind, and then Chen Han was striding back through the doors. "Did you all doubt my abilities?"
	"Are they dead?" Yuxin asked hesitantly as she tried to peer outside.
	"They ran away," Chen Han said simply. "They didn't stand a chance against me."
	"What did they want?" I questioned fearfully.
	The heroine in red just shrugged. "They didn't say."
	Yao Jie's tone was worried. "If the Fire Sea Abyss Sect members really did come here for us . . ."
	"The two of you are guests at my house," Chen Han said lightly. "No one's attacking my guests with me around."
	"I still feel a little uneasy," Yao Jie said. "Once Tian Yong can walk again, the two of us will set off immediately for the Owl and Aspen Sect's headquarters. You don't belong to a sect. I don't want you to get caught up in the conflict. I don't want anything to happen to you because of us staying here."
	"Don't worry about it," Chen Han reassured him. "Normal martial artists can't beat me. Once Tian Yong is healed, I'll personally escort you two back to your sect's headquarters."

~

	That night, I lay awake in bed. Weiwei and Yuxin were fast asleep, and I stared through the darkness at the ceiling in silence. Suddenly, I heard a soft creaking sound coming from the floorboards outside. I slowly sat up and squinted through the dark. After climbing to my feet, I quietly slid open the doors and slipped out into the night.
      The moon was high in the sky, and it had to be well past midnight. A chilly wind bit at my nose and ears as I tiptoed along the walkway. As I rounded the corner, I blinked in surprise. Chen Han was leaning against the railings, gazing out at the mountains in the distance. The red ribbons in her hair glowed silver in the light, fluttering gently in the wind.
	"Sister Chen," I whispered. Chen Han turned to face me, and I noticed the dark circles beneath her eyes. I stared at her at a loss for words. "I-" I started. "I thought we had helped you get over your insomnia."
	She let out a tired sigh. "I thought so too. It only recently started to reoccur."
	"Is it because Fei Ziyi isn't here?"
	Chen Han proceeded to pinch the bridge of her nose. "I don't know. It seems like I'm not over this insomnia, after all."
	I walked over to join her at the railing. "Do you think it's something to do with the different martial art sects?"
      Chen Han offered me a faint smile as she shook her head. "You don't have to worry about me. I should be okay again in a few days."
	"Are you sure?"
	"I'm sure. Don't worry about me."
	I let out a sigh. "Alright, I should try and get back to sleep anyway. Goodnight, Sister Chen."
	"Goodnight, Xiyan."
	In the morning, I sat on the front porch with Yao Jie, Weiwei, and Yuxin.
	"How's Tian Yong?" Weiwei asked softly.
	"He seems to be doing fine," Yao Jie informed us. "I told him about what happened with the murder case in that village." A slight smile flickered across Yao Jie's face. "He was proud of how I handled it. He said I've grown up. He's a little disappointed he can't practice his martial arts, that's all. Oh, do you think we could go to the village today? I want to buy him some of those dessert cakes he's always liked. Maybe he'll cheer up then."
	I rose to my feet. "Let's go ask Sister Chen. I don't see why we can't go."
	Sure enough, in a matter of minutes, the four of us were walking down the dirt path.
	"That jade pendant of yours," I said after a while. "It really does seem like it's important to you. Is there a story behind it?"
	"My father gave it to me," Yao Jie said wistfully. "I think it was his before he passed it on to me. It's the only thing I have from my parents. We were from a poor village, and they were the ones who brought me to the Owl and Aspen Sect in the hopes that I'd be able to live a better life than the one they'd given me. Ever since they left me there, I've never seen them again."
	"And how has your life at the Owl and Aspen Sect been?" Weiwei inquired.
	Yao Jie smiled faintly. "All the people that I've met there . . . I don't regret any of my time with them."
