      Before I could open my mouth, there was the sound of the door flying open. In a panic, I whirled to face the door, afraid the storyteller was back already. But it wasn't the storyteller; it was Weiwei.
      "Weiwei!" I exclaimed.
      Weiwei hurried over to me and threw her arms around me in a tight embrace. "Xiyan, where did you go? I was waiting in front of the restaurant, but when you didn't come . . . I found your mask lying on the street and thought the worst had happened."
      "Weiwei," I sniffled as I hugged her back. "I'm sorry. I got lost again."
      Weiwei finally let me go. Her gaze fell on Master Zeng, and she blinked in surprise. "Master Zeng!"
      Master Zeng inclined his head. "Sit, both of you. I have something you might want to hear. It's about your friend, Xia Yuxin." Weiwei's expression was still worried as we sat down, but I gave her a small smile. Together, we listened intently as Master Zeng continued, "Miss Xia has been spotted a few times by members of my sect. She married the pirate lord. I have a handful of Owl and Aspen members stationed by the port. They were keeping an eye on her for many months, but recently, Miss Xia and the pirate lord haven't been seen by the coast anymore. You are not going to like hearing this, but a couple of female martial artists have been found dead, and I suspect Miss Xia had something to do with it."
	I just stared blankly at the table in front of me.
	"Telling you about Miss Xia wasn't the only reason why I've been looking for you," Master Zeng said. His voice drew me out of my spinning thoughts. "Would the two of you consider joining my Owl and Aspen Sect?"
	I blinked. "I-I'm sorry?"
	Master Zeng just smiled. "Everyone's heard about how you saved my sect from falling into the clutches of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect. It would only make sense that I offered you an opportunity to join. So I've been looking for you to formally ask the two of you to join my sect."
	"Can I refuse?" I asked hesitantly.
	"Of course. But I'd at least like to hear the reason."
	I sighed. "Martial art sects and their petty disputes are the reason why my teacher's master died. In respect for my late teacher and how she never joined a sect, I have no plan of joining one in this lifetime either."
	Master Zeng turned to Weiwei. "What about you, though?"
	"Xiyan speaks for both of us," Weiwei said softly. "Sister Chen was also the one who taught me martial arts. I couldn't think of disrespecting her or her master by joining a sect."
      Master Zeng nodded his head. "Well, if you ever change your mind, my offer is always valid. If you ever need anything from our Owl and Aspen Sect, just ask." Just then, a waiter walked by our table. Master Zeng called him over, then turned to Weiwei and me. "What would the two of you like to eat?"
      "You don't have to-" Weiwei and I started at the same time, but Master Zeng just waved us off.
      "It's my treat. I'll just order a few dishes, then."
      When the waiter left, I leaned forward. "You really didn't need to, sir. I'm not even that hungry." But just as the words left my mouth, my stomach gave a loud rumble.
      Master Zeng chuckled. "Don't worry about it."
      After we finished eating, Master Zeng offered to escort us to the entrance of the town. Weiwei and I took him up on the offer, and the three of us weaved our way through the crowded streets. Lanterns flickered and glowed in the night sky above us. Even after we parted ways with Master Zeng and began our journey back to our village, the lights were still visible until the morning sun finally scrubbed them from the sky.
      "Weiwei," I said quietly as we walked down the dirt road. I was wearing my mask but still had to squint against the brightness of the sun.
      "I know," Weiwei said with a sigh. "You want to go looking for Yuxin."
      I nodded silently.
      Weiwei smiled faintly. "If you want to look for Yuxin, let's go look for her together."
    

    Chapter Twenty-Two

	After saying our farewells to the villagers, Weiwei and I left. The two of us had decided to pay a visit to the blacksmith who made our swords, Mr. Fan. If Yuxin really was targeting female martial artists, we would try to find them before she did. And if anyone knew where we might be able to find the locations of martial artists, the blacksmith would be the one to start with.
      It took us many weeks to arrive at the blacksmith's shop. As I walked down those familiar streets and looked up at the buildings, I felt a sharp pang in my chest. I slid my mask off my face with much difficulty and stepped into the shop with Weiwei.
	"Welcome!" a voice called.
	My gaze fell on the figure behind the counter. I had expected Mr. Fan, but instead, a teenage girl with long black hair grinned up at me.
	"Hello," I said. I exchanged a bewildered glance with Weiwei. "Is Mr. Fan in?"
	"Oh, are you looking for my father?" the girl asked thoughtfully. "He's in the back room. He's working, though. If you need anything, you can just ask me."
	"You're Mr. Fan's daughter?" Weiwei questioned.
	The girl nodded. "My name's Fan Wanqi. I'm fifteen, but I know how to run a shop."
	"I don't remember seeing you here the last time I came to your father's store," I noted.
	Fan Wanqi dropped her gaze. "My mother passed away recently. My father doesn't want me to stay home alone, so now I help him out here."
	"I-I'm so sorry."
	The girl just offered me a sad smile. "Anyways, what brings the two of you here today? Maybe I'll be able to help you out."
	"I don't know if you've heard that female martial artists have been dying," Weiwei said heavily. "But the person behind all their deaths is likely someone my friend and I used to know. We can't let them go on like this."
	Fan Wanqi looked up at Weiwei. "So you want to stop them?"
	"Exactly," I answered. "Your father seems to know a lot of people. We were wondering if he knows where any female martial artists are. We feel like it's our responsibility to warn them."
	"My father does know where a lot of them are," Fan Wanqi informed us. Then she smiled. "I know, too."
	The door to the back room opened, and Mr. Fan stepped out. "Qiqi, these customers aren't giving you a hard time, are they?"
	Fan Wanqi shook her head. "Not at all!"
	Mr. Fan stopped next to his daughter and placed a hand on her shoulder, then looked at Weiwei and me. His face split into a grin. "You're Chen Han's disciples! How's your teacher been doing recently?"
	Weiwei and I exchanged a glance. "You haven't heard?" I asked softly. "She . . . she passed away."
	Mr. Fan's grin faltered. "Come again?"
	I dropped my gaze. "She was killed."
	Mr. Fan shook his head in disbelief. "Not Chen Han! But-but how? I heard the rumors, but I didn't actually think they were true." Fan Wanqi placed a consoling hand on her father's arm.
	Weiwei spoke up when I couldn't find the words. "She was poisoned," she said. "Female martial artists have started dying, and we suspect a former friend of ours is behind it. We want to stop her."
	"There's only two of you," Mr. Fan said slowly as he put the pieces together. "That other young woman . . ."
	I tried my best to keep my voice steady. "We've come to you in the hopes that you can tell us where we can find female martial artists. We want to warn them."
	Fan Wanqi tugged on her father's sleeve. "Father, if they're really dying, we can't just sit by and do nothing. We need to help them."
	Mr. Fan looked from his daughter to Weiwei and me, and then back again. "Of course we'll help."
	Fan Wanqi looked at her father hopefully. "I know where Minmin is. She's my friend-I don't want anything bad to happen to her. I can take them to Minmin."
	Mr. Fan seemed to snap out of his daze. "You can't go. There's a killer out there."
	"Only martial artists are dying," Fan Wanqi pleaded. "Please, Father, let me go warn Minmin!"
	"Your mother just passed away. What do I do if something happens to you?"
	"Father," Fan Wanqi said with a faint smile. "I want to explore the world. I want to go on an adventure like all the heroes I hear about in the stories. Minmin said that when I get older, she'd take me with her one day. Just this once, will you let me go?"
	Mr. Fan looked torn. "I know that Heroine Zhao is a dear friend of yours, but-"
	"Father, this must be fate that I finally have a chance to leave the village. Besides, it's not like I'm going alone."
	After looking at his daughter for a long moment, Mr. Fan addressed Weiwei and me. "The two of you have been learning martial arts. I'm counting on you to keep my daughter out of harm's way. I'm afraid that since you've told her about the situation at hand, even if I don't allow her to go with you, she'll figure out a way to run off on her own to warn her friend." He shook his head, but he was smiling faintly. "My daughter's always wanted to leave this village. But I work long hours and can't accompany her. This is her first opportunity to get a sense of the world beyond our village."
	"When do we leave?" Fan Wanqi asked excitedly.
	I smiled faintly at her eagerness. There was something about the girl that reminded me of my old self. "As soon as possible would be ideal."
	"So soon?" Mr. Fan said as Fan Wanqi gave his arm a squeeze. "I fear that if I let you go, you'll be all grown up by the time you return."
	Fan Wanqi just smiled. "Don't worry. You know that Minmin doesn't live on the other side of the world. I'm gonna go on an adventure! When I get back, I won't leave out a single detail when I tell you about it."
	Mr. Fan gave her a smile, but there was something strained in his expression, and worry flickered in his eyes. "You better keep her safe," he finally said.
	Weiwei nodded her head. "We will."
	Fan Wanqi hurried around the counter to stand next to Weiwei and me. "What are your names?" she asked. "Since we're acquaintances now, you can call me Wanqi-or Qiqi if you like."
	"I'm Xia Xiyan," I introduced myself. "My friend here is Hu Qiuwei."
	"Sister Xia." Fan Wanqi looked up at me. Then she turned to Weiwei. "Sister Hu."
      Mr. Fan stepped out from behind the counter as well. He unfastened the dagger hanging from his belt and gently handed it to his daughter. "There's nothing I can do to prevent myself from worrying about you until you return safe and sound. But I'll feel a little better knowing that you have a means of defending yourself."
	Fan Wanqi smiled as she tugged on her father's arm again. "I'll be back in a few weeks. Don't worry."
	After following Fan Wanqi to prepare a few items for the trip, the three of us stood at the exit of the village.
	"This way," Fan Wanqi said as she motioned for us to follow her. "I've never gone to see Minmin before, but I know the location on maps by heart. I've always wanted to visit her."

~

	That night, the three of us set up camp in the heart of a bamboo forest after a long day of walking. After eating a quick dinner, we were all getting ready for bed.
	"I've always wanted to sleep under the stars like this," Fan Wanqi said wistfully as she stared up at the silent night sky. "My parents would never let me sleep outside, though. They said that I'd catch a cold. But I like the outdoors. There's something freeing about it. I want to explore the world before I have to settle down in one place forever." She absently combed her fingers through her hair as she rambled on, "If I leave forever, who's going to take care of my father? I wanted to learn martial arts, but my parents didn't allow it. Sometimes I wonder where I'd be now if I had joined a martial arts sect when I was younger. Would I have seen the world? I've never even been this far from my village before."
	"You're lucky you have a loving father," Weiwei said as she smiled faintly.
	Fan Wanqi nodded along. "I know. That's what Minmin tells me as well."
	"Tell us about Minmin," I said with a small smile. "What kind of person is she?"
	"Minmin is a good friend of mine," Fan Wanqi explained as she rested her chin on the palms of her hands. "I think she's about seven or eight years older than me. She was part of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect for a while. She left them about five years ago, though. She didn't want to deal with all the conflict and pointless skirmishes between the sects. She visited me a lot to complain about them."
	"The Fire Sea Abyss Sect?" I exchanged a glance with Weiwei.
	Fan Wanqi let out a sigh. "I know, the Fire Sea Abyss Sect's reputation isn't very good right now. According to Minmin, there were quite a lot of conflicts happening within the sect that resulted in the more righteous members leaving."
	"She's living in one place now?" I asked. "I thought that most martial artists don't stay in the same place for very long."
	Fan Wanqi smiled knowingly. "You'll see where she's living when we get there."
	Suddenly, there was a rustling in the bamboo, and we turned in the direction of the sound.
	"Look!" Fan Wanqi jumped to her feet and hurried over to the edge of the trees. "I think I just saw the tail of something!" Then she paused. "It ran."
	Weiwei blinked. "You aren't afraid of the beasts in the forest? What if it was a ghost?"
	"I'm afraid of large beasts," Fan Wanqi admitted. Then she placed her hands on her hips, grinning. "But I'm not afraid of ghosts."
	"Not afraid of ghosts? Have you seen ghosts before?"
	"I had an encounter with a ghost once," Fan Wanqi said knowingly as she returned to her seat. "I was less than ten years old at the time. It was night, and I was going to collect the laundry. And then I saw it. Even now I don't know if it was a real ghost or a fake ghost, but it was very ugly and smelled horrible. It saw me and approached me, but I wasn't afraid. Instead, I laughed at it." She giggled at the shocked looks on our faces. "The ghost must have never been laughed at before. I think it was shocked into fleeing! My father said I was very brave," she concluded proudly. "My mother said I was an idiot who doesn't value my life. Let's sleep. We've still got a way to go tomorrow."

~

	With each day that went by in the demon realm, my longing to see the bright world I constantly read about grew. I wanted to see this land of heroes. I wanted to see the sky, the earth, the trees. My presence wasn't really needed here. The demon lord could just shape another demon out of the darkness to take my place.
	I wanted to be a human.
      As the thought entrenched itself in my mind, I found myself taking human form again. This time, I was a princess in a blue dress that flowed like water. I threw my head back as I danced through the fog. What I was doing was against the rules. Low-level demons like me were prohibited from taking on human form. Human forms were reserved for higher-level ghosts and demons; the higher the status of the ghost, the more human they would look. The more powerful they were, the more they could hold onto their original forms and not transform into creatures of nightmare.
	Suddenly, I heard loud whispering from out of the fog. It seemed like the other demons had found me. I narrowed my eyes as I waited for them to emerge from the surrounding haze. But before I could find any of them, the back of my collar was grabbed by a rough claw. The next moment, I was being flown into the air.
	I looked down to see the smokey demons shoot up from the fog, but they were far too slow to keep up with the creature that had just snatched me away. I tilted my head upward to look at the magnificent crane as it carried me away from the prowling demons. "Bifang?"
	"Playing around in human form is no laughing matter," the bird scolded me. "You know the rules of this place as well as I do. You're lucky that the higher ups are too busy dealing with rounding up escaped ghosts to come after you."
	"You also knew the rules of the heavens very well," I said matter-of-factly. "But you still went ahead and stole fire from them anyway."
	Bifang let out a laugh. "The humans wouldn't have survived without it. Look how well they're doing now. Being banished here is nothing."
	We finally landed on a mountain made of solid rock. Bifang gently set me down before arranging its turquoise and crimson feathers. I turned around to look at the bird. "You shouldn't have to spend your life here. I have an idea-you should do something naughty again and get yourself banished to the human realm! The human realm must be better than this place."
	Bifang leveled me a look. "You can't say that for certain. I've been to the human realm many times before. Humans are unpredictable. At least here, you know what to expect from the ghosts."
	I let out a dejected sigh.
	Bifang was kind enough to indulge me for the rest of the day. For a while I acted out my story for the one-legged bird, switching back and forth between the beautiful maiden and the brave hero. When I finished the story, Bifang let me climb onto its back and we flew around the demon realm for some time. Finally, Bifang set me down on the ground. "I'm afraid this is where we have to part, for now."
	I nodded my head sadly as I reverted to my original form. "Thank you for today, Bifang. I wish there was a way for us to leave this place together."
	"It's not that bad," Bifang said mildly. "Things could always be worse; at least we're not locked in cages like all those souls undergoing their punishments."
	The bird did have a point. "I wish we could spend more time together, but I know you're busy."
	"I make time for you, don't I?"
	I laughed. "Thank you, Bifang. I'll see you soon."
	I watched the bird spread its exquisite wings before it took off and soared into the air. And just like that, I was alone again. Maybe I would go to the library today after all.

~

	In the morning, we were off on our way again. After a long week of walking, Fan Wanqi stopped to point up at the small forested hill in front of us. "That's where Minmin lives," she said proudly.
	I followed her gaze to the structure peeking out from between the trees. "A temple?"
	Fan Wanqi nodded. "She helps out there, and in exchange, the monks give her a room to stay in."
	Weiwei and I followed Fan Wanqi as we began our ascent up the hill. The entire hill was shrouded in fog, and as we drew closer to the top, the path behind us vanished into the haze. I looked up in awe as we passed beneath the main gate. When we finally arrived in front of the main building, I hesitated as I lingered outside the entrance. "Are we allowed to walk in like this?"
	"I don't see why not," Fan Wanqi said thoughtfully. "Temples like this are always open to the public during the day."
	"How about we pray first?" Weiwei suggested. "That way, we won't have to feel as awkward about wandering around the temple afterward."
	"Good idea," I agreed.
	The three of us stepped inside, and I looked up at the altar. There was something powerful about the large Buddha sculpture that sat in the middle of it, and I found it difficult to look away. The hall itself was empty save for a young man kneeling on the floor in front of the altar, pressing his hands together in prayer.
	Fan Wanqi stepped forward and silently motioned for Weiwei and me to kneel as well. Looking up at the Buddha sculpture, I pressed my hands together and shut my eyes. Please help Yuxin get back on the right path, I prayed. Please keep her safe.
	After a long moment, I opened my eyes and slowly rose to my feet. The chamber here was silent, and the only movement came from the flickering of the candles and the smoke from the incense. I looked at the young man was still kneeling in prayer as Weiwei and Fan Wanqi stood up. Taking a silent step forward, I leaned forward to get a glimpse of the man's face. There was just something too familiar about him. "Tian Yong?"
	Tian Yong's eyes fluttered open in surprise. "Xia Xiyan?" His eyes widened as they fell on Weiwei as well. "Hu Qiuwei? What are the two of you doing here?"
	"We could ask you the same thing," I said weakly. "This is a pleasant surprise."
	Tian Yong rose to his feet and motioned for us to follow him outside. Back out in the open, he turned around to face us. "I've been coming here a lot recently. Being at the temple makes me feel more at ease."
	"Are you still part of the Owl and Aspen Sect?" Weiwei asked. "I didn't recognize you at first-you're not wearing the same tawny brown as before."
	Tian Yong looked down at his black clothes. "I'm still a member. I'm just taking some time away. Ever since we parted, I did my best to search for Yao Jie's jade pendant. I found it within a month and buried it next to his grave. After that, I asked for some time away from the sect. And now I'm here."
	"Are the three of you friends?" Fan Wanqi asked curiously.
	Tian Yong nodded as he smiled faintly at the girl. "You could say we're old friends. I'm Tian Yong from the Owl and Aspen Sect. Who might you be?"
	"My name's Fan Wanqi," Fan Wanqi said. "I'm leading Sister Xia and Sister Hu to meet my friend Minmin."
	Tian Yong blinked. "Zhao Minmin?"
	Fan Wanqi looked up with large eyes. "You also know Minmin?"
	"I've been coming here for nearly half a year," Tian Yong said matter-of-factly. "Of course I know Miss Zhao."
	"Brother Tian, can you take us to her?" Fan Wanqi asked eagerly.
	"Miss Zhao tends to be busy until nightfall," Tian Yong informed us. "If you want to see her, you'll have to stick around for a while."
	"We don't mind," I said.
	Tian Yong smiled. "It's been a while since I've seen old friends. How about I give you a tour of the temple, and then we head down to the village at the base of the hill? We've still got quite a few hours until it gets dark, and I want to treat all of you to dinner."
	The three of us followed Tian Yong the areas of the temple that were open to the public before starting on our way back down the path. As we descended the hill, we passed a good amount of people making the trek up. As we passed them, some of the people greeted Tian Yong, and he paused for a short time to chat with them.
	"You seem to know everyone here," Weiwei said in awe as we continued on our way again.
	"I've gotten to know the regulars," Tian Yong said with a faint smile.
	When we reached the bottom of the hill, Tian Yong led us around the backside and into the small town. The four of us sat down at an outdoor noodle shop, and Tian Yong ordered each of us a bowl.
	"It's really good to see you again, Tian Yong," I said as we waited for our food to arrive. "It's nice to see a familiar face."
	Tian Yong inclined his head. "I'm glad to see the two of you as well. I'm glad to see that you're still traveling together."
	I exchanged a glance with Weiwei. "I presume you know what happened to Chen Han?"
	Tian Yong nodded sadly. "It was disheartening to hear the news. Heroine Chen did so much for me when I got injured. And Xia Yuxin . . . I never thought she'd become one of the pirate lord's wives."
	I let out a breath. "So you already know everything. Then you must have already guessed why we want to see Zhao Minmin."
	"Is the reason why you've stayed near the temple for so long because of Miss Zhao?" Weiwei asked.
	Tian Yong looked away sheepishly. "Yes, partially."
	The cook arrived at our table and placed a bowl in front of each of us.
	"Eat." Tian Yong smiled awkwardly as he motioned to our food. "I'm a man of my word; I'll take the three of you to see Miss Zhao once she finishes her work for the day."
	"Brother Tian," Fan Wanqi said in a whisper. "Your face is red. Are you blushing?"
	"What?" Tian Yong put his hands to his face in surprise.
	Fan Wanqi just smiled as she rested her chin on the palms of her hands. "Do you like Minmin?"
	Tian Yong picked up his chopsticks and poked at the noodles in his bowl. "I'll be honest with you; Zhao Minmin and I are together."
	"Really?" I looked up excitedly. "That's great!"
	"I'm happy for the two of you," Weiwei said with a smile.
	"No wonder Minmin hasn't come to visit me lately," Fan Wanqi remarked with a laugh. "I was starting to worry about her, but it turns out I've got nothing to worry about after all!"
	Tian Yong smiled faintly. "I know you're probably wondering how it happened. It's true that the Fire Sea Abyss Sect is responsible for Yao Jie's death, but it's unfair to pin the blame on people who don't even know about the incident. At first I didn't even know Minmin was from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect. I could tell that she was a martial artist, but her style was different than anything I'd seen from the Fire Sea Abyss Sect. She could tell that I was a martial artist as well, and she could also tell that I wasn't in a great place mentally. I told her that my best friend had just passed away, and she tried her best to support me."
	"That sounds exactly like something Minmin would do," Fan Wanqi said with a nod. "If the two of you continue to stay together, I bet you'll see a lot more of me. Minmin says that I'm practically her little sister. And if you end up marrying her, I'll practically be your sister-in-law!"
	Tian Yong's face was very red at this point. "I think it's still a little too soon to start thinking about a wedding."
	Fan Wanqi gave Tian Yong an embarrassed smile. "I'm sorry. I think I got a little overly excited."
	"But," Tian Yong continued, more confidently this time, "I did propose to her. And she said yes."
	Fan Wanqi let out a delighted squeal at that.
	When the four of us finished our dinners and congratulations, Tian Yong led us back up the hill. By this time, the sun had dropped from the sky, and the path was dark. The glow of lanterns flickered out of the fog at the top of the path, and soon we were passing beneath the main gate again.
	Tian Yong led us around to the back of the temple, where a number of monks and nuns were sweeping. They briefly looked up as Tian Yong passed, then went back to their sweeping. At the corner of the courtyard-like space, a young woman with long black hair stood out from the rest as she purposefully swept leaves off of the path.
	"Minmin!" Fan Wanqi rushed forward.
	Zhao Minmin looked up in surprise at the sound of her name, and her face split into a smile. "Little Qi!"
	Fan Wanqi threw her arms around Zhao Minmin. The latter laughed as she swept the girl into her arms and twirled her around.
	"Minmin," Fan Wanqi said when Zhao Minmin finally set her back down on her feet, "I've missed you. Turns out you've been staying here because of Brother Tian."
	Zhao Minmin hid her smile behind a hand. "I see that you've met Tian Yong." Then she turned to look at Weiwei and me. "Are the two of you Little Qi's friends?"
	"These are my new friends, Sister Xia and Sister Hu," Fan Wanqi explained.
	"I'm Xia Xiyan," I said.
	"And I'm Hu Qiuwei," Weiwei added.
	"I'm happy to meet the two of you." Zhao Minmin saluted both of us in turn. "I'm Zhao Minmin. But Little Qi's probably already told you that."
	"Minmin," Fan Wanqi said, "I've come here to warn you."
	Zhao Minmin glanced around to make sure no one was listening in on our conversation. "Is this about the martial artists who've been dying?"
	"We're worried that you could be targeted eventually," I said heavily. "The one suspected of doing the killing is my sister, Xia Yuxin. She's involved with the pirate lord."
	After a long pause, Tian Yong said, "I don't get it. Why is Xia Yuxin killing female martial artists?"
	I dropped my gaze. "I don't fully understand it either."
	Zhao Minmin glanced around at the monks and nuns slowly dispersing from the courtyard. "Let's continue this conversation in my room. I've come here to work, not to bring trouble to the people who work here."
	We followed Zhao Minmin out of the courtyard and down a moss-covered stone path. We finally arrived at a large wooden building, and from there, Zhao Minmin led us down a hallway to one of the many doors. She invited us inside, and we all shuffled in.
	Tian Yong lit the candles, and soon the room glowed with a warm, fiery light. In the light, I realized that Zhao Minmin wasn't wearing the same robe as the monks and nuns at the temple. Instead, she was dressed in a simple, plain-colored outfit.
	"I'm essentially security," Zhao Minmin explained when she caught me looking. "But there hasn't been any sort of conflict since I started working here. I just help with maintenance now."
	"How long have you been practicing martial arts?" Weiwei inquired curiously.
	Zhao Minmin took a seat on her bed. "Ever since I could walk."
	"Heroine Zhao really is an admirable opponent," Tian Yong said as he took a seat next to her. "I don't think I've ever won against her."
	"That's because you keep losing on purpose," Zhao Minmin said with a laugh. "When have you ever fought me seriously?"
	Tian Yong was laughing now too. "Alright, you've got me."
	Zhao Minmin let out a sigh as her smile faded. "I thought that by staying here at this temple, whoever was hunting the other female martial artists wouldn't find me. But judging by the fact that the three of you have found me here, my presence isn't exactly a secret. Tian Yong and I had planned to settle down together in the village at the base of the hill, but when he heard that female martial artists were dying, we both thought it would be safer for me to hide here for the time being."
	"I only know where you are because you told me," Fan Wanqi said. "I don't think anyone besides me would know-"
	"A few members of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect know that I'm here," Zhao Minmin said with a frown. "As long as more than one person knows, I'm bound to be found eventually. For the sake of keeping the monks and nuns out of harm's way, if I'm going to be hunted, I should leave the temple." Then she paused as she turned to Weiwei and me. "As a precaution, could either of you tell me what Xia Yuxin looks like?"
	I took a breath before reaching up and unfastening my mask with deadly steady hands. "She looks like me."
    

    Chapter Twenty-Three

	"Your face-" Tian Yong inhaled sharply. "What happened?"
	I dropped my gaze. "It was Fei Ziyi. After my teacher's death, it was too painful for him to look at me and be reminded of her killer."
	Tian Yong just shook his head. "I can't believe he actually went as far as scarring your face."
	I let out a sigh as I put my mask back on.
	A silence fell between us, and Zhao Minmin spoke up. "It's getting late. You should probably head back down the hill before it starts raining. I was watching the clouds earlier."
	I made my way over to the door. "We won't bother you anymore tonight, then."
	"Tomorrow I'll inform the monks that I'm leaving," Zhao Minmin said as she rose to her feet. "I'll meet you at the gates at noon. I can show you out."
	"You don't need to," I said quickly. "I think we remember the way."
	Zhao Minmin smiled faintly. "I'll let Tian Yong take it from here. He can show you to the village."
	"I imagine the three of you don't have a place to stay for the night," Tian Yong said as he stood up. "You're welcome to stay at my place for the night. My house is a little small, but at least that way you don't have to spend any money."
	Weiwei bowed her head in his direction. "Thank you."
	Finally, Tian Yong turned to Zhao Minmin. "I'll see you tomorrow, then."
	Zhao Minmin smiled at him. "I'll see you tomorrow."
	Once we started off on the path down the hill, Fan Wanqi turned to Tian Yong. "I think you and Minmin are perfect," she said. "I can tell that you really love her."
	"I do," Tian Yong said, and determination sparked in his eyes. "The two of us think it's about time for us to withdraw from the martial arts world and settle down. I was planning to inform the Owl and Aspen Sect about my withdrawal, but until the word gets out that female martial artists have stopped being hunted, I think it's good to be able to fall back on their support. For the longest time, martial arts was my life. But after I met Minmin, I realized that I didn't want to live that sort of dangerous life anymore."
	I clasped my hands behind my back. "I wish the two of you happiness." Maybe not all of us could have the happy ending we envisioned, but I prayed with everything I had that Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin could.
      When we reached Tian Yong's house, Fan Wanqi flopped down on the floor in exhaustion. I tugged my hair out of its ponytail before lying down next to her. Finally, I unfastened my mask and stared up at the ceiling. I thought my head would be spinning as I tried to process everything, but instead, I just felt blank. Empty. Numb. I was tired, I decided.
      Weiwei appeared in my line of vision with a blanket in hand. She laid it over Fan Wanqi and me before taking a seat on the wooden floor. "Are you feeling alright?" she asked softly.
      I nodded absently. "I really hope Yuxin doesn't try to do anything bad to Minmin."
      "Yuxin won't get to her," Weiwei reassured me. "We'll be by Minmin's side. Tian Yong will be there too, and if it comes down to a fight, Yuxin doesn't stand a chance against the two of them together."
      "I'm just worried," I whispered. "I don't want there to be any more death-any more sadness. I just want Minmin and Tian Yong to live happily. And Yuxin . . . I don't want her hurt or sad either."
      "Xiyan, Qiuwei." Tian Yong emerged from the room in the back. "I was just about to offer the three of you my room."
      "It's fine," I said with a smile. Then I put a finger to my lips. "Wanqi's sleeping."
      "I'll leave you be, then," Tian Yong said quietly. "Goodnight."
      "Goodnight."
      Tian Yong disappeared, and I returned to staring up at the ceiling. If Yuxin truly was killing female martial artists, then I was bound to meet Yuxin at some point if I stuck around with Zhao Minmin. And when I do run into her . . . I closed my eyes and lay there for a very long time.
      "Xiyan," Weiwei's voice said softly after a while. "Are you still awake?"
      When I didn't answer, Weiwei fell silent. Weiwei was worried enough about me already. I didn't need her to worry about me anymore.
      
~

      In the morning, the four of us sat around Tian Yong's small wooden table. "I woke up early," Tian Yong informed us. "After asking around in the village, I found out that the latest reported death of a female martial artist took place in a town not too far from Jingcheng."
      "The capital?" I looked up from my food.
      "There's probably a large number of female martial artists there," Tian Yong said grimly.
      "We could either make our way toward Jingcheng in the hopes that we meet her midway," Weiwei said slowly, "or we have you and Minmin go in the opposite direction. Maybe you can avoid her completely."
      "Zhao Minmin and I are both martial artists," Tian Yong said. "When there's injustice, we will face it head on."
      "I want to come too," Fan Wanqi said determinedly. "I want to help out."
      "We promised your father that we'd bring you back home after we saw Minmin," Weiwei said with a sigh. "We'll be dropping you off on our way."
      Fan Wanqi's face fell. "But-"
      "No 'buts,'" I said sternly. "It's safer this way."
      Fan Wanqi just dropped her gaze to the table.
      After we finished our breakfast, the four of us made our way back to the temple at the top of the hill. The path was damp and muddy from the night's rain. We waited by the front gate, and I watched the leaves in the trees sway back and forth in the breeze.
      Fan Wanqi let out a sigh as she stared up at the sky. "I understand that my father works very hard to support the two of us, but sometimes I wish we could move away from that small town. There's still so much I haven't seen."
      Tian Yong bent down so he could talk to the girl at eye level. "Have you told your father this before?"
      "I have," Fan Wanqi said, "but my father says our life is very stable at the moment. I know he wants me to be safe and happy, but sometimes I wish someone would appear in front of me and say, 'Come, Qiqi. Take my hand, and I'll take you on an adventure.'" She smiled sadly. "No one has."
      "You just need to wait a little longer," I said softly. "Someone will show up if you wait long enough."
      Fan Wanqi just shook her head. "I used to think that way. My mother wanted to see the world too, but she never got the chance. She was born in that village and never left it. I know she wanted to wander, but she stayed because of me. Before she died, she told me to go out and see the world for her. Even if she never got the chance, she hoped that I'd be able to go for the both of us.
      "I know my father just wants us to be safe. I understand where he's coming from-he knows a lot of martial artists and how dangerous the martial arts world is. But I don't think I can just sit around at home knowing there's a whole world out there."
      Tian Yong smiled at Fan Wanqi. "How about Minmin and I talk to your father? After we find Xia Yuxin and make sure she's stopped killing, the two of us can take you around with us. We can take you wherever you want to go."
      Fan Wanqi's eyes lit up. "You'd really do that?"
      Tian Yong nodded. "There's still some places Minmin and I want to see before we settle down in one place. You're her best friend, after all. I'm sure she would love to spend more time with you after I've made her hide out in the temple for so long."
      "Did I hear my name?" Everyone turned around to watch Zhao Minmin pass under the gate.
      "Minmin!" Fan Wanqi waved at her friend.
      "Little Qi!" Zhao Minmin wrapped her arms around Fan Wanqi in a warm embrace. "Did Tian Yong give you enough for breakfast?"
      Fan Wanqi smiled. "Of course!"
      "You live relatively close to the village here," Zhao Minmin said as she helped brush loose strands of hair away from Fan Wanqi's face. "You should come and visit us more often."
      Fan Wanqi nodded contently. "Brother Tian said you can take me to travel around after you find Xia Yuxin."
      Zhao Minmin patted the girl on the head. "All you need to do is ask. We can take you anywhere you want to go."
      "Are we ready to head off?" Tian Yong asked.
      Zhao Minmin touched the sword strapped to her back. "I've got everything I need."
      Fan Wanqi and Zhao Minmin chatted happily as we made our way down the hill. The journey back to Fan Wanqi's village was long, but it seemed to go by quickly.
      
~

	"Father!" Fan Wanqi called. We had just entered Mr. Fan's blacksmith shop, and the four of us lingered by the doorway as Fan Wanqi rushed forward.
	Mr. Fan stepped out from behind the counter to greet his daughter with open arms. "You're back!" Then he looked over Fan Wanqi's head. "Heroine Zhao! It's been long over a year since I've seen you last! How have you been?"
	"I've been doing great," Zhao Minmin said with a smile, and her eyes sparkled as she looked over at Tian Yong. "I've got a fianc  now."
	Mr. Fan grinned. "Congratulations you two! Who might this lucky man be?"
	"This is Tian Yong," Minmin said. "And this is Mr. Fan, the blacksmith."
	Mr. Fan bowed his head. "It's a pleasure to meet you."
	Tian Yong returned the gesture. "Likewise."
	Mr. Fan turned to address Weiwei and me. "And thank you for keeping my daughter safe."
	I smiled faintly. "Of course."
	"Will the four of you stay for dinner?" Mr. Fan asked hopefully. "I close my shop late, but I want to treat you all to a meal."
	"Our apologies, Mr. Fan," Zhao Minmin said regretfully. "But we've got an agenda that shouldn't be delayed."
	"Oh," Mr. Fan said disappointedly. "I understand. I wouldn't want to keep you from doing what you need to do. I wish you safe travels."
	"Stay safe!" Fan Wanqi called after us as the four of us made our way toward the door.
	I lingered in the doorway and waved to the girl.
	Fan Wanqi waved back with sad eyes. As I stepped out onto the street beyond, I felt a pang in my chest. Fan Wanqi was still waiting for a chance to see the world. We're all waiting for things, I realized. We're all waiting for things we might never get. I was waiting for the old Yuxin to return, but the more I thought about it, the more I realized that the next time I saw her, she would be far from the person I had once known.

~

	"I've asked around," Zhao Minmin informed us as we regrouped at the entrance to the small village we were passing through. "I'm afraid that Xia Yuxin has her eyes set on another target."
	"What did you hear about this martial artist?" I asked quickly.
	"Her last name is Su," Zhao Minmin recalled. "She belongs to one of the smaller martial arts sects: the Wandering Fox Sect."
	Weiwei frowned faintly. "I've never heard of the Wandering Fox Sect before."
	I shook my head. "Me neither."
	"The Wandering Fox Sect isn't well known," Tian Yong said. "But even if the sect itself isn't known, all of us martial artists have heard about Miss Su at some point in time. She's the Wandering Fox Sect's ace."
	"If she's really that good, why doesn't she join a more well-known sect?" I inquired.
	"It just so happens that her father is the leader of the Wandering Fox Sect," Tian Yong answered. "I don't think she's going to leave them any time soon."
	"Is she in the capital right now?" Weiwei questioned.
	"She's on her way there," Zhao Minmin said. "We should try to catch up to her before she runs into Xia Yuxin."
	The four of us continued down the path, and for the sake of time, we found a place to rent horses in the next village down. Whenever we reached a new town, we'd split into groups and search it as quickly as we could. Instead of asking around about Yuxin, we determined that it was better to ask about Miss Su. No one knew what Yuxin looked like, but on the other hand, many more people were familiar with the martial artist of the Wandering Fox Sect.
	I stopped one of the villagers walking down the street. "Excuse me, ma'am," I said breathlessly. "Do you know if a Miss Su has passed through here? She's a martial artist belonging to the Wandering Fox Sect."
	"Su?" The woman furrowed her brow. "Do you mean Su Yao?"
	"Yes, exactly!"
	The woman let out a heavy sigh. "Apparently, she was found dead a few days ago."
	My heart sank. "Do you know where she was found?"
	"If you keep following the road to Jingcheng, you'll find the town."
	When I regrouped with the other three, they seemed to have all heard the news as well.
	"What do we do now?" I whispered. "Now that Heroine Su is dead, Yuxin will be on the move again."
	"If she needs a target," Zhao Minmin said slowly, "let's give her a target."
	"You?" Weiwei asked, shocked. "We can't let you-"
	"It will be fine," Zhao Minmin reassured her. "It's not like I'm going to meet her alone; the three of you will be with me."
      We decided to set up camp in one of the forests outside of town, and over the next couple of days, Zhao Minmin took on a number of jobs in the area, announcing her presence and spreading the story that she was on her way to Jingcheng.
      One night, as we were sitting around the fire, Zhao Minmin said, "I hope this plan will work." The chill was beginning to set in despite the flames. "Even though it's been a few years since I left the Fire Sea Abyss Sect, I was regarded as one of their top members. My name should still have some weight."
      Tian Yong took Zhao Minmin's hand. "I think it will work. And that's why you're going to have to be especially careful."
      Zhao Minmin tiredly rested her head on Tian Yong's shoulder. "I met Miss Su once when I was younger. I remember it was a cold winter day, and I had been punished to kneel in the snow. I can't remember what I was being punished for, but the moment my punishment was over, Miss Su hurried over to me with a cup of hot tea for me to drink. I think the master of the Wandering Fox Sect was meeting with the master of the Fire Sea Abyss Sect that day. Miss Su was kind. I want to find justice for her."
      "My late friend used to do the same for me whenever I got in trouble," Tian Yong reminisced with a faint smile.
      I stared at Tian Yong. "I can't imagine you getting in trouble."
      Zhao Minmin interjected knowingly, "He was a little bit of a troublemaker." 
      "I used to be a little immature and reckless," Tian Yong admitted. "I loved practicing martial arts, but I didn't enjoy many of the other classes we had to take. Let's just say that those teachers and I didn't have the best relationship. They were always angry at me because they knew I could excel if I applied myself, but I was stubborn and refused. Fortunately, I grew out of that phase around the age of twelve."
      "That reminds me a little bit of my life at the palace," I recalled. "Weiwei was always doing her best to keep me out of trouble." Then I brought the focus of the conversation back to our mission. "Anyways, if we do run into Yuxin, I hope that I'll be able to talk to her and convince her to stop. If she doesn't want to listen, we can tie her up and wait until she does. At least that way she won't be able to hurt anyone else."
      "Maybe we can deal with Yuxin by herself," Weiwei pointed out, "but then what do we do if the pirate lord is there too?"
      "Then we run and try to think of a different plan," Zhao Minmin said with a sigh. "I'm afraid his martial arts is at the same level as Master Huang and Master Zeng. But people know what the pirate lord looks like. If he really was near the capital, we would have heard about it by now."
	I let out a breath. "I really hope Yuxin can come back."
	Weiwei just placed a reassuring hand on my shoulder.

~

	The following day, the three of us arrived at the town where Su Yao from the Wandering Fox Sect had died. Weiwei and I bought veiled hats at the first store we could find. If Yuxin was here, it would be best if she didn't recognize us immediately. As we walked around, Tian Yong held up a portrait he had drawn of Yuxin, asking anyone he could if they'd seen someone similar to the young woman in the painting.
	By the time night began to caress the land with its quiet darkness, we finally got a lead. Apparently, Yuxin had been repeatedly spotted hanging around a restaurant in the center of town every morning. After locating and identifying the restaurant, we decided to get a room at an inn a short distance down the street. We discussed our next steps and went to bed, but I spent the entire night lying awake. By the time morning came, I had not gotten a wink of sleep.
	Tian Yong and I stood outside the entrance to the restaurant. "Ready?" he asked.
	I nodded as I looked up through the veil of my hat. I was wearing Zhao Minmin's clothes, and even the sword at my side was not my own. Today, I was Zhao Minmin.
	The real Zhao Minmin had taken my mask and was guarding the back entrance of the restaurant. And to make our act more convincing, Tian Yong would accompany me inside. Once we entered the restaurant, we were immediately greeted by one of the staff members and shown to a table. I glanced around at the customers sitting at the tables. None of them were Yuxin.
	The staff member seated the two of us at a table toward the back of the restaurant and hurried back to greet the new customers who had appeared in the doorway. From my new vantage point, I scanned the faces in the restaurant again. No Yuxin. I frowned to myself and turned to watch the young women in flowy pink dresses twirl on the stage on the opposite side of the room.
      The longer we waited, the more my confidence began to ebb away. I watched the entrance the entire time, but there was still no sign of Yuxin. Tian Yong was watching the back entrance, and the door hadn't opened once.
	We stayed at the restaurant for hours, but ultimately, Yuxin didn't show up. All we could do was leave and try our luck the next day. As we passed by Weiwei, who was watching the entrance from a short distance down the street, I subtly shook my head. Weiwei dipped her head once before turning to inform Zhao Minmin.
	We tried again for the next couple of days, and by the fourth day, I was starting to worry that Yuxin had seen through us. But on the fifth day, something felt different. This time, Tian Yong and I ended up at a table close to the stage. It was only after we had ordered our food and were halfway through our meal that I noticed the restaurant was emptier than usual. Then, I suddenly realized the front door was closed. While I initially thought this was due to the strong winds outside, upon closer inspection, it seemed like it had been locked from the inside.
	But I had been watching the door the entire time . . . when had someone locked it? Then it hit me: the staff member who had shown us to our table! I quickly scanned the restaurant for him, but he had vanished.
	I slowly rose to my feet. Tian Yong gave me a worried look, but I motioned for him to stay where he was. My fingers curled around the sheath of the sword at my side as I swiftly made my way toward the door. It was indeed locked; someone had put a piece of wood through the handles to keep it from opening. I frowned as I pried the wood from the door and quietly set it on the floor.
	When I turned back around, a dancer I had not seen before was making her way toward Tian Yong. Her magenta skirts fluttered around her feet as she walked. By the time I returned to the table, the dancer had taken my seat. Her eyes glittered as she looked up at me and smiled. "Zhao Minmin, I presume?"
      I stared at her. It was Yuxin.

    Chapter Twenty-Four

	"I'm sorry," Tian Yong said as he offered Yuxin a polite smile. Judging from his tense posture, I knew he had recognized Yuxin through her layers of heavy makeup. "Can we help you?"
	Yuxin just giggled as she lifted one of her flowing sleeves to hide her painted lips. Her eyes landed on me. "I've heard a lot about you, Miss Zhao."
	I remained silent as I stared down at Yuxin through my opaque veil.
	"Miss Zhao-" Yuxin playfully reached forward with a slender hand.
	Tian Yong was there in an instant and caught Yuxin's wrist before she could reach my veil. "Do I know you from somewhere?" he asked. "I could have sworn that we've met before."
	Yuxin laughed as she dropped her hand back to her side. "I'm afraid we haven't." Then Yuxin turned back to me. She rose to her feet and made to step around Tian Yong. "Miss Zhao, would you care to follow me-"
	"I'm sorry, miss," Tian Yong interrupted. "Heroine Zhao isn't going anywhere."
	I glanced over at the stage to find that all the other young women who had formerly been dancing there had spread out to the different tables. Since all of them were entertaining the customers, no one gave Yuxin a second glance.
	Yuxin was still smiling. "That's alright. Then how would you like to come with me instead?"
	Tian Yong's expression was serious as he pried Yuxin's hands off him. "What do you want with us?"
	"What do I want?" Yuxin echoed. "I don't want anything really . . ." But just as the words left her mouth, she whirled and made another snatch for my veil.
	Tian Yong caught Yuxin's wrist with one hand, and the other went to the hilt of his sword as a warning.
	Yuxin just gave him a smile. "If I don't see the woman behind the veil, how do I know if she really is Zhao Minmin?"
	"Yuxin," I said firmly, speaking up for the first time. I reached up and brushed aside my veil. "You're right. I'm not Zhao Minmin."
	Yuxin's eyes widened in surprise as she stared at me. "Xiyan? What happened to your face?" Concern flashed in her eyes as she reached toward me, but I folded my arms over my chest.
      "Yuxin, just what is it that you want? I don't understand. I thought you never wanted to hurt again. And yet you went and joined hands with the pirate lord. I can only imagine how he's been treating you."
	Yuxin let out a sad laugh as she let her hand fall back to her side. "Yes, I sold myself to the pirate lord."
	"You're killing female martial artists," I said painfully. "Yuxin, why? I know what you did back in Jingcheng. After Sister Chen died, Brother Gao wrote to us. He uncovered the fact of how you rose to fame so quickly there because you killed all your competitors."
	"Brother Gao told you all of that?" Yuxin looked up at the ceiling, taking a deep breath to center herself. "I won't lie to you. I don't want to lie to you. I did kill them."
	"Why?" I whispered.
	Yuxin let out a soft sigh as she met my gaze. "Xiyan, you're the only one who truly knows me. I'm nothing more than a cursed girl, fated to be broken again and again. I've come to realize it's my heart that's been getting in the way of obtaining what I really want. My emotions are getting in the way of my goals. At the brothel, I thought that dream was gone for good. When Young Master Wen bought my freedom, I didn't care about the dream anymore. But now it's the only thing I can hold onto. I'm going to be the female hero who subdues the demon. All I've ever wanted was to be loved. All I ever wanted was to be respected. No one's ever played nice with me. I've long been stained with blood. They mistreated me. They made me suffer-they made me live a life worse than death! Is it wrong to want revenge?"
	I just stared at her as she pulled up one of the empty seats at our table. "Yuxin . . ."
	Yuxin smiled faintly as she sat down. "It's been a while since we've last seen each other, Xiyan." She reached across the table for my hand, but I moved it out of her reach. Something flickered behind her eyes, but her smile remained as she let her hand fall back to her side. "How have you and Weiwei been?"
	A frown tugged at my lips. "I didn't think you gave either of us any thought since you left."
	"You're still my sister," Yuxin said softly. "How could I not think about you?"
	"Sister Chen was a sister to you too! Yuxin"-I shook my head as I blinked back tears-"I don't understand. Why do you need to hurt so many people?"
	Yuxin's eyes were pained. "I told you my story. I thought you of all people would understand. You're my sister. But it turns out in the end, you don't understand. You don't understand me at all. I keep making the same mistakes, Xiyan. What's wrong with me? Young Master Wen, Brother Gao, you . . . all of you are just distractions. I've put my faith in the wrong people time and time again. I've come to realize that I can only rely on myself.
      "After we parted ways, I encountered the pirate lord by chance. I sold myself to him, and he brought me back to his ship. His other wives tried to kill me, so I killed them. Everything I've done was to survive. He thought I was ruthless and that we were a match made in heaven. He was willing to teach me everything Sister Chen wasn't. I told him I wanted to be the most famous female martial artist in the land, and he agreed to help me make my wish come true."
	"If you continue down this path," I said quietly, "people won't speak your name in praise. They'll be whispering it in fear. Yuxin-" All of a sudden, the doors to the restaurant burst open. My head snapped around as my eyes fell on the figure standing in the doorway. It was Fan Wanqi.
      "Sister Xia! Brother Tian!" she panted as she rushed toward us. She skidded to a stop in front of us, hands on her knees as she tried to catch her breath. "I've come here to warn you!"
	"Warn us of what?" Tian Yong asked quickly.
	"His name's Fei Ziyi," Fan Wanqi gasped out. "He's here! He came to my father's shop to buy weapons and ranted that he was going to kill Xia Yuxin. My father and I tracked you down and raced here as fast as we could. But we're no match for Fei Ziyi. My father's got him distracted for now, but Fei Ziyi will be here soon!"
	Yuxin let out a laugh. "So Fei Ziyi wants to kill me now." She reached to pour herself a glass of wine, but I grabbed her wrist and swiftly rose to my feet.
      "We should go. Quickly now."
	"You're trying to protect me?" Yuxin blinked in surprise.
	I let out a breath. "I don't want you to die."
	Tian Yong turned to address Fan Wanqi. "You and your father are both here?"
	The girl nodded. "My father feels like he owes you a favor. None of you are a match for Fei Ziyi if it comes down to a fight, and he doesn't want you to get hurt."
	Tian Yong furrowed his brow. "It's true we're not on Fei Ziyi's level alone. But if Zhao Minmin and I work together, I think we should be able to win against him."
	"Come on," I said quickly as I turned to Yuxin. "We need to get you out of here. Here"-I pulled off my veil hat and set it on her head-"wear this."
	"Did you see Qiuwei on the way in?" Tian Yong asked Fan Wanqi.
	"Sister Hu?" Fan Wanqi frowned as she tried to remember. "I didn't see her."
	"I should warn her that Fei Ziyi is here," Tian Yong said worriedly.
	After I watched Tian Yong dart out of the restaurant, I grabbed Yuxin by the hand. "We've got to go!"
	"Wait!" Yuxin tugged her hand free of mine.
	"Wait for what? Yuxin, we don't have time!"
	Yuxin's eyes were panicked. "We're out of time."
	"Out of time? What do you mean?" I grabbed Yuxin's hand again and turned toward the door. But a split second later, there was a scream as all the windows were kicked in and black-clothed figures leaped into the room. More screams sounded as the pirates began slashing at the customers chaotically sprinting toward the doors.
	"Sister Xia! Look out!" I whirled around and realized to my horror that Fan Wanqi was standing between a pirate and me. The pirate was holding a wicked-looking dagger and seemed to have lunged at me with it. I was so paralyzed with shock that all I could do was look on in horror as Fan Wanqi struggled with the pirate over the blade. Fan Wanqi's hands were bleeding as she grasped at the blade with all her might. I sprung forward, but just before I could attack the pirate, Fan Wanqi lost her blood-slicked grip on the blade.
	I cried out as the dagger lodged itself in the girl's chest. Fan Wanqi staggered backward into me, and I dropped to my knees as Fan Wanqi slumped in my arms.
	"Murderer!" Yuxin shrieked. "Someone's been murdered! It's the pirates!"
	My head snapped up to look at Yuxin. "Yuxin, you-!" But whatever I was going to say next was cut off as all the customers in the restaurant began to panic even more. And in the confusion, Yuxin took off running.
	"Wanqi," I whispered. I frantically took Fan Wanqi's blood-soaked hands in my own. "Fan Wanqi!"
	"Sister Xia," Fan Wanqi choked out as she strained to look up at me. "He-he was going to stab you in the back. Hurry-run while you still can!"
	My vision swam as I tried and failed to blink back my tears. "You shouldn't have tried to protect me like that-"
	Fan Wanqi smiled up at me. "If I didn't protect you, who would? Besides"-she coughed as she choked on her blood-"I must have looked very heroic just now. Did I look very heroic?"
	"Wanqi," I sobbed. "You can't die!"
	Suddenly, another pirate lunged at me, but just as I looked up at him, he stopped and sprung at another fleeing customer instead. And then, just as quickly as they appeared, the pirates leaped back out the windows, and the restaurant went quiet.
	"She's working with the pirates!" someone yelled. I whirled around to find a man pointing at me. "I saw with my own eyes how the pirates didn't attack her!" The man pointed a shaky finger at the bodies strewn throughout the restaurant. "She's a murderer!"
	"No!" Fan Wanqi sputtered. "She's not!" But her words went unheard over the cries that had risen up in the restaurant. I let out a sob as Fan Wanqi coughed up a mouthful of blood.
	"Murderer!" the crowd chanted as they pointed at me.
	I rapidly shook my head. "No-I'm not!" As their voices became a deafening roar, I clapped my hands over my ears. My vision was blurred with tears, and the world swam around me. "It wasn't me!"
	There was a commotion at the door to the restaurant. I looked up as Weiwei, Mr. Fan, and Fei Ziyi appeared. All three of them rushed inside. When Weiwei noticed me on the ground, her face paled, and she dropped to her knees at my side.
	"I didn't murder anyone," I sobbed. "Wanqi-someone save Wanqi!"
	Weiwei blinked back tears as her eyes fell on Fan Wanqi's limp figure.
      Fei Ziyi stood with the crowd. The color drained from his face as well as he surveyed the scene.
	"That's my daughter!" Mr. Fan let out a cry as he hurried to cradle Fan Wanqi in his arms. Then he whirled to look at me. Rage and sadness flashed in his eyes.
	"Father," Fan Wanqi rasped as she struggled to speak. "Don't blame Sister Xia."
	"Little Qi!" Zhao Minmin's voice sounded. A moment later, she and Tian Yong appeared in my field of vision. Both of them were splattered with blood, and Zhao Minmin's sword slipped from her fingers as she dropped to her knees beside Fan Wanqi.
	Fan Wanqi's smile was strained. "Minmin. You're okay."
	Zhao Minmin stifled her tears as she took one of the girl's hands. "Yes, I'm okay. The pirates attacked me, but Tian Yong came to my aid. I'm okay, Little Qi. You'll be okay too."
	Fan Wanqi's breathing was labored. "In our next life, promise to take me on an adventure, will you?"
      Zhao Minmin squeezed her hand. "I promise."
      Fan Wanqi smiled up at her, but then she stilled.
	Zhao Minmin let out a sob as she clasped the girl's lifeless hand. Tian Yong knelt down next to Zhao Minmin to place a hand on her shoulder.
	"Murderer!" the customers continued to yell as they pointed at me.
	"She's not!" Weiwei raised her voice. She glared at the crowd before pulling me to my feet and leading me toward the back exit. I was in too much shock to protest. Fei Ziyi followed the two of us while Zhao Minmin and Tian Yong remained inside with Mr. Fan.
	"Where's Xia Yuxin?" Fei Ziyi finally asked. His expression was dark, and I could hardly recognize him. For the first time since I met him, Fei Ziyi was actually dressed as a martial artist.
	"She ran," I said blankly. Silent tears were still streaming down my face, but I didn't even notice them anymore.
	Fei Ziyi rounded on me. "Xia Xiyan, you let her get away again!"
	"My friend was dying!" I raised my voice as I resisted the urge to sob. "Of course I had to stay by her side during her final moments!"
      Fei Ziyi pointed an accusing finger at me as his eyes flashed. "This is your fault! If you didn't have me delayed, that girl wouldn't have died!"
	"I don't want Yuxin to die either!" I cried.
	"Listen to yourself!" Fei Ziyi said angrily. "How can you tell me to spare her life after everything she's done?"
	"Fei Ziyi," I tried, but my voice failed me as he drew his sword. "I-"
	"Fei Ziyi." Weiwei took a step in front of me to face him. "Wasn't the last time you attacked Xiyan enough? You can't pin all the blame on her."
	"Hu Qiuwei." Fei Ziyi seemed to be trying his best to remain calm. "Whose side are you on? Don't you want to see Xia Yuxin dead as well after all that she's done?"
	Weiwei just folded her arms over her chest. "If you'll excuse us, we need to go and track down Yuxin."
	Fei Ziyi smiled unpleasantly at the two of us. "That's if I don't get to her first. Goodbye."
	"Fei Ziyi!" I yelled at his retreating back. "Stop right there!" But Fei Ziyi just disappeared around the corner of the street.
	"Xiyan," Weiwei said softly as she placed a hand on my shoulder. "Let's go back to the inn. We've attracted quite a crowd."
	She was right; a crowd of townsfolk had gathered around us, whispering loudly among themselves. "But what about Wanqi?"
	Weiwei placed her veiled hat over my head before gently taking my hand. "Let's head back to the inn first."
	Dazed, I let Weiwei lead me down the street. The faces of the people we passed blurred by. Fan Wanqi's blood still coated my hands.
	"Weiwei." I finally found my voice once she gently shut the door to the inn room behind us. "Have I been doing everything wrong?" I hopelessly searched her face for answers.
      Despite the tears streaming down her own face, Weiwei smiled faintly as she shook her head. "You should know by now that I'll stay by your side no matter what. I should have been in the restaurant with you."
	I shook my head. "We should part ways, Weiwei. I can't drag you down with me like this. Wanqi took that knife for me this time. I don't want you being the one taking it next time. I'm not worth it." I slumped to the floor and buried my head in my arms. My heart hurt so much. A heaviness pressed down on me from all sides, and each breath I took strained my lungs.
	Weiwei took a seat next to me and wrapped her arms around me. I just sat there as silent tears continued to stream down my face.
	When Zhao Minmin and Tian Yong finally entered the inn room, the sky had faded into an inky night.
	"How's Mr. Fan?" Weiwei asked the question that was stuck on the tip of my tongue.
	"He's devastated," Tian Yong said heavily. His eyes were red and swollen. Zhao Minmin's were as well. "He refused to let go of his daughter's hand. He told her, 'Come, Qiqi. Wake up so I can take you on an adventure.' He was still holding onto her body when we left him." Tian Yong shook his head as he wiped his eyes with the back of his sleeve.
	I opened my mouth to say something, but all that came out was a strangled sound.
	"I know you want to keep Xia Yuxin alive," Zhao Minmin said softly as she knelt down in front of me. "But after all the lives she's taken . . ."
	I stared up at Zhao Minmin as she pulled my mask out from her belt. She placed it at my feet before standing back up.
	Trembling, I reached for the mask. No one stopped me when I fastened it over my hair.
	Weiwei broke the silence that had fallen. "If we hurry, we might be able to catch up with Yuxin. With that said, Fei Ziyi is much better at tracking people down than us. Sister Zhao, do you know if there's any female martial artists around here? If we go to them directly, maybe we can find Yuxin before Fei Ziyi does."
	I just sat there silently as Zhao Minmin drew us a map. I got the feeling that if Fei Ziyi hadn't left so quickly, she would have given him the map instead.
      "What about Mr. Fan and Wanqi?" I finally whispered.
	Zhao Minmin let out a sigh. "Mr. Fan wants to take his daughter's body back to his village to bury her there. Tian Yong and I are going to go with him to attend the funeral. Would the two of you like to come along?"
	Weiwei looked at me.
	I just shook my head. "I don't think I'm fit to attend the funeral. I'm the one who got Wanqi killed. I'll start trying to track down Yuxin. I won't let her run again. I'll use my life to stop her if that's what it takes."
	"Xiyan!" Weiwei said in alarm. "You can't throw your life away like that!"
	I let out a shaky breath as I looked up to address Zhao Minmin and Tian Yong. "Please send my condolences to Mr. Fan at Wanqi's funeral. I just hope that after I'm gone, the two of you will be willing to attend my funeral as well."

~

	It had been at least a month since we parted ways with Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin. While Weiwei and I initially managed to stay one step behind Yuxin and the pirates using Zhao Minmin's map, we never crossed paths with her. Instead, we encountered the deceased martial artists who had fallen under her blade. As we ventured further from the capital, Yuxin's trail disappeared entirely. Now unsure of what to do or where to look for clues, I was at my wits' end as the two of us tried to find our way out of a foggy bamboo forest.
      "Weiwei, you need to leave me. All you've done for me-I'm already in your debt for life." I marched through the bamboo. We had long lost the path, and the cold was beginning to set in. The fog was so thick that I couldn't even see the sky.
	"Xiyan," Weiwei said firmly as she hurried after me, "I've told you before that I'm going to stay by your side."
	"Weiwei." I stopped walking to look at her. "You told me that I shouldn't throw my life away, but you can't throw your life away either! I want you to live a long, happy life."
	Weiwei just let out a sigh. "I'm not going anywhere."
	"Why do you have to be so stubborn? Even if I can't lead a happy life, at least you still can. I want you to go while you still can. Forget about Yuxin. Forget about me. Start over."
	"Xiyan-" She started, but I just turned and continued walking. "Xiyan!" Weiwei called after me. "Stop!"
	I stopped walking and turned to look over my shoulder at her. Weiwei stood there in the fog, her eyes pained and her expression conflicted.
	"Xiyan," Weiwei finally whispered. "Does it have to be like this?"
	I just smiled sadly. "Goodbye, Weiwei." Then taking a deep breath, I turned away from Weiwei and continued down the path. After a few moments, I turned around to find that Weiwei had vanished into the mist.

~

	I sat in the corner of the shabby restaurant. Three liquor jars sat overturned on the table in front of me. I couldn't remember when I had finished them or if I had even opened them at all. In a daze, I reached for one of the bottles. But my fingers only closed around open air. My head spun as I grasped for the jars, and I struggled for a long time before I finally caught hold of one of them.
	I triumphantly lifted the jar to my lips, but it was empty. My momentary triumph faded back into a dazed stupor as I slowly returned the jar to the table. I needed to find Yuxin, but . . . who was Yuxin? I furrowed my brow as I tried to remember, but my futile attempts only resulted in a throbbing headache. I just felt tired. So tired.
	I still had some sense about me, though; I knew I couldn't fall asleep here. The way some of the customers were casting glances in my direction made my spine prickle. I shakily rose to my feet and started to make my way toward the door. The room swam before my eyes.
	Outside, I squinted as I tried to focus on the path. I wasn't sure how far I walked, but by the time I looked back, I was alone in the night. All the buildings had vanished into the dark. I continued until I was surrounded by trees. I was lost again, but this time my head hurt too much to care.
	There was something silver in the distance, and I slowly approached it. My vision wavered as I stared at the puddle of water. It was silver from the moonlight, and I stood there for a moment, watching how it glowed through the dark. I could see my own masked face reflected in the water, and ever so slowly, I reached up and removed my mask.
	I sank to my knees in front of the puddle. I just sat there, staring at my reflection for a long moment. I slapped myself across the face. I should have never come to the human realm.

~

      Today, the library was completely empty. I lay on the floor in human form, reading through a stack of books.
	Suddenly, I sat up. I could hear whispers coming from behind the towering bookcases, and I jumped to my feet as I shape-shifted into the hero. A spear materialized in my hands, and my fingers tightened around it as I wearily scanned the area.
	My fellow demons floated through the bookcases, surrounding me. "If it isn't you again," one of them said with a laugh. "What are you still doing here? You haven't been banished to the human realm yet?"
	I frowned. "Why do you follow me wherever I go?"
	"We're bored," another demon said. "And you're interesting."
	I just swung my spear at the demons, cutting through their smokey bodies as they flew around me.
	"Lady Hui is going to be angry if she sees you pretending to be a human here," a demon said as it floated past my head. I swung my spear at it, but it passed harmlessly through its body.
	Then the spear was being ripped out of my hands, and I didn't even have time to look around before something hard struck me on the back of the head. I toppled over as everything went black.
	When I came to, I was lying on a stone bench. I slowly sat up and winced as my head throbbed painfully.
	"You're awake." Lady Hui's cold voice reached my ears, and I turned toward the sound.
	"Lady Hui!" I quickly scrambled onto my human feet so I could bow to her.
	Lady Hui scoffed. "I'm here to give you a warning. If you don't do your job again, I can assure you that there will be consequences."
	"I missed work?"
	"Seems like you were too busy sleeping here to feed your ghosts," Lady Hui said in a displeased manner. "You only have one job, and you still managed to mess it up. Are you choosing to go against the wishes of the demon lord?"
	I rapidly shook my head.
	Lady Hui looked at me distastefully. "Stop wearing that human skin. You don't deserve it."
	I dejectedly reverted to my original form. "Lady Hui, all I want is to see the human realm with my own eyes. Even a single glance will be enough."
	"I advise you to stop longing for things that can never be yours," Lady Hui said as she turned away from me. "In the end, the only thing you'll find is disappointment and regret."
	I stared after Lady Hui as she glided away. For the past hundreds of years, I had studied the language, culture, and history of the human realm. I wanted to see the world I read about with my own eyes. Being banished to the human realm . . . would it really be that bad of a thing?

~

	I awoke to a flood of bright sunlight.
	"Xiyan!" Weiwei's voice called in relief. "You're awake!"
      I blinked as I slowly sat up. My face felt like it was on fire, and I hissed in pain. I was in a small wooden room that resembled the cheapest inn room I'd ever seen. My face. I clapped a hand to the side of my head as flashbacks from the previous night came back to me. Using the puddle as a mirror, I had taken a knife and carved a single character onto my face: Demon.
      "Weiwei?" I said. "Why are you here? I told you to leave me."
	Weiwei shook her head as she helped me up. "I never left. I continued following you. I followed you to the restaurant, but when you got up to leave, you were followed. I fought off your pursuers, but you had vanished. I was scared half to death. Then when I finally found you lying in the forest, your face was a bloody mess! I carried you all the way to the closest inn to clean and bandage your wounds. Xiyan, if I hadn't followed you . . . I don't even want to think about what could have happened."
	The severity of my situation sunk in, and Weiwei wrapped her arms around me as I burst into tears.
	When I finally calmed down, Weiwei gave me a bowl of soup. Even though every sip sent new waves of pain through my face, my head was clear again for the first time in weeks. "Weiwei, we need to go back and find Tian Yong." While there was no sign or word of Yuxin yet, Weiwei and I both knew where she would return to: the coast.
	"Tian Yong? What can Tian Yong do against the pirates?"
	"Tian Yong can help me speak to Master Zeng of the Owl and Aspen Sect. I want to ask Master Zeng for help."

~

	I wasn't sure how many days, weeks, or months had passed by the time we arrived at Tian Yong's house. The wounds on my face had scarred over, and I no longer removed my mask, even when I was alone. My face was so scarred that I couldn't bring myself to look at it. But I didn't regret it. Had it not been for me, Yuxin would not have become the person she is today. Maybe I was the one who cursed her. It was my arrival that turned her birth into an inauspicious event, and in turn, doomed all our fates.
      Now, standing in front of Tian Yong's house, I held my breath as I knocked on the door. To my relief, the door slid open, and Zhao Minmin appeared in the doorway. She smiled warmly as she motioned for us to step inside. "I knew you'd come looking for us here."
	I blinked. "You did?"
	"Xia Yuxin is still out there," she said knowingly. "And the two of you are no match for the pirates. You need the help of other martial artists."
	"Where's Tian Yong?" Weiwei asked as she scanned the house.
	Zhao Minmin poured each of us a cup of steaming tea before motioning for us to join her at the table. "He's been running back and forth from the Owl and Aspen Sect's headquarters," she told us. "He's been using the sect's resources to get information about Xia Yuxin. I would have gone with him if we didn't think it would be for the best for one of us to stay at the house in case you came looking. I was hoping you could come, Xiyan. We were all grieving that day, and I want to apologize to you. Little Qi was my good friend, but that was no excuse for me to have treated you the way I did either."
	I offered her a weak smile. "I don't blame you." Then Weiwei and I exchanged a glance. "Has anything happened with Yuxin recently?" I asked hesitantly.
	"The pirates have been sailing along the coast. Xia Yuxin has been spotted among them."
	"What else has Tian Yong found about Yuxin?" Weiwei said when I just stared at the steam wafting up from my cup.
	"Apparently, the pirate lord is dead," Zhao Minmin said quietly. "Xia Yuxin has been attracting quite a lot of attention since then. It seems like she's the one in charge now."
	Weiwei inhaled sharply. "She killed him?"
	"That I don't know for sure, but what I do know is that Xia Yuxin's name has become quite well known over the past few months. The name people have been giving her is quite intimidating. They call her the Demon that Arose from the Sea."
    

    Chapter Twenty-Five

	"She's not a demon," I started in shock. "I-" I was at a loss for words.
	"The two of you want to see Tian Yong, right?" Zhao Minmin mercifully changed the topic. "He should get back sometime tonight. How about I go prepare a bath for you? I can tell you've been on the road for many weeks. You can wear some of my clothes while we wash yours."
	"Thank you," Weiwei said gratefully.
	Zhao Minmin had us follow her to the back of the house. I took a bath first and changed into a plain outfit Zhao Minmin had set out for me. It was only after I finished washing my old clothes in the small yard outside that I realized I was clean for the first time in many weeks.
	As I waited for my clothes to dry, I sat next to the window and absently gazed out at the sky beyond. Weiwei had finished her bath too and was talking quietly with Zhao Minmin. As I sat there, a thought struck me. Could Minmin be the one who'd stop Yuxin? I wondered. A female hero would rise up to subdue the demon. A sound at the door drew me back to reality. It took me a moment to realize that the sky had gone dark and that it was now raining heavily.
	Zhao Minmin threw the door open to reveal Tian Yong, and a smile bloomed on her face.
	Tian Yong returned the smile as Zhao Minmin wrapped her arms around him.
	"We have guests," Zhao Minmin said as she finally drew away.
	Tian Yong looked over at Weiwei and me with a faint smile. "I'm glad to see that the two of you are alive and well."
	Weiwei inclined her head. "Likewise."
	"I was worried you might run into Fei Ziyi," Tian Yong said as he took a seat at the table. He set his sword down before pouring himself a cup of tea. Zhao Minmin sat next to him and got to work picking leaves out of his rain-soaked hair.
	"Tian Yong," I said seriously, "would it be possible to bring me into the Owl and Aspen Sect's headquarters? I still have a favor to redeem, and I want to beg Master Zeng for help. I want to stop Yuxin before she can cause any more harm. I want to stop her before she's remembered forever as a demon."
	
~

	That night, I sat next to the window. Tian Yong and Zhao Minmin had already retired to their room, and the candles were slowly flickering out. Tian Yong had agreed to take us into the Owl and Aspen Sect, but he couldn't say for sure whether Master Zeng would agree to help. "Master Zeng will help us, right?" I asked Weiwei.
	"I think Master Zeng will help you," Weiwei said quietly. "He wanted you to join his sect the last time you met, remember? Maybe he'll help you in exchange for you joining."
	I shook my head. "We already made ourselves clear that we won't join sects."
	"Xiyan," Weiwei said after a while. "It's late. You should go to bed."
	I turned back to the window. The night was quiet, apart from the sound of the rain pattering down. "You don't have to stay awake with me-I'll go to bed soon."
	"Xiyan," Weiwei tried again, softer this time.
